Reason's Obstacles and the Need for Revelation
Nasafi enumerates reason's difficulties and asserts the need for revelation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the fundamental limitations of unaided human reason and why divine revelation is a necessary assistant.

Core Idea
Reason cannot overcome its own obstacles without revelation.

Imam Nasafi opens by cataloging the many hindrances that afflict the rational seeker: doubts, passions, worries, and physical pains. He concludes that these obstacles make an external helper essential, and that helper is divine revelation.

Guided Path
1
Read the opening description
Read the Arabic passage and translation carefully. Notice the list of obstacles Nasafi enumerates: doubts, desires, worries, and pains.
These are not abstract; they reflect real human experience in seeking truth.
2
Identify the conclusion
After listing obstacles, Nasafi states 'flabbud' (there must be). Locate the logical connector and the conclusion that revelation is that assistant.
The phrase 'وذلك هو الوحي السماوي' is the key.
3
Reflect on the necessity
Ask yourself: why does Nasafi think reason alone is insufficient? The answer lies in the obstacles he lists.
The passage argues from human limitation, not from scriptural authority.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
صاحبه، وربما تعارضه الشبهات، وتصده عن حقيقة النظر الأماني والشهوات، وتمنعه عن الإحاطة بكل دقيق من الأمور وجليل، اعتراء الهموم وأسباب شغل القلب على صاحبه، وترادف الآلام والأوجاع عليه، وتشغله عن الاستقصاء في البحث والتأمل مع ما في المطالب النظرية من الغموض والدقة فلابد من معاون له إياه ليصل باتصاله به إلى ما يجب الوصول إليه. وذلك هو الوحي السماوي، والله الموفق. على أن العقول لو كان في جبلتها إمكان الوصول إلى جميع مصالح الدارين إلا أن ذلك لن يكون إلا بآداب الفكر، ونصّ مطية الخاطر، والانكباب على النظر الدائم والبحث الكامل، ويلحقه بذلك مشقة عظيمة، وتلزمه مؤنة كثيرة. ثم إنه إذا نبه على ذلك بالسمع وأرشد إلى كيفية استخراج ما يرومه بعقله تنبه لذلك، وسهل عليه الأمر وخفت له المؤنة. ولهذا كان الغالب في اتباع الأنبياء عليهم السلام الاستمرار على الحق والتشبث به، وإن كان أكثرهم خالين عن صناعة النظر موصوفين بالبلادة، مشغولين باكتساب أسباب المعاش والغالب على الفلاسفة العدول عن الصواب والوقوع في الكفر والضلال، وإن كانوا موسومين برجاحة العقول وقوة الألباب وصفاء القرائح، متفرغين سنين كثيرة وأعمارًا طويلة للبحث عن المعالم الإلهية والمعاني الدينية، معتزلين الخلق في مدارسهم، لتأيد الصنف الأول بمادة الوحي السماوي وخلاء الصنف الثاني عن ذلك، بل لا نكاد نجد أحدًا من الأوائل المنتسبين إلى الفلسفة متمسكاً بالتوحيد مقراً بوظائف الأمر والنهي معترفا بالحشر والمعاد على ما هو الحق إلا إذا كان من أتباع الأنبياء عليهم السلام أخذ الدين منهم أو من أتباعهم، وإذا كان الأمر كذلك فمن لم يتلق هذه النعمة العظيمة بالشكر، واعتقد أن الإرشاد إلى ذلك تسهيل الأمر عليه وتخفيف المؤنة خارج عن الحكمة، فهو الأحمق الذي لا دواء لحمقه ولا حيلة لبرئه عما ابتلى به من داء جهله والله الهادي. على أنه لو كان في العقل الغناء كما يزعمون وليس في إرسال المرسل زيادة تخفيف وتيسير أو معنى من المعاني بل فيه عين ما في العقل، لما أوجب ذلك كون الإرسال سفها، بل هو من باب الإفضال والإحسان، إذ إعطاء ما زاد على الكفاية يعد إفضالاً وزيادة في الإنعام، ووجود ذلك في العالم مما لا يخفى، كإعطاء الله تعالى ما فيه زيادة لذة من الأغذية وإن كان بدون ذلك من الأغذية حصول ما هو المقصود من بقاء الأبدان. ولهذا قسمت الحكماء ما ساق الله تعالى إلى عباده من أنواع نعمه قسمين: أحدهما من لواحق المرفق وهو ما يحصل به المقصود من غير أن يكون فيه زيادة لذة كالشعير والذرة، وغير ذلك من الحبوب التي يحصل بتناولها بقاء الأبدان وكالصوف والشعر اللذين يحصل بهما ما هو المقصود من اللباس من ستر العورة، ودفع أذى الحر والبرد. والآخر من لواحق الزينة وهو ما فيه زيادة لذة وراحة وراء ما يتعلق به من مصلحة البدن وقيام النهمة كالأطعمة المشهية والثياب الفاخرة.
Its [reason's] owner, and perhaps doubts conflict with it, and vain desires and passions prevent it from true consideration, and prevent it from encompassing every precise and grand matter, the occurrence of worries and causes of heart-occupation upon its owner, and the succession of pains and ailments upon him, and they occupy him from thoroughness in investigation and reflection along with what is in theoretical matters of obscurity and subtlety. So there must be an assistant for him to reach, by connection with it, what must be reached. And that is divine revelation, and God is the Grantor of success. Although if minds had in their disposition the possibility of reaching all the interests of the two abodes, yet that would not be except with disciplines of thought, the saddling of the mount of the mind, and devoting oneself to constant consideration and complete investigation, and there attaches to that great hardship, and much burden becomes incumbent upon him. Then, if he is alerted to that by the [revealed] hearing and guided to the manner of extracting what he seeks by his reason, he becomes alert to it, and the matter becomes easy for him, and the burden lightens. For this reason, the prevalent [characteristic] among the followers of the prophets, peace be upon them, is persistence upon truth and clinging to it, even though most of them are devoid of the art of theoretical investigation, described as dullness, occupied with earning the means of livelihood. And the prevalent [characteristic] among the philosophers is deviating from correctness and falling into disbelief and misguidance, even though they are marked by soundness of intellects, strength of minds, and purity of natural dispositions, having devoted many years and long lifetimes to research into divine landmarks and religious meanings, isolating themselves from creation in their schools. This is because the first group is supported by the substance of divine revelation and the second group is devoid of that. Rather, we hardly find any of the early [thinkers] attributed to philosophy who clings to monotheism, acknowledges the duties of command and prohibition, and recognizes the resurrection and the final return as is the truth, except if he was among the followers of the prophets, peace be upon them, taking religion from them or from their followers. And if the matter is thus, then whoever does not receive this great blessing with gratitude, and believes that guidance to that, making the matter easy for him and lightening the burden, is outside of wisdom, he is the imbecile for whose imbecility there is no cure and no stratagem for his recovery from the disease of ignorance with which he is afflicted. And God is the Guide. Moreover, if reason were sufficient as they claim, and there is in sending messengers no increase of lightening and facilitation or any meaning, but rather in it is the very same as what is in reason, that would not make sending [messengers] foolishness; rather it is from the category of bestowal of favor and beneficence, since giving what exceeds sufficiency is considered favor and increase in grace. And the existence of that in the world is not hidden, like God, exalted, giving foods in which there is an increase of pleasure, even if without those foods the intended [purpose] of preservation of bodies is attained. For this reason, the wise divided what God, exalted, has conveyed to His servants of the kinds of His blessings into two divisions: one is from the accessories of necessity – and it is that by which the intended [purpose] is attained without there being in it an increase of pleasure, like barley and corn, and other grains by whose consumption the preservation of bodies is attained, and like wool and hair by which the intended [purpose] of clothing – covering of the private parts and repelling the harm of heat and cold – is attained. And the other is from the accessories of adornment – and it is that in which there is an increase of pleasure and comfort beyond what is connected to it of bodily benefit and satisfaction of appetite, like appetizing foods and fine garments.
Source pages p. 688

Commentary
This passage is a sustained argument for the necessity of divine revelation as an aid to human reason. The author, Imam Nasafi, begins by describing the difficulties that beset a rational seeker of truth: doubts, passions, worries, and physical pains hinder thorough investigation. Therefore, an assistant is needed, and that is divine revelation. Even if the intellect could in principle reach all beneficial truths, it would require immense discipline, hardship, and time. Revelation alerts the seeker, guides him on how to extract what he seeks with his intellect, thus making the task easy and lightening the burden. This explains why the followers of prophets generally persist in truth despite lacking sophisticated reasoning skills, whereas philosophers—despite their intellectual gifts—often fall into error and disbelief. The reason is the support of revelation for the former and its absence for the latter. Rarely is a philosopher found who adheres to monotheism and recognizes divine commands and the afterlife unless he has learned from prophets or their followers. Therefore, those who do not receive this great blessing with gratitude and consider it unwise are incurable fools. Finally, Nasafi refutes the objection that if reason were sufficient, sending messengers would be superfluous. He argues that even if revelation added nothing new to reason, it would still be an act of divine favor (ifdal) and beneficence (ihsan), since giving beyond sufficiency is always generosity. He illustrates this with food: God gives pleasurable foods even though plain food suffices for bodily survival. He then cites the division of God's blessings into two categories by the wise: (1) accessories of necessity (lawahiq al-mirfaq) – things that fulfill the essential purpose without extra pleasure, like barley, corn, wool, and hair; (2) accessories of adornment (lawahiq al-zina) – things that bring extra pleasure and comfort beyond bare necessity, like appetizing foods and fine garments. Thus, revelation is a gift of adornment that facilitates and eases the human quest for truth.

Key Terms
الشبهات
الأماني
الشهوات
النظر
الوحي السماوي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some believe that human reason alone, without any external aid, can achieve certainty in all matters.
Correction: Nasafi demonstrates that reason is beset by doubts, passions, and distractions that prevent it from reaching truth. Therefore, an assistant—divine revelation—is necessary.

Checkpoint
According to Nasafi, what necessitates an assistant for reason?
A) The inherent weakness of the human intellect
B) The multitude of obstacles that hinder reason
C) The inability to obtain food and shelter
D) The lack of philosophical training

Key Takeaway
Human reason, despite its capacity, requires divine revelation to overcome its own limitations and reach truth.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Think of a time when you were absolutely certain of something based on your own reasoning, only to later realize you were wrong. Which of Nasafi's obstacles (doubts, desires, worries, etc.) was secretly steering your mind? Will you now humbly admit that your reason, without revelation, is not enough to secure truth?
?
Your phone, your career, your reputation—these occupy your mind daily. When did you last allow divine revelation to truly interrupt your busy thoughts? If revelation is the necessary assistant for your reason, why do you still trust your own thoughts more than the Qur'an when making life's big decisions?
?
Nasafi says reason cannot encompass 'every precise and grand matter.' What is one 'grand matter' (like the nature of God, the unseen, or the purpose of life) that you have tried to figure out using only logic? What would it cost you to finally accept that you need divine revelation as your guide for that matter?

Revelation Eases the Path of Reason
Nasafi describes the hardship of unaided reason and the easing effect of revelation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how divine revelation lightens the burden of rational inquiry and makes the search for truth accessible.

Core Idea
Revelation turns a grueling intellectual journey into a guided, manageable path.

Even if reason could theoretically reach all truths, Nasafi explains that it would require immense discipline and hardship. Revelation acts as a guide, alerting the seeker and showing how to extract what he seeks, thereby making the task easy.

Guided Path
1
Read the conditional statement
Notice Nasafi says 'even if minds had the possibility... yet that would not be except with disciplines of thought and constant investigation.' This acknowledges reason's potential but highlights the cost.
The phrase 'على أن العقول لو كان في جبلتها إمكان' sets up a concession.
2
Understand the burden
He describes the 'great hardship' and 'much burden' that would be required. Identify these descriptions in the text.
The burden includes mental discipline and total devotion.
3
See how revelation alleviates
The passage then states: when revelation alerts and guides, the matter becomes easy and the burden lightens. Compare the two conditions.
Revelation acts as a shortcut and instructor.

Source Text

Commentary
This passage is a sustained argument for the necessity of divine revelation as an aid to human reason. The author, Imam Nasafi, begins by describing the difficulties that beset a rational seeker of truth: doubts, passions, worries, and physical pains hinder thorough investigation. Therefore, an assistant is needed, and that is divine revelation. Even if the intellect could in principle reach all beneficial truths, it would require immense discipline, hardship, and time. Revelation alerts the seeker, guides him on how to extract what he seeks with his intellect, thus making the task easy and lightening the burden. This explains why the followers of prophets generally persist in truth despite lacking sophisticated reasoning skills, whereas philosophers—despite their intellectual gifts—often fall into error and disbelief. The reason is the support of revelation for the former and its absence for the latter. Rarely is a philosopher found who adheres to monotheism and recognizes divine commands and the afterlife unless he has learned from prophets or their followers. Therefore, those who do not receive this great blessing with gratitude and consider it unwise are incurable fools. Finally, Nasafi refutes the objection that if reason were sufficient, sending messengers would be superfluous. He argues that even if revelation added nothing new to reason, it would still be an act of divine favor (ifdal) and beneficence (ihsan), since giving beyond sufficiency is always generosity. He illustrates this with food: God gives pleasurable foods even though plain food suffices for bodily survival. He then cites the division of God's blessings into two categories by the wise: (1) accessories of necessity (lawahiq al-mirfaq) – things that fulfill the essential purpose without extra pleasure, like barley, corn, wool, and hair; (2) accessories of adornment (lawahiq al-zina) – things that bring extra pleasure and comfort beyond bare necessity, like appetizing foods and fine garments. Thus, revelation is a gift of adornment that facilitates and eases the human quest for truth.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think revelation makes reason unnecessary or bypasses it entirely.
Correction: Nasafi shows revelation assists reason by guiding it, not replacing it; the seeker still uses his own reason ('bi-'aql') to extract what he seeks.

Checkpoint
What does revelation provide according to this passage?
A) A complete system of knowledge that requires no thought
B) An alert and guidance on how to use reason to extract truth
C) A replacement for all rational investigation
D) A command to abandon reason

Key Takeaway
Revelation does not negate reason but makes its pursuit of truth much easier by providing guidance and method.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you tend to trust your own reasoning more than revelation when making important life decisions? When has your intellect struggled and what would change if you let revelation lead?
?
Think of a truth you once found difficult to accept. Did you arrive at it through exhausting reasoning or did revelation make it clear and easy? How can you intentionally seek that ease more often?
?
In what area of your life are you still 'saddling the mount of the mind' alone, without consulting scripture? What is one specific truth you will let revelation guide you on today, starting now?

Prophethood

Proof from History: Prophets' Followers vs. Philosophers
Nasafi contrasts prophet followers and philosophers to show revelation's indispensability.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will see the empirical evidence for the effectiveness of revelation: followers of prophets, despite lacking skill, adhere to truth, while philosophers, despite brilliance, often deviate.

Core Idea
Historical observation proves revelation's superiority over unaided reason.

Nasafi now turns to a historical comparison. The followers of prophets, even those of simple intellect and occupied with livelihood, consistently hold to truth. Philosophers, with all their intellectual power and dedication, frequently fall into error and disbelief. The difference is the support of revelation.

Guided Path
1
Read the comparison
Carefully read the description of each group: the prophet's followers are 'devoid of the art of theoretical investigation, described as dullness' but 'persistent upon truth'; philosophers are 'marked by soundness of intellects' but 'deviating into disbelief.'
Note the contrast in outcome despite opposite starting points.
2
Identify the cause
Nasafi explicitly states the cause: the first group is supported by revelation, the second lacks it. Find that sentence.
The cause is 'maddat al-wahy al-samawi' (substance of divine revelation).
3
Draw the conclusion
Reflect on the implications: even the best unaided reason is unreliable; revelation provides a firm anchor.
Nasafi then declares that anyone ungrateful for this blessing is an incurable fool.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
صاحبه، وربما تعارضه الشبهات، وتصده عن حقيقة النظر الأماني والشهوات، وتمنعه عن الإحاطة بكل دقيق من الأمور وجليل، اعتراء الهموم وأسباب شغل القلب على صاحبه، وترادف الآلام والأوجاع عليه، وتشغله عن الاستقصاء في البحث والتأمل مع ما في المطالب النظرية من الغموض والدقة فلابد من معاون له إياه ليصل باتصاله به إلى ما يجب الوصول إليه. وذلك هو الوحي السماوي، والله الموفق. على أن العقول لو كان في جبلتها إمكان الوصول إلى جميع مصالح الدارين إلا أن ذلك لن يكون إلا بآداب الفكر، ونصّ مطية الخاطر، والانكباب على النظر الدائم والبحث الكامل، ويلحقه بذلك مشقة عظيمة، وتلزمه مؤنة كثيرة. ثم إنه إذا نبه على ذلك بالسمع وأرشد إلى كيفية استخراج ما يرومه بعقله تنبه لذلك، وسهل عليه الأمر وخفت له المؤنة. ولهذا كان الغالب في اتباع الأنبياء عليهم السلام الاستمرار على الحق والتشبث به، وإن كان أكثرهم خالين عن صناعة النظر موصوفين بالبلادة، مشغولين باكتساب أسباب المعاش والغالب على الفلاسفة العدول عن الصواب والوقوع في الكفر والضلال، وإن كانوا موسومين برجاحة العقول وقوة الألباب وصفاء القرائح، متفرغين سنين كثيرة وأعمارًا طويلة للبحث عن المعالم الإلهية والمعاني الدينية، معتزلين الخلق في مدارسهم، لتأيد الصنف الأول بمادة الوحي السماوي وخلاء الصنف الثاني عن ذلك، بل لا نكاد نجد أحدًا من الأوائل المنتسبين إلى الفلسفة متمسكاً بالتوحيد مقراً بوظائف الأمر والنهي معترفا بالحشر والمعاد على ما هو الحق إلا إذا كان من أتباع الأنبياء عليهم السلام أخذ الدين منهم أو من أتباعهم، وإذا كان الأمر كذلك فمن لم يتلق هذه النعمة العظيمة بالشكر، واعتقد أن الإرشاد إلى ذلك تسهيل الأمر عليه وتخفيف المؤنة خارج عن الحكمة، فهو الأحمق الذي لا دواء لحمقه ولا حيلة لبرئه عما ابتلى به من داء جهله والله الهادي. على أنه لو كان في العقل الغناء كما يزعمون وليس في إرسال المرسل زيادة تخفيف وتيسير أو معنى من المعاني بل فيه عين ما في العقل، لما أوجب ذلك كون الإرسال سفها، بل هو من باب الإفضال والإحسان، إذ إعطاء ما زاد على الكفاية يعد إفضالاً وزيادة في الإنعام، ووجود ذلك في العالم مما لا يخفى، كإعطاء الله تعالى ما فيه زيادة لذة من الأغذية وإن كان بدون ذلك من الأغذية حصول ما هو المقصود من بقاء الأبدان. ولهذا قسمت الحكماء ما ساق الله تعالى إلى عباده من أنواع نعمه قسمين: أحدهما من لواحق المرفق وهو ما يحصل به المقصود من غير أن يكون فيه زيادة لذة كالشعير والذرة، وغير ذلك من الحبوب التي يحصل بتناولها بقاء الأبدان وكالصوف والشعر اللذين يحصل بهما ما هو المقصود من اللباس من ستر العورة، ودفع أذى الحر والبرد. والآخر من لواحق الزينة وهو ما فيه زيادة لذة وراحة وراء ما يتعلق به من مصلحة البدن وقيام النهمة كالأطعمة المشهية والثياب الفاخرة.
Its [reason's] owner, and perhaps doubts conflict with it, and vain desires and passions prevent it from true consideration, and prevent it from encompassing every precise and grand matter, the occurrence of worries and causes of heart-occupation upon its owner, and the succession of pains and ailments upon him, and they occupy him from thoroughness in investigation and reflection along with what is in theoretical matters of obscurity and subtlety. So there must be an assistant for him to reach, by connection with it, what must be reached. And that is divine revelation, and God is the Grantor of success. Although if minds had in their disposition the possibility of reaching all the interests of the two abodes, yet that would not be except with disciplines of thought, the saddling of the mount of the mind, and devoting oneself to constant consideration and complete investigation, and there attaches to that great hardship, and much burden becomes incumbent upon him. Then, if he is alerted to that by the [revealed] hearing and guided to the manner of extracting what he seeks by his reason, he becomes alert to it, and the matter becomes easy for him, and the burden lightens. For this reason, the prevalent [characteristic] among the followers of the prophets, peace be upon them, is persistence upon truth and clinging to it, even though most of them are devoid of the art of theoretical investigation, described as dullness, occupied with earning the means of livelihood. And the prevalent [characteristic] among the philosophers is deviating from correctness and falling into disbelief and misguidance, even though they are marked by soundness of intellects, strength of minds, and purity of natural dispositions, having devoted many years and long lifetimes to research into divine landmarks and religious meanings, isolating themselves from creation in their schools. This is because the first group is supported by the substance of divine revelation and the second group is devoid of that. Rather, we hardly find any of the early [thinkers] attributed to philosophy who clings to monotheism, acknowledges the duties of command and prohibition, and recognizes the resurrection and the final return as is the truth, except if he was among the followers of the prophets, peace be upon them, taking religion from them or from their followers. And if the matter is thus, then whoever does not receive this great blessing with gratitude, and believes that guidance to that, making the matter easy for him and lightening the burden, is outside of wisdom, he is the imbecile for whose imbecility there is no cure and no stratagem for his recovery from the disease of ignorance with which he is afflicted. And God is the Guide. Moreover, if reason were sufficient as they claim, and there is in sending messengers no increase of lightening and facilitation or any meaning, but rather in it is the very same as what is in reason, that would not make sending [messengers] foolishness; rather it is from the category of bestowal of favor and beneficence, since giving what exceeds sufficiency is considered favor and increase in grace. And the existence of that in the world is not hidden, like God, exalted, giving foods in which there is an increase of pleasure, even if without those foods the intended [purpose] of preservation of bodies is attained. For this reason, the wise divided what God, exalted, has conveyed to His servants of the kinds of His blessings into two divisions: one is from the accessories of necessity – and it is that by which the intended [purpose] is attained without there being in it an increase of pleasure, like barley and corn, and other grains by whose consumption the preservation of bodies is attained, and like wool and hair by which the intended [purpose] of clothing – covering of the private parts and repelling the harm of heat and cold – is attained. And the other is from the accessories of adornment – and it is that in which there is an increase of pleasure and comfort beyond what is connected to it of bodily benefit and satisfaction of appetite, like appetizing foods and fine garments.
Source pages p. 688

Commentary
This passage is a sustained argument for the necessity of divine revelation as an aid to human reason. The author, Imam Nasafi, begins by describing the difficulties that beset a rational seeker of truth: doubts, passions, worries, and physical pains hinder thorough investigation. Therefore, an assistant is needed, and that is divine revelation. Even if the intellect could in principle reach all beneficial truths, it would require immense discipline, hardship, and time. Revelation alerts the seeker, guides him on how to extract what he seeks with his intellect, thus making the task easy and lightening the burden. This explains why the followers of prophets generally persist in truth despite lacking sophisticated reasoning skills, whereas philosophers—despite their intellectual gifts—often fall into error and disbelief. The reason is the support of revelation for the former and its absence for the latter. Rarely is a philosopher found who adheres to monotheism and recognizes divine commands and the afterlife unless he has learned from prophets or their followers. Therefore, those who do not receive this great blessing with gratitude and consider it unwise are incurable fools. Finally, Nasafi refutes the objection that if reason were sufficient, sending messengers would be superfluous. He argues that even if revelation added nothing new to reason, it would still be an act of divine favor (ifdal) and beneficence (ihsan), since giving beyond sufficiency is always generosity. He illustrates this with food: God gives pleasurable foods even though plain food suffices for bodily survival. He then cites the division of God's blessings into two categories by the wise: (1) accessories of necessity (lawahiq al-mirfaq) – things that fulfill the essential purpose without extra pleasure, like barley, corn, wool, and hair; (2) accessories of adornment (lawahiq al-zina) – things that bring extra pleasure and comfort beyond bare necessity, like appetizing foods and fine garments. Thus, revelation is a gift of adornment that facilitates and eases the human quest for truth.

Key Terms
اتباع الأنبياء
الفلاسفة
مادة الوحي السماوي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that intellectual sophistication and dedicated study automatically lead to religious truth.
Correction: Nasafi shows that philosophers, despite their advantages, often err; true guidance comes from revelation.

Checkpoint
According to Nasafi, what is the most likely reason philosophers deviate from truth?
A) They are too occupied with worldly matters.
B) They lack natural intelligence.
C) They are devoid of the support of divine revelation.
D) They do not study enough.

Key Takeaway
History shows that revelation, not intellectual power, is the decisive factor in attaining truth.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You have both intellect and access to revelation. What if you were born into a society without prophets? Based on Nasafi's observation, what would be the likely state of your beliefs? How does that make you feel about the blessing of revelation?
?
The followers of the prophets are described as 'dull' and occupied with livelihood, yet they cling to truth. Are you more like them or the philosophers in your intellectual pride? Where do you rely on your own reasoning over revelation? What would it take for you to humbly accept the 'substance of divine revelation' as your support?
?
Nasafi says that those who reject this blessing are incurable fools. Do you treat revelation as a burden or a gift? Examine your attitude towards religious obligations: do you see them as a burden that lightens the load, or as an unnecessary restriction? What change is needed in your heart?

Prophethood
advanced
8 min
Revelation as Divine Favor: Beyond Sufficiency
Nasafi refutes the objection that revelation is unnecessary by categorizing it as a divine favor beyond necessity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that even if reason were sufficient, revelation is still a generous gift from God that adds ease and comfort, akin to the division of blessings into necessities and adornments.

Core Idea
Revelation is an act of divine generosity, not redundancy.

Nasafi anticipates an objection: if reason is enough, why send messengers? He refutes by arguing that even if revelation added nothing new, it would still be a favor (ifdal) and beneficence (ihsan), as God gives beyond sufficiency. He illustrates with the division of God's blessings into necessities and adornments.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection and refutation
Nasafi first states the hypothetical objection: even if revelation had only what reason has, sending messengers would not be foolish but an act of favor.
The phrase 'لما أوجب ذلك كون الإرسال سفها' is key.
2
Understand the concept of 'ifdal'
Nasafi explains that giving beyond sufficiency is considered favor. Revelation is an extra gift that makes things easier.
This is a core theological concept: God's generosity exceeds what is necessary.
3
Learn the two categories of blessings
He divides blessings into: 1) accessories of necessity (lawahiq al-mirfaq) – meeting essential needs without extra pleasure, and 2) accessories of adornment (lawahiq al-zina) – providing extra pleasure and comfort.
Revelation falls into the second category: it adds ease and delight.
4
Apply the analogy
Just as God gives delicious foods and fine clothes beyond bare necessity, revelation is a gift of adornment to the intellect.
This makes revelation an expression of divine love, not a redundant command.

According to the passage, which category does divine revelation belong to?

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you treat the Quran and Sunnah as a basic necessity (like barley) that you consume just enough to 'get by' spiritually, or as a delightful feast that you savor? What would change if you approached each verse as a delicious gift from Allah rather than merely a duty? Commit to reading one verse today with the intention of tasting its sweetness.
?
The passage says giving beyond sufficiency is a favor. Have you ever thanked Allah for the extra ease and beauty revelation brings to your life—beyond just guidance? Make a list this week of three aspects of revelation that feel like 'adornment' to you, then thank Allah for each one.
?
If reason alone were sufficient to know right from wrong, would you still eagerly seek the Quran and hadith? Or do you sometimes rely more on your own intellect than on divine revelation? Challenge yourself to memorize one new verse this week not for a test or duty, but as a personal gift from your Lord.

Empirical Evidence That Reason Alone Does Not Lead to True Monotheism
Al-Nasafi argues from historical observation that philosophers failed to attain true monotheism without prophets.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how historical observation of philosophers demonstrates the necessity of prophethood for true monotheism.

Core Idea
Philosophers without prophets never achieved true monotheism.

This passage from Imam al-Nasafi presents a compelling empirical argument: look at the history of philosophy. Hardly any philosopher adhered to correct beliefs about God, divine commands, and the afterlife unless they followed a prophet. This shows that reason alone is not enough—prophets are a divine necessity.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
The passage uses a historical observation as evidence.
2
Identify the author's claim about philosophers
The author states that among early philosophers, hardly anyone adhered to monotheism, duties of command/prohibition, and belief in resurrection unless they were followers of prophets. Find the exact wording.
Look for the phrase 'لا نكاد نجد أحدًا'.
3
Reflect on the consequence
Ask yourself: If reason alone cannot produce correct belief, what does that mean for the necessity of prophethood? How does this fit into the broader Islamic doctrine of prophethood?
The author concludes that rejecting prophets as a blessing is foolishness.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
السماوي وخلاء الصنف الثاني عن ذلك، بل لا نكاد نجد أحدًا من الأوائل المنتسبين إلى الفلسفة متمسكاً بالتوحيد مقراً بوظائف الأمر والنهي معترفا بالحشر والمعاد على ما هو الحق إلا إذا كان من أتباع الأنبياء عليهم السلام أخذ الدين منهم أو من أتباعهم، وإذا كان الأمر كذلك فمن لم يتلق هذه النعمة العظيمة بالشكر، واعتقد أن الإرشاد إلى ذلك تسهيل الأمر عليه وتخفيف المؤنة خارج عن الحكمة، فهو الأحمق الذي لا دواء لحمقه ولا حيلة لبرئه عما ابتلى به من داء جهله والله الهادي.
The sky and emptying the second kind of that; rather, we hardly find anyone among the early philosophers adhering to monotheism, acknowledging the duties of command and prohibition, recognizing the resurrection and the final return as is the truth, except if he was a follower of the prophets (peace be upon them) taking religion from them or from their followers. And if the matter is such, then whoever does not receive this great blessing with gratitude, and believes that guidance to that is an easing of the matter upon him and a lightening of the burden outside of wisdom, he is the fool for whose foolishness there is no cure and no remedy for his recovery from the disease of ignorance with which he is afflicted. And Allah is the Guide.
Source pages p. 689

Commentary
This passage presents an empirical argument for the necessity of prophethood. The author observes that among the early philosophers, who relied solely on reason, it is nearly impossible to find anyone who adhered to true monotheism (tawhid), acknowledged religious duties (sharia), and believed in resurrection (hashr) and the final return (ma'ad) as is the truth, unless that person was a follower of the prophets. This shows that reason alone is insufficient to arrive at correct belief and practice. Therefore, sending prophets is a great blessing; to consider it unnecessary or an inconvenience is foolishness (hamaq) with no cure. The passage ends by asserting that Allah is the Guide.

Key Terms
التوحيد
الحشر
المعاد
الأنبياء
الفلسفة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Reason and philosophy alone can lead to correct belief in God and the afterlife.
Correction: The author provides historical evidence that philosophers who did not follow prophets failed to achieve true monotheism, resurrection, and divine commands. Therefore, reason alone is insufficient without revelation.

Checkpoint
Why does the author argue that philosophy alone is insufficient for true belief?
A) Because philosophers are inherently biased.
B) Because historical observation shows philosophers did not achieve true monotheism unless they followed prophets.
C) Because reason is evil.
D) Because prophets are needed only for laws.

Key Takeaway
History shows that true monotheism and belief in resurrection require prophetic guidance; reason alone is not enough.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Where in your own life have you relied solely on your intellect, dismissing the guidance of revelation? What was the result, and what does this lesson call you to change today?
?
Al-Nasafi calls ingratitude for the blessing of prophethood an incurable foolishness. Have you truly received this blessing with gratitude, or do you sometimes take the Quran and Sunnah for granted? What would genuine gratitude look like in your daily actions?
?
The early philosophers, despite their brilliance, could not attain true monotheism without prophets. Are there areas of your belief or practice where you are subtly trusting your own reasoning over clear prophetic guidance? What step will you take today to submit more fully?

Prophethood as Grace Beyond Reason
The author argues that sending prophets is an act of grace even if reason sufficed.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why sending prophets is considered an act of grace (tafdil) and not foolishness, even on the hypothetical assumption that reason alone sufficed for guidance.

Core Idea
Providing more than the minimum is grace, not folly.

This lesson addresses a common objection: if reason is sufficient for knowing God and moral guidance, why send prophets? The author of the Tabsirah engages this challenge by conceding the hypothetical for the sake of argument, then demonstrating that even then, sending prophets would be an act of divine grace and beneficence. He supports this with vivid analogies from everyday blessings, showing that God always gives more than the bare minimum.

Guided Path
1
Understand the hypothetical concession
Notice that the author begins by granting the opponent's claim for argument's sake: even if reason sufficed, sending prophets would not be foolish.
This is a common dialectical strategy in kalam: conceding a point to show it doesn't lead to the conclusion.
2
Grasp the principle of grace vs. necessity
The author states that giving more than sufficient (kifaya) is considered grace (tafdil) and beneficence (ihsan), not foolishness (safah).
This principle is key: it reframes the objection from redundancy to generosity.
3
Examine the division of blessings
Read the passage's classification of divine blessings into necessities (lawahiq al-marfiq) and adornments (lawahiq al-zina). Understand examples for each.
Necessities meet basic needs; adornments add pleasure. Both are gifts from God.
4
Apply the analogies to prophethood
The author uses analogies of body parts (two eyes, ears) and multiple rational proofs to show that God gives more than needed. Similarly, sending prophets is extra guidance.
These analogies reinforce that excess is completeness, not foolishness.
5
Note the author's overall strategy
Understand that this argument is presented as a lenient (musahala) approach; the real proofs against sufficiency of reason were given earlier.
This helps situate the passage within the larger work.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
على أنه لو كان في العقل الغناء كما يزعمون وليس في إرسال المرسل زيادة تخفيف وتيسير أو معنى من المعاني بل فيه عين ما في العقل، لما أوجب ذلك كون الإرسال سفها، بل هو من باب الإفضال والإحسان، إذ إعطاء ما زاد على الكفاية يعد إفضالاً وزيادة في الإنعام ، ووجود ذلك في العالم مما لا يخفى، كإعطاء الله تعالى ما فيه زيادة لذة من الأغذية وإن كان بدون ذلك من الأغذية حصول ما هو المقصود من بقاء الأبدان. ولهذا قسمت الحكماء ما ساق الله تعالى إلى عباده من أنواع نعمه قسمين: أحدهما من لواحق المرفق وهو ما يحصل به المقصود من غير أن يكون فيه زيادة لذة كالشعير والذرة، وغير ذلك من الحبوب التي يحصل بتناولها بقاء الأبدان وكالصوف والشعر اللذين يحصل بهما ما هو المقصود من اللباس من ستر العورة، ودفع أذى الحر والبرد. والآخر من لواحق الزينة وهو ما فيه زيادة لذة وراحة وراء ما يتعلق به من مصلحة البدن وقيام النهمة كالأطعمة المشهية والثياب الفاخرة، ولئن كان بدون ذلك كفاية. لم يعد ذلك سفهًا بل عد إنعامًا وإفضالا وكذا الله تعالى خلق للخلق عينين وأذنين، وكذا كل ذي عدد في الجسم، وإن كانت الحاجة تندفع والمقصود يحصل بواحد ولم يعد ذلك سفهًا بل عد تماما، وكذا الله تعالى لم يكتف بإقامة دليل واحد عقلي على ثبوته وتوحيده، بل جعل في كل مما خلق وذرأ آية لذلك ولم يعد سفها فكذا فيما نحن فيه لم يكن إرسال الرسل سفهًا وإن كان في العقل عنه غنية وكفاية، بل يعد إنعامًا وإفضالاً. ثم هذا كله منا على طريق المساهلة، فأما دلائل بطلان القول بوقوع الغنية بمجرد العقل فقد سبق ذكرها بعون الله وتوفيقه.
However, even if reason were sufficient as they claim, and there is no extra alleviation or facilitation in sending messengers, nor any meaning beyond what is in reason, but rather exactly what is in reason, that would not necessitate that sending is foolishness. Rather, it is from the category of grace and beneficence, for giving what exceeds sufficiency is considered grace and an increase in favor. And the existence of that in the world is not hidden, such as Allah's giving that which contains increased pleasure from foods even if without that food the goal of maintaining bodies is achieved. For this reason, the wise divided what Allah has brought to His servants from the types of His blessings into two divisions: one of them is from the accessories of necessity, which is what achieves the goal without having an increase of pleasure, like barley and corn, and other grains by which the maintenance of bodies is achieved, and like wool and hair by which the goal of clothing is achieved, covering private parts and repelling harm of heat and cold. And the other is from the accessories of adornment, which is that which contains increased pleasure and comfort beyond what is connected to it of bodily benefit and satisfying appetite, such as appetizing foods and fine clothes. And even if without that there was sufficiency, that is not considered foolishness but rather considered grace and favor. Similarly, Allah created for creation two eyes and two ears, and likewise everything that has a number in the body, even if the need is fulfilled and the goal is achieved by one, that is not considered foolishness but rather considered completeness. Similarly, Allah did not suffice with establishing one rational proof for His existence and His oneness, but rather placed in everything He created and disseminated a sign for that, and that is not considered foolishness. So likewise in our subject, sending messengers is not foolishness even if reason had sufficiency and adequacy about it, but rather it is considered grace and favor. Then all this from us is by way of leniency. As for the proofs of the falsehood of the claim of sufficiency by mere reason, they have already been mentioned with Allah's help and success.
Source pages p. 689

Commentary
This passage addresses a hypothetical objection: even if reason alone were sufficient for guidance, sending prophets would still not be senseless (safah). The author argues that providing more than the minimum (kifaya) is an act of grace (tafdil) and benevolence (ihsan). He illustrates this with the division of divine blessings into necessities (lawahiq al-marfiq) and adornments (lawahiq al-zina). Necessities like barley and wool meet basic needs; adornments like fine foods and clothes add pleasure and comfort. Providing the latter beyond sufficiency is not foolish but gracious. Similarly, Allah created humans with two eyes and two ears, though one would suffice, and this is considered perfection (tamam), not folly. Likewise, Allah gives multiple rational proofs for His existence and oneness. Thus, sending prophets is a similar act of grace, even if reason sufficed. The author notes this argument is lenient (musahala); the real proofs against sufficiency of reason have been given earlier.

Key Terms
الإفضال
الإحسان
الكفاية
لواحق المرفق
لواحق الزينة
السفه

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: If reason alone is sufficient for guidance, then sending prophets is redundant and therefore foolish.
Correction: The author shows that providing more than the minimum is an act of grace, not foolishness. God's generosity is not constrained by sufficiency.

Checkpoint
According to the author, why is sending prophets not foolishness even if reason sufficed?
A) Because reason is not actually sufficient.
B) Because it is an act of grace and favor, like providing more than necessary.
C) Because prophets bring new laws.
D) Because reason cannot know God.

Key Takeaway
Sending prophets is an act of divine grace, not foolishness, because God gives more than the minimum, and this generosity is evident throughout creation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you experience comfort, health, or beauty beyond the bare minimum, do you ever dismiss it as unnecessary or feel entitled to it? How does this lesson challenge that attitude and call you to see every extra blessing as a personal act of divine love?
?
God did not stop at providing one rational proof but placed signs in everything. In which area of your life have you been ignoring the many signs He has sent, settling for the minimum in your relationship with Him? What would it look like to respond to this abundance with grateful faith?
?
You believe the Prophet was sent as a mercy, but do you truly live as if his coming was an unnecessary luxury or an indispensable grace? What would change in your daily actions if you internalized that prophethood is God's generous gift beyond reason, not a redundant command?

Refuting the Objection: Sending Prophets to Rejecters Is Unwise?
The author refutes the objection that sending prophets to those who reject them is unwise.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand two key arguments used by Maturidi scholars to refute the objection that sending prophets to rejecters is unwise.

Core Idea
God's wisdom is not bound by human analogy; rejection does not nullify the purpose of prophethood.

Opponents of prophethood sometimes argue that it is unwise for God to send prophets to people He knows will reject and harm them. Imam Nasafi responds with two powerful points: first, that the opponents are inconsistent because they also deny wisdom in sending to those who accept, and second, that we cannot simply analogize from human kings to God. This lesson unpacks these arguments.

Guided Path
1
Understand the objection
Read the objection stated at the beginning: sending a prophet to someone who will reject is 'outside of wisdom'.
The objection is based on a human sense of prudence.
2
Follow the first response
Notice how the author turns the tables by showing the opponents' inconsistency: they also refuse to call sending to those who accept as wise.
3
Examine the second response
The author then challenges the analogy from the witnessed world (shahid) to the unseen (gha'ib), arguing that the two cases are not identical.
This is a key epistemological principle in kalam.
4
Reflect on the method
This lesson exemplifies a key Maturidi method: questioning the validity of analogical reasoning when comparing Creator and creation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وما زعموا أن إرسال الرسول إلى من يعلم المرسل أنه لا يجيبه إلى ما يدعوه، ويقابل رسوله بالتكذيب، خارج عن الحكمة. قلنا لهم وإرسال الرسول إلى من يعلم أنه بجيبه ويقبل نصحه وينجو بذلك عن الهلكة ويكتسب لنفسه به المنافع الجمة ويقبل على طاعة المرسل، حكمة وأنتم تأبون القول به، وتنسبونه أيضا إلى السفه، وهو دليل سفهكم. ثم يقال لهم : إن إرسال الرسول إلى من يعلم أنه لا يجيبه ويوصل المكروه إلى رسوله إن كان في الشاهد قبيحًا فلم قلتم : إنه في الغائب قبيح؟ وبأي معنى تجمعون بينهما؟ وقد بينا غير مرة أن الاستدلال بالشاهد على الغائب إنما يستقيم عند استوائهما في المعنى. ثم تقولون لو أن ملكًا من الملوك علم من طائفة من الناس أنهم لا يطيعونه
And what they claimed: that sending a messenger to someone whom the sender knows will not respond to what he calls him to, and will meet his messenger with denial, is outside of wisdom. We said to them: And sending a messenger to someone whom he knows will respond to him and accept his advice and thereby be saved from destruction and gain for himself great benefits and turn to obedience to the sender is wisdom. Yet you refuse to say it, and you also attribute it to foolishness, and that is evidence of your foolishness. Then it is said to them: If sending a messenger to someone whom he knows will not respond and will bring harm to his messenger is considered ugly in the witnessed realm, why do you say that it is ugly in the absent realm? And by what meaning do you equate the two? We have stated many times that analogizing from the witnessed to the absent is only valid when they are equal in meaning. Then you say: If a king knows about a group of people that they will not obey him
Source pages p. 690

Commentary
This passage presents an objection from opponents (al-khusum) and the author's response. The objection is: sending a prophet to people whom God knows will reject him and harm the messenger is unwise (kharij 'an al-hikma). The author gives two replies. First, by the same logic, sending a prophet to those who will accept and benefit would be wise, but the opponents refuse to admit that, which shows their inconsistency and folly. Second, the author challenges the basis of the analogy from the witnessed world (shahid) to the unseen (gha'ib). In the witnessed world, a king sending a messenger to those who will harm him is considered ugly (qabih). But for this analogy to hold in the unseen, the two cases must be identical in meaning, which is not established. The author notes that this point has been made multiple times. The passage ends mid-sentence, but the argument is clear.

Key Terms
الرسول
الحكمة
الشاهد
الغائب
الاستدلال

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: God's actions must be judged by human standards of prudence, so sending prophets to those who will reject is unwise.
Correction: God's wisdom is not constrained by human analogies; moreover, repentance and acceptance are not known with certainty, and the purpose of prophethood includes establishing evidence against rejecters.

Checkpoint
How does the author refute the objection that sending a prophet to those who reject him is unwise?
A) By claiming it is still wise.
B) By pointing out the opponents' inconsistency regarding those who accept, and questioning the analogy from shahid to gha'ib.
C) By denying that God knows the future.
D) By quoting the Quran.

Key Takeaway
The objection that prophethood is unwise due to rejection is refuted by showing the opponents' inconsistency and the fallacy of analogizing from human kings to God.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Are there areas in your life where you find yourself judging God's actions by human standards of prudence, expecting that He should only send guidance to those who will accept it? How does this lesson challenge that assumption?
?
Think of a time you were resistant to a message or guidance (from the Quran, a teacher, or life) and rejected it. In light of this passage, do you think your rejection made God's sending of that guidance unwise? What does that say about your view of God's wisdom?
?
The opponents' consistency was broken by showing they also deny wisdom in sending to accepters. In your own faith, do you ever apply double standards—accepting certain divine actions as wise only when they align with your preferences? What would it take to submit to God's wisdom unconditionally?

Sending Prophets: Grace, Not Foolishness
Nasafi defends prophethood through analogy with creation's extras.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Nasafi uses an analogy from creation (two eyes, multiple proofs) to argue that sending prophets is an act of grace (in‘am) rather than foolishness (safah).

Core Idea
Giving more than the bare minimum is grace, not foolishness.

Nasafi anticipates a possible objection: if the intellect can suffice to know God, why send prophets? Is that not foolishness? He responds by drawing an analogy from the created world. Just as God gave us two eyes and multiple proofs of His existence, so too He gives prophets as an extra gift of grace. This lesson unpacks that analogy.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then read the English translation. Let the argument's flow come through before interpreting.
2
Identify the analogy's components
Notice that Nasafi first gives a human example (two eyes/ears), then a divine example (multiple proofs), then applies the same logic to prophethood.
The analogy is the core of the argument.
3
Understand the concessive remark
At the end, Nasafi notes that this argument is presented 'by way of concession' (musahalah), and that stronger proofs were given earlier. This places the analogy in context.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بدون ذلك كفاية. لم يعد ذلك سفهًا بل عد إنعامًا وإفضالا وكذا الله تعالى خلق للخلق عينين وأذنين، وكذا كل ذي عدد في الجسم، وإن كانت الحاجة تندفع والمقصود يحصل بواحد ولم يعد ذلك سفهًا بل عد تماما، وكذا الله تعالى لم يكتف بإقامة دليل واحد عقلي على ثبوته وتوحيده، بل جعل في كل مما خلق وذرأ آية لذلك ولم يعد سفها فكذا فيما نحن فيه لم يكن إرسال الرسل سفهًا وإن كان في العقل عنه غنية وكفاية، بل يعد إنعامًا وإفضالاً. ثم هذا كله منا على طريق المساهلة، فأما دلائل بطلان القول بوقوع الغنية بمجرد العقل فقد سبق ذكرها بعون الله وتوفيقه.
Without that, sufficiency. That was not considered foolishness but was counted as grace and favor. Similarly, God Most High created for creation two eyes and two ears, and likewise everything that has number in the body, even if the need is fulfilled and the purpose is attained by one, and that was not considered foolishness but was counted as perfection. Similarly, God Most High was not satisfied with establishing one rational proof for His existence and His oneness, but He placed in everything He created and scattered a sign for that, and it was not considered foolishness. So likewise in our case, sending the messengers was not foolishness, even if the intellect is free from need of it and sufficient, but it is counted as grace and favor. Then all this from us is by way of concession; as for the proofs of the falsehood of the statement that sufficiency occurs with mere intellect, they have already been mentioned with the help and success of God.
Source pages p. 690

Commentary
This passage is an argument by analogy defending the wisdom of sending prophets against the charge of foolishness (safah). The author begins by noting that in human affairs, providing more than the bare minimum is not considered foolish but is counted as grace (in‘am) and favor (ifdal). For example, God created two eyes and two ears, even though one would suffice for the need; this is seen as perfection (tamam), not foolishness. Likewise, God did not limit Himself to a single rational proof of His existence and oneness but placed signs in every created thing. Similarly, sending prophets is not foolishness even if the intellect could theoretically dispense with them, because it is an act of grace. The author then remarks that this argument is presented by way of concession (musahalah), and that the definitive proofs against the sufficiency of reason alone have already been given earlier.

Key Terms
سفه
إنعام
إفضال
غنية
مساهلة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Providing more than necessary is wasteful or foolish.
Correction: The author argues that in creation (two eyes, multiple proofs), giving more than the minimum is seen as grace and perfection, not foolishness.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is sending prophets not considered foolishness?
A) Because prophets bring laws that reason cannot discover.
B) Because God always does what is necessary and never adds extra.
C) Because giving more than the bare minimum is counted as grace and favor, not foolishness.
D) Because the intellect is completely incapable of knowing God without prophets.

Key Takeaway
Sending prophets, like creating two eyes or providing multiple proofs, is an act of grace that goes beyond mere sufficiency.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Are you content with the bare minimum in your relationship with Allah—such as performing only obligatory acts—or do you seek His extra grace through voluntary worship and seeking knowledge? What would it mean for you to treat the sending of prophets as a personal favor from God to you, not just a historical event? If you truly believe that every extra blessing (like two eyes or multiple proofs) is a sign of God's generosity, how does that change the way you respond to His messenger today?

Reply to Objection: Sending Prophets to Non-Believers is Not Unwise
Nasafi presents and refutes an objection about sending prophets to those who will not believe.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam Nasafi refutes the objection that sending a prophet to someone known to disbelieve is unwise, using both a tu quoque argument and a methodological critique of analogy from the witnessed to the unseen.

Core Idea
God's sending prophets is wise even when He knows they will reject; the analogy to human affairs fails.

In this passage, Imam Nasafi addresses a common objection: if God knows someone will never believe, why send a prophet to them? The objectors claim this is outside wisdom. Nasafi responds with two arguments: first, turning the tables on the objectors, and second, questioning the validity of their analogy from human experience to divine action. This lesson unpacks both rebuttals.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Note what the objectors claim and how Nasafi structures his reply.
The objection is that sending a prophet to one who will not respond is 'outside of wisdom'.
2
Identify the first reply (tu quoque)
Nasafi counters by pointing out that the objectors themselves would consider sending a prophet to one who will respond as wisdom, yet they reject that notion — thus they are inconsistent.
This argument highlights the logical flaw in the objectors' position.
3
Identify the second reply (analogy critique)
Nasafi then questions the basis of their analogy from human affairs to divine actions, stating that inference from the witnessed to the unseen is only valid when meanings are equivalent.
This is a methodological point about the limits of analogical reasoning in theology.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اعتراض للخصوم: وما زعموا أن إرسال الرسول إلى من يعلم المرسل أنه لا يجيبه إلى ما يدعوه، ويقابل رسوله بالتكذيب، خارج عن الحكمة. الرد عليه: قلنا لهم وإرسال الرسول إلى من يعلم أنه يجيبه ويقبل نصحه وينجو بذلك عن الهلكة ويكتسب لنفسه به المنافع الجمة ويقبل على طاعة المرسل، حكمة وأنتم تأبون القول به، وتنسبونه أيضا إلى السفه، وهو دليل سفهكم. ثم يقال لهم : إن إرسال الرسول إلى من يعلم أنه لا يجيبه ويوصل المكروه إلى رسوله إن كان في الشاهد قبيحًا فلم قلتم : إنه في الغائب قبيح؟ وبأي معنى تجمعون بينهما؟ وقد بينا غير مرة أن الاستدلال بالشاهد على الغائب إنما يستقيم عند استوائهما في المعنى.
Objection of the opponents: And they claimed that sending a messenger to one whom the sender knows will not answer him to what he calls him to, and will meet his messenger with denial, is outside of wisdom. The reply to it: We said to them: And sending a messenger to one whom he knows will answer him and accept his advice and thereby be saved from destruction and acquire for himself abundant benefits and obey the sender, is wisdom, yet you refuse to say it and also attribute it to foolishness, and that is evidence of your foolishness. Then it is said to them: Sending a messenger to one whom he knows will not answer him and will bring harm to his messenger — if it is ugly in the witnessed, then why do you say it is ugly in the unseen? And by what meaning do you combine them? And we have stated more than once that drawing inference from the witnessed to the unseen is only valid when they are equal in meaning.
Source pages p. 690

Commentary
This passage presents an objection and its answer. The objectors claim that sending a prophet to someone whom God knows will not respond and will deny the messenger is outside wisdom (hikmah). The author replies with two points. First, a tu quoque: if sending a prophet to one who will respond is wisdom, then why do you reject that and call it foolishness? That itself is foolishness. Second, they argue that the analogy from the witnessed (shahid) to the unseen (gha'ib) is only valid when the meanings are equivalent. The objectors assume that if it is ugly in human affairs to send a messenger to someone who will harm him, then the same applies to God. But this analogy fails unless the meanings are exactly the same, which they are not due to the difference between Creator and creature.

Key Terms
حكمة
سفه
شاهد
غائب
استدلال

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that God's knowledge of future disbelief makes sending a prophet pointless or unwise.
Correction: Nasafi shows that sending a prophet can still be wise even if the recipient rejects it, because the act itself may serve other purposes, and the analogy to human affairs is flawed.

Checkpoint
What is the second argument the author uses to refute the objection?
A) God's wisdom is beyond human understanding.
B) The analogy from witnessed to unseen is invalid because God is not like humans.
C) The objectors themselves practice what they condemn.
D) Prophets bring benefit even to those who reject them.

Key Takeaway
Nasafi refutes the objection by exposing the objectors' inconsistency and by clarifying that analogical reasoning from the witnessed to the unseen requires equivalence in meaning.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever dismissed someone's actions as foolish, only to realize later that you lacked the full picture? How does this lesson challenge you to be more humble when evaluating God's wisdom?
?
What if you are the one who rejects the prophet? Does this lesson change how you view God's wisdom in sending messengers to you even if He knew you would reject? How does that affect your accountability today?
?
Nasafi says calling God's wisdom 'foolishness' is evidence of foolishness. Have you ever, even in your heart, thought God made a mistake in His plan for you? Confess that and seek to submit to His wisdom.

The King Analogy: Sending Messengers to Disobedient Subjects Is Wise
Nasafi presents a king analogy to show wisdom in sending messengers to disobedient subjects.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Nasafi uses a king analogy to argue that sending prophets to those who reject them is wise because the messengers are compensated with eternal reward.

Core Idea
Compensation transforms apparent foolishness into wisdom.

Nasafi presents a clever analogy from human kingship to counter the objection that sending prophets to people who will harm them is unwise. He constructs a scenario where a king sends messengers to rebels and compensates them abundantly, making the act wise. This lesson walks through the analogy and its implications.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing. Then read the translation. Let the analogy unfold.
2
Identify the scenario
Note that the king knows the rebels will not obey and will harm his allies. He has two options: punish or send messengers.
The king's foreknowledge is key to the analogy.
3
Understand the compensation
The king promises the messengers eternal blessings for temporary harm. This changes the moral calculus.
This is the core of the argument.
4
Consider the question and answers
The king asks: am I wise? If opponent says no, they show ignorance. If yes, their objection collapses.
Apply the same logic to God and prophets.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم تقولون لو أن ملكًا من الملوك علم من طائفة من الناس أنهم لا يطيعونه ولا ينقادون له بل يؤثرون عداوته، وينتصبون حربًا لأوليائه، وعلم أنه لو قابلهم بالاستئصال وعاملهم بالتنكيل والاجتياح قبل الأعداد والأنداد، وأخذ الحجة عليهم، لنسبه من عاين فعله أو بلغه صنيعه إلى الظلم والعدوان، ووسمه بسمة الجور والظلم والبغي، فبعث إليهم سفراء وقدم إليهم بشراء ونذراء ليلزمهم حجته ويظهر لدى الناس في الانتقام منهم وإنزال البأس أنه يعطى الرسول بمقابلة ما يصل إليه من المكروه الذي ينقضي في أسرع مدة نعما دائمة يتقلب فيها مدة مديدة وينيله بمقابلة ذلك من اللذات ما يتمنى الرسول أن لو كان أوصل إليه من المكروه أضعاف ما أوصل، أكان هذا المرسل حكيمًا في ذلك؟ فإن قالوا: لا، ظهر جهلهم بالحكمة والسفه، وإن قالوا: نعم، ظهر أن ما ظنوه سفها، حكمة، وخاب سعيهم وبطلت شبهتهم، وبالله التوفيق.
Then you say: If a king among kings knew of a group of people that they would not obey him nor submit to him, but rather prefer his enmity and set themselves up for war against his allies, and he knew that if he were to exterminate them and treat them with punishment and destruction before the numbers and peers, and take the argument against them, whoever witnessed his action or heard of his deed would attribute to him injustice and aggression and mark him with the mark of tyranny, injustice, and transgression. So he sent to them ambassadors and presented to them bringers of good news and warners to establish his argument against them and to make it apparent among the people in taking revenge on them and inflicting punishment, that he gives the messenger, in return for the harm that reaches him which passes in the shortest time, permanent blessings in which he turns about for a long period, and gives him in return for that pleasures such that the messenger would wish that he had caused him harm many times over. Would this sender be wise in that? If they say: No, their ignorance of wisdom and foolishness becomes apparent. If they say: Yes, it becomes apparent that what they thought was foolishness is wisdom, and their effort fails and their specious argument is nullified. And with God is success.
Source pages p. 691

Commentary
This passage is an independent argument using a hypothetical example from human affairs. The author constructs a scenario: a king knows that a group will not obey him and will oppose him. If he simply punishes them, he would be called unjust. Instead, he sends ambassadors (messengers) to establish his argument, and promises to compensate the messengers for any harm they suffer with eternal blessings and pleasures. The question is: is such a king wise? If the opponent says no, they show ignorance of wisdom. If they say yes, then their claim that God sending prophets to rejecters is foolish collapses. The argument relies on the principle that compensating a messenger for temporary harm with permanent reward makes the act wise.

Key Terms
حكمة
سفه
ملك
رسول
حجة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Sending a prophet to someone who will harm him is inherently unwise.
Correction: The king analogy shows that if the messenger is compensated with eternal reward, the act becomes wise.

Checkpoint
In the king analogy, what makes sending the messengers wise?
A) The king punishes the rebels immediately.
B) The messengers are forced to go.
C) The messengers are compensated with permanent blessings for temporary harm.
D) The rebels are given no choice.

Key Takeaway
Sending prophets to those who reject them is wise because the messengers are compensated with eternal reward.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you were a prophet facing rejection, would the promise of eternal reward really sustain you? Examine your own heart – do you truly believe that Allah's compensation makes any hardship worth it? What would need to change in your certainty for you to live that conviction?
?
The analogy hinges on the king being wise because he compensates the messenger. How does this compel you to reconsider your own judgments about Allah's actions when you see believers suffering? Will you trust His wisdom even when you don't see the compensation yet?
?
If you were that king, would you send messengers knowing they'd be harmed? What does your answer reveal about your grasp of justice and wisdom? Commit to one area where you will stop judging Allah's wisdom by your limited perspective.

Refutation of Al-Khali's Claim: Commanding Without Benefit Is Not Foolish
Nasafi refutes al-Khali‘s claim that commanding without benefit is foolishness.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Nasafi argues that divine command and prohibition without benefit or harm is not foolishness, because obligation gives purpose to creation.

Core Idea
Obligation gives purpose to creation; without it, all would be foolish.

Al-Khali' claimed that commanding without benefit is foolish, implying that God's commands would be pointless. Nasafi refutes this by showing that obligation (taklif) itself is the purpose that makes creation meaningful. This passage explains that without reward and punishment, creation would be an aimless cycle, but with obligation, it becomes wise.

Guided Path
1
Understand al-Khali's claim
Recognize the objection: commanding without benefit or harm is foolishness. This is the position Nasafi refutes.
Al-Khali‘ is a specific opponent; his name means 'the one who strips away'.
2
Grasp Nasafi's conditional argument
Nasafi shows that if there were no obligation, reward, or punishment, then creation would indeed be purposeless and foolish. This is a counterfactual to expose the flaw in al-Khali's reasoning.
The conditional 'if not... then...' is key to the argument.
3
Follow the conclusion
Since obligation does exist, creation is not foolish but wise. Therefore, calling it foolish is itself foolish.
The argument turns al-Khali's accusation back on him.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقد خرج الجواب عما تعلق به الخليع، أن الأمر والنهي بما لا نفع للأمر في تحصيله ولا ضرر على الناهي في فعل ما نهى عنه سفه، إذ قد بينا في أثناء كلامنا أن التكليف لو لم يكن وانعدم الثواب والعقاب ولم تصر الدنيا مطية إلى الآخرة التي فيها يجازى المحسن بإحسانه والمسيء بإساءته، صار تخليقه العالم ليوجد ثم يتلاشى ويثبت ثم ينعدم، ويفنى من غير أن يتعلق به غرض أو يحصل له عاقبة حميدة. وهذا النوع من الفعل سفه يذم فاعله، وتأبى الحكمة إطلاقه، وذا غير جائز على الله تعالى. فإذا صار تخليق العالم بواسطة التكليف حكمة، فمن ظن ذلك سفها فهو سفه.
And the answer has come out concerning what al-Khali‘ clung to: that commanding and forbidding (al-amr wa al-nahy) of that which there is no benefit for the commander in its attainment and no harm for the prohibitor in doing what he forbade is foolishness (safah). For we have explained in the course of our speech that if obligation (al-taklif) were not, and reward and punishment were non-existent, and the world did not become a mount to the Hereafter in which the good-doer is rewarded for his goodness and the evil-doer is punished for his evil, then His creation of the world to exist then vanish, and to be established then cease to exist, and to perish without any purpose attached to it or any praiseworthy outcome resulting, this type of act is foolishness, the doer of which is blamed, and wisdom refuses to allow it. And this is not permissible for God Most High. So when creation of the world becomes wisdom by means of obligation, then whoever thinks that is foolishness is foolish.
Source pages p. 691

Commentary
This passage is a rebuttal of al-Khali‘’s argument. Al-Khali‘ claimed that commanding and forbidding without any benefit to the commander or harm to the prohibitor is foolishness (safah). The author responds by explaining that if there were no obligation (taklif), no reward or punishment, and the world were not a means to the Hereafter, then creation would be purposeless: things come into existence and then perish without any aim or good consequence. Such an act would indeed be foolish and unworthy of God. But since God has established obligation, the creation of the world becomes wise. Therefore, calling it foolishness is itself foolish.

Key Terms
خليع
أمر و نهي
تكليف
ثواب
عقاب
حكمة
سفه

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that obligation is pointless if God is self-sufficient.
Correction: The author shows that obligation gives purpose to creation, without which creation would be foolish.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what would make creation foolish?
A) If there were many prophets.
B) If there were no obligation, reward, or punishment.
C) If God created the world for no reason.
D) Both B and C.

Key Takeaway
Obligation (taklif) is the key that transforms creation from a purposeless cycle into a wise and meaningful act of God.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you live as if this world is merely a mount to the Hereafter, or have you made it your final destination? What would you change today if you truly believed that every action is being weighed for an eternal outcome?
?
Have you ever considered some of God's commands burdensome or pointless? After reading that without obligation creation would be foolishness, how does that reframe your attitude toward His commands?
?
The passage says calling God's command foolish makes the caller foolish. Do you secretly harbor any resentment against God's decree, thinking it unfair or meaningless? Will you repent from that and submit to His wisdom, even when you do not see the benefit?

The Wisdom of Sending Messengers Despite Harm
The author proves divine wisdom in sending messengers despite harm.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the author proves that sending messengers despite their suffering is an act of divine wisdom, not folly.

Core Idea
God's wisdom is evident in compensating prophets' temporary harm with eternal bliss.

This passage tackles a profound objection: why would a wise God allow His prophets to suffer? The author constructs a powerful analogy that turns the accusation of folly into a proof of wisdom. By walking through the hypothetical and the compensation argument, you will see how apparent injustice is actually a display of perfect wisdom.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse every word. Then read the English translation to grasp the overall argument.
Notice the rhetorical question at the end — it's the climax of the argument.
2
Follow the hypothetical scenario
The author first imagines what would happen if God punished the disbelievers immediately without sending messengers. Understand why that would lead to accusations of injustice.
3
Analyze the compensation argument
God sends messengers and compensates their temporary harm with eternal blessings. This refutes the charge of folly. Consider why a messenger would wish for more harm.
4
Reflect on the rhetorical question
The question 'Is this sender wise?' forces the opponent to either admit ignorance or concede wisdom. Reflect on how this defeats the objection.
This is a classic tawqif (stopping) argument.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا ينقادون له بل يؤثرون عداوته، وينتصبون حربًا لأوليائه، وعلم أنه لو قابلهم بالاستئصال وعاملهم بالتنكيل والاجتياح قبل الأعداد والأنداد، وأخذ الحجة عليهم، لنسبه من عاين فعله أو بلغه صنيعه إلى الظلم والعدوان، ووسمه بسمة الجور والظلم والبغي، فبعث إليهم سفراء وقدم إليهم بشراء ونذراء ليلزمهم حجته ويظهر لدى الناس في الانتقام منهم وإنزال البأس أنه يعطى الرسول بمقابلة ما يصل إليه من المكروه الذي ينقضي في أسرع مدة نعما دائمة يتقلب فيها مدة مديدة وينيله بمقابلة ذلك من اللذات ما يتمنى الرسول أن لو كان أوصل إليه من المكروه أضعاف ما أوصل، أكان هذا المرسل حكيمًا في ذلك؟ فإن قالوا: لا، ظهر جهلهم بالحكمة والسفه، وإن قالوا: نعم، ظهر أن ما ظنوه سفها، حكمة، وخاب سعيهم وبطلت شبهتهم
And they do not submit to him, rather they prefer his enmity, and they set themselves up as war against his allies. And He knew that if He were to confront them with extermination and treat them with punishment and destruction before [establishing] the messengers and adversaries, and taking the proof against them, then whoever witnessed His action or heard of His deed would attribute to Him injustice and aggression, and brand Him with the mark of oppression, injustice, and transgression. So He sent to them messengers and presented to them bringers of good news and warners, in order to bind them with His proof and to make manifest among the people—in the [act of] taking vengeance upon them and inflicting calamity—that He gives the messenger, in exchange for what reaches him of harm that passes in a very short time, perpetual blessings in which he will turn about for a long period, and He bestows upon him in exchange for that such pleasures that the messenger would wish that he had caused to reach him of harm double what he caused. Is this sender wise in that? If they say: No, their ignorance of wisdom and folly becomes apparent. And if they say: Yes, then it becomes apparent that what they thought was folly is wisdom, and their effort fails and their false argument is invalidated.
Source pages p. 691

Commentary
This passage presents a proof by analogy demonstrating the wisdom of God sending messengers despite the harm they suffer. The argument begins by describing the disbelievers' refusal to submit and their hostility. God knows that if He destroyed them immediately without sending messengers and establishing proof, observers would accuse Him of injustice. Therefore, He sends messengers to establish proof, and when He punishes, it is clear that He compensates the messenger for temporary harm with eternal blessings, so the messenger would wish to have suffered more. The author asks: is this sender (God) wise? If the opponent says no, they show ignorance. If yes, then their accusation of folly is refuted. The passage concludes that what seemed like folly is actually wisdom.

Key Terms
