ثم الدليل على أن الرسالة تثبت فيما مضى من الأزمنة ما مر من أن الجواهر الموجودة في العالم منقسمة إلى أغذية وسموم وأدوية، ولا وصول إلى الامتياز بين البعض منها والبعض بالتجربة، ولا بقاء للأبدان بدون تناول الأغذية ورأينا الناس من اهتدوا إليها وإلى معرفة طبائعها ومعرفة مقادير الأدوية التي تتعلق بها المصلحة ولا تحصل بالنقصان منها المصلحة وتحصل بالزيادة عليها المضرة مع أن لا وقوف بشيء من الحواس على شيء منها ولا بالعقول، إذ أصح خليقة الله تعالى حساً وأوفرهم عقلاً يمكنه الوصول إلى ذلك ما لم يختلف إلى أستاذ حاذق حصل له العلم بذلك من غيره، فثبت أن من علم ذلك علم بأخباره غيره إياه لا بحسه وعقله لقصور علم غيره عنه مع مساواته في العقل والحس إلى أن ينتهي العلم بذلك إلى إخبار من له العلم بحقيقة كل من ذلك لما أنه خلقه على ما خلقه، وفي ذلك أبين دليل على ثبوت الرسالة فيما مضى لبعض من اصطفاه الله تعالى لذلك وأكرمه بإعلامه إياه طبائع هذه الجواهر ولهذا اضطر أهل العلم بطبائع هذه الجواهر المنكرين للرسالة إلى الاعتراف بأن العلم بطبائعها توقيفي فإنهم مهما قيل لهم ممن أخذتم العلم بطبائع هذه الأشياء؟ قالوا من بقراط؟ فإذا قيل لهم : وممن أخذه بقراط؟ قالوا: من أسغلينوس الإمام الذي عرج بروحه إلى السماء فاطلع عليها ، وكذا العلم بالنجوم وهيئة الأفلاك وطبائع الكواكب وكيفية سيرها والسعد فيها والنحس ، وأحكام الاتصالات بينها لن يتوصل إلى ذلك إلا بالتوقيف لتعذر الحواس والعقول عن ذلك، ولهذا لم يقف على ذلك أحد من أرباب الحواس السليمة والعقول الوافرة، ولهذا اضطر أهل النجوم
Then the proof that prophethood (risaalah) is established in past times is that which has passed: that the substances (jawaahir) existing in the world are divided into foods, poisons, and medicines, and there is no way to distinguish between some of them and others by experience (tajribah), nor can bodies survive without consuming foods, and we see people who have been guided to them and to knowledge of their natures and to knowledge of the quantities of medicines that bring benefit—benefit is not attained by deficiency and harm is attained by excess—while no sense perceives any of that, nor do intellects, for the soundest of Allah's creatures in sense and the most abundant in intellect can only attain that by going to a skilled teacher (ustadh haadhiq) who has obtained the knowledge from another. So it is established that whoever knows that knows it by another's informing him, not by his sense and intellect, because of the deficiency of the knowledge of others relative to him while being equal in intellect and sense, until the knowledge ends at one who has knowledge of the reality of each of them because He created them as He created them. In that is the clearest proof of the establishment of prophethood in the past for some whom Allah chose for that and honored by informing him of the natures of these substances. And for this reason, the people of knowledge of the natures of these substances who deny prophethood are forced to admit that knowledge of their natures is derived from divine teaching (tawqifi). For whenever it is said to them, 'From whom did you take knowledge of the natures of these things?' they say, 'From Hippocrates.' Then if it is said to them, 'From whom did Hippocrates take it?' they say, 'From Asclepius (Asghalinus), the imam whose spirit ascended to the heavens and was informed of them.' Likewise, knowledge of the stars, the configuration of the spheres, the natures of the planets, how they move, their auspiciousness and inauspiciousness, and the judgments of the conjunctions between them—one cannot reach that except through divine teaching due to the inability of the senses and intellects to grasp that. And for that reason, no possessor of sound senses and abundant intellect has attained it. And for that reason, the people of astrology are compelled...
Source pages p. 699

Commentary
This passage presents a proof for the general establishment of prophethood in past ages. The author begins with a familiar argument: the substances in the world are divided into foods, poisons, and medicines. Distinguishing them is impossible through mere experience or reason, especially concerning the precise quantities of medicines that bring benefit or harm. Yet we see that people have learned these things. They learn from a skilled teacher, and this chain of teaching must eventually end with someone who was directly informed by the Creator, because the knowledge cannot be attained by the unaided human faculties. This person is a prophet. The author offers two historical examples to support this: the medical tradition traces back to Asclepius, who according to legend ascended to heaven and was shown these matters; and likewise, the knowledge of astrology, including celestial movements and astrological judgments, could only come from divine teaching, not from senses or intellect. Therefore, the very existence of such specialized knowledge among humans proves that prophethood is a reality. The passage ends abruptly noting that astrologers are compelled (to admit divine teaching), but the sentence is incomplete due to the page break.

Key Terms
الرسالة
الجواهر
التجربة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That such knowledge was discovered gradually through human trial and error.
Correction: The author argues that trial and error (experience) alone cannot yield precise distinctions, especially for quantities where excess harms; therefore divine teaching is necessary.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is it impossible to distinguish foods, poisons, and medicines by experience alone?
A) Because they look identical.
B) Because the quantities that bring benefit or harm cannot be determined by trial and error.
C) Because people never tried to distinguish them.
D) Because the intellect is sufficient.

Key Takeaway
Specialized knowledge about substances cannot be acquired by human faculties alone; its existence proves divine teaching through prophets.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The passage says that even the most intelligent person cannot know the nature of substances without a teacher. Where in your life have you assumed your intelligence alone is sufficient, ignoring the need for prophetic guidance? Will you admit that area today and seek the Prophet’s ﷺ teachings on it?
?
Are there truths you resist accepting because they come from revelation rather than your own reasoning? Can you name one specific teaching of the Prophet ﷺ that you find difficult—and will you submit to it even if your intellect cannot fully grasp it?
?
If you truly believed that some knowledge can only come from a prophet, how would that change the way you prioritize learning the Quran and Sunnah over other sources of information? What concrete step will you take this week to learn from the Prophet ﷺ?

Prophethood

Historical Evidence: Hippocrates, Asclepius, and Astrology
Nasafi uses medical and astrological traditions to show that deniers admit divine origin.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how historical examples from medicine and astrology demonstrate that even those who deny prophethood are forced to admit divine teaching.

Core Idea
Deniers admit that knowledge came from a divinely taught source like Asclepius.

After establishing the logical necessity of a divine teacher, Imam al-Nasafi provides concrete historical examples. He points to the medical tradition traced to Hippocrates and Asclepius, and to the science of astrology. In both cases, the experts themselves acknowledge that their knowledge originated from a supernatural source. This lesson examines these examples and their role in confirming prophethood.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and translation
Read the text carefully. Notice how the author uses the chain of transmission in medicine to show that the ultimate source is divine.
2
Understand the medical chain
The author says that when asked, doctors trace their knowledge to Hippocrates, who learned from Asclepius, who ascended to heaven and was taught by God.
This is an acknowledgment of divine teaching.
3
Consider the astrology example
Similarly, knowledge of stars and their influences cannot be attained by senses or intellect, so astrologers also rely on a divine source.
4
Connect to the main proof
These examples show that even people who reject prophethood implicitly accept that such knowledge requires divine teaching, which proves that prophets existed.

Prophethood
beginner

Proof of Prophethood from the Need for Divine Instruction
Nasafi proves the necessity of revelation for knowledge of substances, stars, crafts, and languages.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the need for divine instruction in fields like medicine, astrology, and crafts proves the necessity of prophethood.

Core Idea
Human reason and senses are insufficient for essential knowledge — revelation is necessary.

Nasafi presents a compelling argument that prophethood is necessary because certain vital human knowledge, such as the distinction between foods and poisons, the motions of stars, and the origins of languages, cannot be attained by reason or experience alone. He traces the origins of such knowledge back to divine revelation, showing that even those who deny prophethood implicitly admit this. This lesson unpacks his reasoning step by step.

Guided Path
1
Read the full argument
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing, then the translation. Let the author's flow come through before interpreting.
This is a long passage covering multiple examples.
2
Understand the core thesis
Notice that the author starts with the thesis: knowledge of the natures of substances (foods, poisons, medicines) is impossible by sense or reason alone, so it must be taught by someone with complete knowledge — a prophet.
This is the logical foundation.
3
Examine the medical example
See how even the greatest minds need a teacher, and how medical knowledge is traced back to Asclepius, who ascended to heaven. This shows even experts acknowledge divine origin.
This is a historical argument.
4
Trace the same logic to astrology and other fields
Nasafi applies the same reasoning to astrology (traced to Hermes/Idris), then to crafts, animal training, commerce, geography, and languages. In each case, human capability falls short.
Each example reinforces the same point.
5
Conclude the necessity of prophethood
The cumulative evidence shows that essential human knowledge must come from revelation, which implies the existence of prophets as recipients of that revelation.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الدليل على ثبوت الرسالة في الأزمنة الماضية: ثم الدليل على أن الرسالة تثبت فيما مضى من الأزمنة ما مر من أن الجواهر الموجودة في العالم منقسمة إلى أغذية وسموم وأدوية، ولا وصول إلى الامتياز بين البعض منها والبعض بالتجربة، ولا بقاء للأبدان بدون تناول الأغذية ورأينا الناس من اهتدوا إليها وإلى معرفة طبائعها ومعرفة مقادير الأدوية التي تتعلق بها المصلحة ولا تحصل بالنقصان منها المصلحة وتحصل بالزيادة عليها المضرة مع أن لا وقوف بشيء من الحواس على شيء منها ولا بالعقول، إذ أصح خليقة الله تعالى حساً وأوفرهم عقلاً يمكنه الوصول إلى ذلك ما لم يختلف إلى أستاذ حاذق حصل له العلم بذلك من غيره، فثبت أن من علم ذلك علم بأخباره غيره إياه لا بحسه وعقله لقصور علم غيره عنه مع مساواته في العقل والحس إلى أن ينتهي العلم بذلك إلى إخبار من له العلم بحقيقة كل من ذلك لما أنه خلقه على ما خلقه، وفي ذلك أبين دليل على ثبوت وكيفية سيرها والسعد فيها والنحس ، وأحكام الاتصالات بينها لن يتوصل إلى ذلك إلا بالتوقيف لتعذر الحواس والعقول عن ذلك، ولهذا لم يقف على ذلك أحد من أرباب الحواس السليمة والعقول الوافرة، ولهذا اضطر أهل النجوم حين سئلوا عن ذلك إلى أن قالوا: بدء معرفته من قبل هرمس الحكيم وقد عرج بروحه إلى السماء، فكانت في ملكوت السماوات وعرف ذلك كله مشاهدة. وزعم بعض من ادعى العلم بالحقائق أن هرمس هو اسم إدريس عليه السلام، عند أهل المغرب في علم يعرفونه بهذا الاسم، وأهل التواريخ يزعمون أن علم النجوم نزل على إدريس عليه السلام. وهذا من أبين الدلائل أن ذلك كله ثبت بطريق الوحي من الله تعالى. وكذا العلم بالحرف التي بها قوام المعاش واتخاذ الستر والكن والوقاية من الحر والبرد. وكذا العلم بكيفية رياضة الدواب الصعبة مما ليس يعلم بالتأمل أنها لأي منفعة خلقت وبأي وجه يمكن رياضتها وتذليل صعابها وإيناس نافرها ومستوحشها. وكذا العلم بأنواع التجارات التي لا يقوم للناس دين ولا دنيا إلا بها. وكذا العلم بما يفرق بين حوائجهم فى البلدان لن يثبت إلا بالتوقيف لقصور العقول والحواس عن الوقوف على ذلك. وكذا العلم بطرق البلدان، وكذا العلم بالألسن إذ لا وجه إلى الاصطلاح إلا بعد ثبوت العلم بلسان ليتوصل بمعرفة ذلك اللسان إلى الاصطلاح على لسان آخر إذ لا وصول إلى ذلك إلا بعد وقوف المصطلحين بعضهم على ما في ضمير البعض، فإذا لابد من كون لسان ثابتا بالوحي.
The proof for the establishment of prophethood in past times: Then the proof that prophethood is established in past times is that which has passed: that the substances existing in the world are divided into foods, poisons, and medicines, and there is no access to distinguishing between some of them and others by experience, and no survival of bodies without consuming foods. And we have seen people who were guided to them and to knowledge of their natures and knowledge of the amounts of medicines to which benefit is attached, and benefit is not obtained by decreasing them, and harm is obtained by increasing them, while there is no cognition by any of the senses of any of them, nor by intellects. For the soundest of God’s creatures in sense and the most abundant of them in intellect can only reach that if he goes to a skillful teacher who has acquired knowledge of that from others. So it is established that whoever knows that, knows it by the informing of another to him, not by his sense and intellect, due to the deficiency of the knowledge of others besides him despite their equality in intellect and sense, until that knowledge ends at the informing of one who has knowledge of the reality of each of those things because He created them as He created them. And in that is the clearest proof for the establishment of prophethood in the past for some whom God chose for that and honored by informing him of the natures of these substances. And for this reason the people of knowledge of the natures of these substances, who deny prophethood, were forced to admit that knowledge of their natures is tawqifī (dependent on divine instruction). For whenever it is said to them, ‘From whom did you take knowledge of the natures of these things?’ they said, ‘From Hippocrates?’ And when it is said to them, ‘And from whom did Hippocrates take it?’ they said, ‘From Asclepius the imam who ascended with his spirit to the heavens and was informed of them.’ And likewise knowledge of the stars, the configuration of the spheres, the natures of the planets, the manner of their motion, good fortune and bad fortune therein, and the judgments of the conjunctions between them — no one can arrive at that except by tawqīf because the senses and intellects are incapable of that. And for this reason no one from among the possessors of sound senses and abundant intellects has ever attained that. And for this reason the astrologers, when asked about that, said: ‘The beginning of knowledge of it was from Hermes the Wise, and he ascended with his spirit to the heavens, and he was in the kingdom of the heavens and knew all of that by witnessing.’ And some of those who claimed knowledge of realities claimed that Hermes is the name of Idris (peace be upon him), according to the people of the Maghrib in a knowledge they know by this name, and the historians claim that the knowledge of the stars was revealed to Idris (peace be upon him). And this is among the clearest proofs that all of that was established by way of revelation from God. And likewise knowledge of the crafts by which livelihood is maintained and the making of covering, shelter, and protection from heat and cold. And likewise knowledge of the manner of training difficult beasts, which cannot be known by reflection for what benefit they were created and in what way it is possible to train them, subdue their difficulties, and tame their wild and untamed ones. And likewise knowledge of the types of commerce without which neither religion nor worldly life is established for people. And likewise knowledge of what distinguishes their needs in the lands — it is not established except by tawqīf, due to the deficiency of intellects and senses in attaining that. And likewise knowledge of the routes of lands, and likewise knowledge of languages, since there is no way to convention except after the establishment of knowledge of one language to attain through knowledge of that language to convention upon another language, for there is no access to that except after the conventionalists know what is in the conscience of some others. Therefore there must be a language established by revelation.
Source pages p. 700

Commentary
This passage is a proof for the establishment of prophethood in past times. It begins by stating the thesis: the proof for prophethood in past eras is that the substances (jawahir) in the world are divided into foods, poisons, and medicines. Humans cannot distinguish between them by mere experience or sense perception, nor can they survive without food. Yet we observe people who have been guided to knowledge of their natures and the correct dosages of medicines. Even the most perfect in sense and intellect cannot attain this knowledge without learning from a skilled teacher. Therefore, such knowledge must ultimately come from someone who knows the true nature of these substances because He created them as they are. This shows that there must have been a prophet informed by God. The author then notes that even those who deny prophethood are forced to admit that knowledge of natures is tawqīfī (divinely taught), as seen in their genealogy of medical knowledge back to Asclepius, who ascended to heaven. The same applies to astrology: it cannot be known by sense or reason, so astrologers trace it to Hermes (identified by some with Prophet Idris). The author concludes that this is clear evidence that such knowledge came through revelation. He then extends the argument to other domains: crafts (such as making shelter and clothing), training wild animals, commerce, geography (routes of lands), and languages. For each, he argues that human reason and senses are insufficient, so they must have been divinely taught. This proves the necessity of prophethood.

Key Terms
الرسالة (risala)
التوقيف (tawqif)
الجواهر (jawahir)
الوحي (wahi)
إدريس (Idris)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The examples of Asclepius, Hermes, etc. are mere mythology and do not constitute valid proof.
Correction: Nasafi uses these as commonly accepted historical claims among experts in those fields. Even if their historical accuracy is debated, the argument shows that practitioners themselves admit the divine origin of their knowledge.

Checkpoint
According to the author, why does knowledge of medicine, stars, crafts, and languages prove the necessity of prophethood?
A) Because these sciences are too complex for humans to learn without teachers.
B) Because human senses and reason alone cannot attain this knowledge, so it must come from divine revelation.
C) Because all ancient knowledge was transmitted by prophets.
D) Because the practitioners of these sciences admitted they learned from prophets.

Key Takeaway
The necessity of prophethood is proven by the fact that knowledge humans depend on for survival and civilization can only come from divine revelation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you face a difficult question about life’s purpose, whose knowledge do you turn to? Have you ever consciously relied on divine guidance over your own reasoning? How would your life change if you truly believed that your most critical knowledge depends on revelation?
?
The passage shows that even great minds like Hippocrates admitted their knowledge came from above. Are you humble enough to acknowledge that what you know about good and evil, success and failure, ultimately depends on God’s teaching? If so, what step will you take today to submit your intellect to His book?
?
If knowledge of simple things like foods and medicines requires a prophet, what does that imply about your ability to navigate spiritual matters on your own? How does this challenge your self-reliance in seeking truth, and what are you willing to surrender to hear the voice of the One who knows creation?

Knowledge from Divine Revelation: The Necessity of Tawqif
The author enumerates categories of knowledge that require divine revelation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why many essential types of human knowledge, such as languages and trades, must originate from divine revelation (tawqif) rather than from reason or senses alone.

Core Idea
Our intellect and senses are insufficient; revelation is the necessary source for foundational knowledge.

This passage from Imam al-Nasafi presents a powerful argument for the necessity of prophethood and divine revelation. He lists numerous areas of human knowledge that cannot be acquired solely through empirical observation or rational deduction. The existence of this knowledge among people is itself a proof that Allah taught it to them via prophets. As you read, see how each example points to the same conclusion: our natural capacities have limits, and revelation fills those gaps.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the English translation. Pay attention to the flow of examples.
The passage uses a repetitive structure: 'وكذا العلم بـ...'.
2
Identify the main claim
The author states that knowledge of various sciences cannot be obtained except through tawqif (divine instruction). Note how he uses the Hermes/Idris story to introduce the idea.
3
Examine the list of sciences
Go through each item in the list: basic skills, animal training, trades, needs, geography, languages, reproduction, child-rearing, magic, warfare. Ask yourself why each cannot be learned by reason or senses.
Pay special attention to the reasoning about languages – it's a key argument.
4
Reflect on the conclusion
The author concludes that since these sciences cannot be attained by senses or intellect, their existence proves they are from Allah via revelation. Consider how this argument supports the necessity of prophethood.

حين سئلوا عن ذلك إلى أن قالوا: بدء معرفته من قيل هرمس الحكيم وقد عرج بروحه إلى السماء، فكانت في ملكوت السماوات وعرف ذلك كله مشاهدة. وزعم بعض من ادعى العلم بالحقائق أن هرمس هو اسم إدريس عليه السلام، عند أهل المغرب في علم يعرفونه بهذا الاسم، وأهل التواريخ يزعمون أن علم النجوم نزل على إدريس عليه السلام. وهذا من أبين الدلائل أن ذلك كله ثبت بطريق الوحي من الله تعالى. وكذا العلم بالحرف التي بها قوام المعاش واتخاذ الستر والكن والوقاية من الحر والبرد. وكذا العلم بكيفية رياضة الدواب الصعبة مما ليس يعلم بالتأمل أنها لأي منفعة خلقت وبأي وجه يمكن رياضتها وتذليل صعابها وإيناس نافرها ومستوحشها. وكذا العلم بأنواع التجارات التي لا يقوم للناس دين ولا دنيا إلا بها. وكذا العلم بما يفرق بين حوائجهم فى البلدان لن يثبت إلا بالتوقيف لقصور العقول والحواس عن الوقوف على ذلك. وكذا العلم بطرق البلدان، وكذا العلم بالألسن إذ لا وجه إلى الاصطلاح إلا بعد ثبوت العلم بلسان ليتوصل بمعرفة ذلك اللسان إلى الاصطلاح على لسان آخر إذ لا وصول إلى ذلك إلا بعد وقوف المصطلحين بعضهم على ما في ضمير البعض، فإذا لابد من كون لسان ثابتا بالوحي. وكذا العلم بوجوه أسباب التناسل، والعلم بكيفية تربية الصغار والعلم بتدابير أغذية ما ليس له نطق. وكذا العلم بالسحر وتغيير جواهر الأشياء بأنواع المعالجات. وعلوم محاربة الأعداء. فكان ثبوت العلم بهذه الأشياء مع استنساخ حصول ذلك بشيء من الحواس أو العقل، دليلاً أن العلم بها كلها توقيف من عند العليم الخبير الذي لا يعزب عنه شيء ولا يخفى عليه خافية، وذلك يكون بالوحي إلى من اصطفاه لرسالته والله الموفق.
When they were asked about that, they said: The beginning of his knowledge was from what was said of Hermes the wise, and his spirit ascended to heaven, and he was in the dominion of the heavens and knew all that by direct vision. And some of those who claimed knowledge of realities claimed that Hermes is the name of Idris (peace be upon him) among the people of the West in a science they know by this name, and the historians claim that the science of stars was revealed to Idris (peace be upon him). And this is among the clearest proofs that all that was established by way of revelation from Allah the Exalted. Likewise the knowledge of letters by which sustenance is established and the making of coverings, shelters, and protection from heat and cold. Likewise the knowledge of the method of training difficult beasts, which is not known by reflection for what benefit they were created and in what way their training, subduing of their difficulties, and domesticating their wild and shy ones is possible. Likewise the knowledge of the types of trades without which neither religion nor worldly life is established for people. Likewise the knowledge of what distinguishes their needs in the lands, which is only established by divine instruction (tawqif) due to the incapacity of intellects and senses to comprehend that. Likewise the knowledge of routes of lands, and likewise the knowledge of languages, for there is no way to convention except after the establishment of knowledge of one language to reach, by knowing that language, the convention of another language, since there is no access to that except after the conventioneers come to know what is in the conscience of each other. Thus there must be a language established by revelation. Likewise the knowledge of the ways of the causes of reproduction, and the knowledge of the method of raising children, and the knowledge of the management of nutrition for those without speech. Likewise the knowledge of magic and the alteration of the essences of things by various treatments. And the sciences of fighting enemies. So the establishment of knowledge of these things, along with the impossibility of their attainment by any of the senses or intellect, is evidence that knowledge of all of them is a divine instruction (tawqif) from the All-Knowing, the All-Aware, from whom nothing is absent and no secret is hidden, and that is by revelation to whom He has chosen for His message. And Allah is the granter of success.
Source pages p. 701

Commentary
This passage is an argument that many essential types of knowledge must originate from divine revelation (tawqif). The author begins by referencing a claim that the origin of certain knowledge goes back to Hermes the Wise (identified by some as Prophet Idris), who allegedly ascended to heaven and observed celestial realities. This, he says, is a clear proof that such knowledge came through revelation. Then he enumerates several categories of knowledge that cannot be acquired through reason or senses alone: (1) knowledge of letters and basic survival skills like making clothes and shelter; (2) knowledge of training wild animals; (3) knowledge of trades essential for religion and worldly life; (4) knowledge of differentiating societal needs; (5) knowledge of geographical routes; (6) knowledge of languages, which requires a first language established by revelation before any conventional language can be agreed upon; (7) knowledge of reproduction and child-rearing; (8) knowledge of feeding infants; (9) knowledge of magic and alchemy; and (10) knowledge of warfare. Since none of these can be attained purely by empirical observation or logical reasoning, their existence among humans is evidence that Allah taught them through prophets via revelation. This reinforces the necessity of prophethood.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that languages and trades originate solely from human convention and ingenuity.
Correction: The author argues that a first language must be revealed because convention requires a prior shared language; similarly, many trades and sciences require knowledge that cannot be derived from observation or logic alone, indicating divine origin.

Miracles as Proof of Prophethood and Their Transmission via Tawatur
The author enumerates miracles as proof of prophethood and argues that tawātur transmission yields necessary knowledge.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that miracles (mu'jizat) serve as the primary evidence for prophethood and that knowledge of these miracles is reliably transmitted through tawātur (concurrent testimony), producing necessary certainty.

Core Idea
Miracles breaking natural laws are the ultimate proof of prophethood, and tawātur ensures their certainty for all times.

This passage from Imam al-Nasafi's Tabṣirat al-Adilla establishes the foundational proof of prophethood: miracles that break the usual course of nature. The author provides examples from various prophets and then explains how the knowledge of these miracles reaches later generations—not through weak chains but through massive, concurrent testimony (tawātur) that leaves no room for doubt or collusion.

Guided Path
1
Identify the main claim
Read the opening sentence which states that miracles are the evidence for prophethood. Notice that the author immediately lists examples from different prophets.
The list includes miracles of Prophet Muhammad ﷺ as well.
2
Examine the examples
Go through each miracle mentioned. Reflect on how each breaks a natural custom and supports a prophet's claim.
3
Understand the transmission method
The author distinguishes between direct observation for contemporaries and the mutawātir report for later generations. Focus on the conditions: impossibility of collusion due to diversity of narrators.
This is a key epistemological argument.
4
Reflect on the conclusion
The passage ends with the impossibility of collusion. Ask yourself: why does this secure certainty? The commentary will elaborate.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المعجزات دليل لثبوت الرسالة ثم الدليل على ثبوت الرسالة لبعض الرسل على التعيين ظهور المعجزات الناقضات للعادات على أيدي كثير منهم كخروج الناقة من الصخر، وصيرورة النار بردًا وسلامًا على إبراهيم، وقلب العصا حية، وتسخير الريح والجن والشياطين وتسبيح الجبال، وإلانة الحديد، وإحياء الموتى، وحنين الأسطوانة وشكاية الناقة، وكلام الجمل المسموم ، ونبع الماء من بين الأصابع وغير ذلك مما هي أدلة صدق إدعاء هم الرسالة على ما بينا من كيفية وجه الدلالة. ثم ثبوت ذلك لأهل زمانهم بالمشاهدة ولمن بعدهم بالخبر المتواتر الذي يوجب العلم الضروري، كما أثبت ذلك بالبلدان النائية والأمم الخالية، ولا مجال للتهمة فيه لا بالفسق ولا بالانتفاع لامتناع إجماع الناس الذين لا يتصور تواطؤهم على الكذب على خبر واحد هو في نفسه كذب، لاستحالة اجتماع دواعي الكذب أناس مختلفين جبلوا على أهواء مختلفة، وآراء مشتتة، وهمم متفرقة، وطبائع
[The section heading: Miracles are evidence for the establishment of prophethood] Then the evidence for the establishment of prophethood for some messengers specifically is the appearance of miracles that break customs at the hands of many of them, such as the emergence of the she-camel from the rock, the turning of fire into coolness and safety for Abraham, the turning of the staff into a serpent, the subjugation of the wind, jinn, and devils and the glorification of the mountains, the softening of iron, the reviving of the dead, the moaning of the pillar and the complaint of the camel, the speech of the poisoned camel, the gushing of water from between the fingers, and other things which are proofs of the truth of their claim to prophethood, according to what we have explained concerning the manner of the indication. Then the establishment of that for the people of their time is by direct observation, and for those after them by the mutawātir report that yields necessary knowledge, just as that is established for distant lands and past nations. And there is no room for suspicion in it, neither by immorality nor by self-interest, because of the impossibility of the consensus of people whose collusion on a lie cannot be imagined, concerning a single report that is itself a lie, due to the impossibility of the coming together of motives for lying among diverse people who are created with different inclinations, dispersed opinions, scattered ambitions, and varied temperaments.
Source pages p. 702

Commentary
This passage provides the proof of prophethood through miracles and explains the epistemological transmission of that proof. The author begins by stating that miracles (mu'jizat) that break natural customs are the evidence for the specific appointment of prophets. He lists several examples: the she-camel from the rock (Prophet Salih), the cooling of fire (Abraham), the staff becoming a serpent (Moses), the subjugation of wind and jinn (Solomon), the softening of iron and reviving the dead (David and Jesus), and various miracles of Prophet Muhammad ﷺ like the moaning pillar, the complaining camel, the speaking poisoned camel, and water gushing from fingers. These are proofs of their truthfulness. Then he explains how knowledge of these miracles is established: for contemporaries, through direct observation; for later generations, through mutawātir (concurrent) reports that produce necessary (ḍarūrī) knowledge. Tawātur is a transmission by such a large group that it is impossible for them to collude on a lie, and the report itself is free from any suspicion of falsehood because the reporters are numerous, diverse in temperaments and motives, making agreement on a lie impossible. This argument secures the certainty of prophetic miracles for those who did not witness them.

Key Terms
معجزات
رسالة
تواتر
علم ضروري
ناقض للعادة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Historical reports of miracles can be doubted like any other report.
Correction: The author argues that tawātur transmits them with such certainty that no doubt can enter, because collusion is impossible.

Checkpoint
What condition does the author give for a report to be accepted as mutawātir and thus yield necessary knowledge?
A) It must be narrated by at least five trustworthy people.
B) It must be from a prophet.
C) It must be impossible for the narrators to have colluded on a lie due to their diversity and large numbers.
D) It must be recorded in a scripture.

Key Takeaway
Miracles that break natural customs are the definitive proof of a prophet's truthfulness, and the tawātur transmission ensures that this knowledge remains certain for all later generations.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you personally accept the miracles of the prophets as certain historical facts, or is there a shadow of doubt? If you doubt, what does that say about your reliance on the tawātur transmission that the author argues makes collusion impossible? Can you honestly point to a reason to reject them, or is your hesitation rooted in modern skepticism rather than evidence?
?
The author claims that diverse people with different inclinations cannot come together to fabricate a lie. Look at your own life: have you dismissed a truth because you disliked the person who conveyed it? How does this lesson expose your own prejudices and call you to accept truth regardless of its source?
?
If the certainty of prophethood rests on miracles transmitted through tawātur, then your belief in Prophet Muhammad ﷺ is built on the testimony of thousands. Does your daily conduct reflect that same certainty—do you pray, give charity, and avoid sin as if you truly believe that a Prophet was sent to you? Or do you act as if it's just a story? What would change if you lived with the same conviction as those who witnessed the miracles firsthand?

The Divine Origin of Sciences Beyond Human Capacity
Argument for divine origin of certain sciences.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the existence of certain sciences that cannot be acquired through senses or intellect serves as evidence for divine revelation.

Core Idea
Some knowledge can only come from God — that proves prophethood.

The author begins by listing several fields of knowledge — from procreation to warfare — that human beings could not have discovered on their own. Their very existence points to a divine teacher who communicates through revelation. This sets the foundation for the use of miracles as proof.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing it, then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through.
2
Identify the listed sciences
Notice the different types of knowledge mentioned: procreation, child rearing, animal nourishment, sorcery, alchemy, warfare.
These are diverse fields.
3
Understand the argument logic
The author argues that because these sciences cannot be attained by the senses or intellect alone, their existence must be due to divine teaching (tawqeef).
This is the core logical move.
4
Connect to prophethood
This argument establishes the necessity of revelation, preparing for the discussion of miracles as proof for specific prophets.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وكذا العلم بوجوه أسباب التناسل، والعلم بكيفية تربية الصغار والعلم بتدابير أغذية ما ليس له نطق. وكذا العلم بالسحر وتغيير جواهر الأشياء بأنواع المعالجات. وعلوم محاربة الأعداء. فكان ثبوت العلم بهذه الأشياء مع استنساخ حصول ذلك بشيء من الحواس أو العقل، دليلاً أن العلم بها كلها توقيف من عند العليم الخبير الذي لا يعزب عنه شيء ولا يخفى عليه خافية، وذلك يكون بالوحي إلى من اصطفاه لرسالته والله الموفق. المعجزات دليل لثبوت الرسالة ثم الدليل على ثبوت الرسالة لبعض الرسل على التعيين ظهور المعجزات الناقضات للعادات على أيدي كثير منهم كخروج الناقة من الصخر، وصيرورة النار بردًا وسلامًا على إبراهيم، وقلب العصا حية، وتسخير الريح والجن والشياطين وتسبيح الجبال، وإلانة الحديد، وإحياء الموتى، وحنين الأسطوانة وشكاية الناقة، وكلام الجمل المسموم، ونبع الماء من بين الأصابع وغير ذلك مما هي أدلة صدق إدعائهم الرسالة على ما بينا من كيفية وجه الدلالة. ثم ثبوت ذلك لأهل زمانهم بالمشاهدة ولمن بعدهم بالخبر المتواتر الذي يوجب العلم الضروري، كما أثبت ذلك بالبلدان النائية والأمم الخالية، ولا مجال للتهمة فيه لا بالفسق ولا بالانتفاع لامتناع إجماع الناس الذين لا يتصور تواطؤهم على الكذب على خبر واحد هو في نفسه كذب، لاستحالة اجتماع دواعي الكذب أناس مختلفين جبلوا على أهواء مختلفة، وآراء مشتتة، وهمم متفرقة، وطبائع متباينة، ولهذا قال طفيل الغنوي وهو يذكر موت رجل من قومه: وجاء من الأخبار ما لا يكذب تأويني هم من الليل منصب تظاهرن حتى لم تكن لي ريبة ولم يك غما أخبروا متعقب ألا نراه قال وجاء من الأخبار ما لا يكذب ثم نبه عن العلة فقال: تظاهرن حتى لم تكن لي ريبة ولم يك عما أخبروا متعقب وقال سويد بن صبغي من الأخبار عين جلية ترادفن حتى ما لقلبك صارف وهذا ظاهر، وقد أقمنا الدلالة في أول الكتاب على كون الخبر المتواتر موجبا للعلم الضروري جاعلاً المخبر عنه كالمنظور إليه للسامع، فلا نشتغل بإعادة ذلك، والله الموفق.
Likewise, knowledge of the aspects of procreation, and knowledge of the method of raising young, and knowledge of the management of the nourishment of those without speech. Likewise, knowledge of sorcery and changing the essences of things by various treatments. And the sciences of warfare against enemies. So the establishment of knowledge of these things, despite the impossibility of obtaining that by any of the senses or intellect, is evidence that knowledge of all of them is a divine teaching from the All-Knowing, the All-Aware, from whom nothing is hidden nor any secret concealed, and that is by revelation to the one He has chosen for His message. And God is the Guide. Miracles are evidence for the establishment of prophethood. Then the evidence for the establishment of prophethood for some messengers in particular is the appearance of miracles that break customs at the hands of many of them, such as the emergence of the she-camel from the rock, the becoming of fire as cool and safe for Abraham, the turning of the staff into a serpent, the subjugation of the wind and the jinn and the devils, the glorification of the mountains, the softening of iron, the reviving of the dead, the groaning of the pillar and the complaint of the she-camel, the speech of the poisoned camel, the gushing of water from between the fingers, and other things that are proofs of the truthfulness of their claim to prophethood, according to what we have explained regarding the manner of the indication. Then its establishment for the people of their time is by direct observation, and for those after them by the mutawatir report which necessitates necessary knowledge, just as that is established for distant lands and past nations. There is no room for suspicion in it, neither due to sin nor due to self-interest, because of the impossibility of the consensus of people whose collusion on falsehood cannot be conceived regarding a single report that is inherently false, due to the impossibility of the coming together of motives for falsehood among diverse people who are naturally disposed to different inclinations, scattered opinions, divergent ambitions, and varying temperaments. Hence Tufayl al-Ghanawi said, mentioning the death of a man from his people: 'And there came from the news what does not lie / it sheltered me from the night's distress / they were successive until I had no doubt / and no grief over what they reported was followed up' – do you not see that he said 'And there came from the news what does not lie' then he pointed out the reason and said: 'they were successive until I had no doubt' and 'no grief over what they reported was followed up'? And Suwayd ibn Sab'i said: 'From the news came a clear eye / successive until your heart has no diversion.' This is evident. And we have established the proof at the beginning of the book that the mutawatir report necessitates necessary knowledge, making the reported thing like that which is seen by the listener, so we will not busy ourselves with repeating that. And God is the Guide.
Source pages p. 702

Commentary
This passage is a combined proof for the divine origin of certain sciences and for the establishment of prophethood through miracles transmitted via tawatur. The author first lists several branches of knowledge—such as the sciences of procreation, child rearing, animal husbandry, sorcery, alchemy, and warfare—that human beings could not have acquired through sensory perception or rational inference alone. The very fact that such knowledge exists, despite the inability of the senses or intellect to produce it, demonstrates that it must be a divine bestowal (tawqeef) from God, communicated through revelation to His chosen messengers. This sets the stage for the main topic: miracles as evidence for specific prophetic claims. The author defines miracles as events that break customary patterns (nawaqid li'l-‘adat). He cites well-known examples from various prophets: the she-camel from rock (Prophet Salih), the fire becoming cool (Prophet Ibrahim), the staff turning into a serpent (Prophet Musa), the subjugation of wind, jinn, and devils (Prophet Sulayman), the glorification of mountains and softening of iron (Prophet Dawud), reviving the dead (Prophet Isa), and several from Prophet Muhammad (the groaning pillar, the complaint of the camel, the speech of the poisoned camel, and water gushing from fingers). These miracles serve as proof of the truthfulness of their claimants because they are beyond human capacity and confirm the divine message. The author then explains how these miracles are known to later generations: those who witnessed them directly had certain knowledge through observation, while later people rely on the mutawatir report—a report transmitted by such a large number of trustworthy narrators that collusion on falsehood is impossible. This type of report yields necessary knowledge (al-‘ilm al-daruri), rendering the reported event as certain as if the listener had seen it himself. The author argues that there is no possibility of intentional falsification because the narrators are too numerous and diverse in their inclinations, opinions, ambitions, and temperaments to agree on a lie. He supports this with two lines of Arabic poetry: the first by Tufayl al-Ghanawi, who describes news that is reliable because it comes from multiple independent sources, and the second by Suwayd ibn Sab‘i, who likewise emphasizes the cumulative certainty of repeated reports. Finally, the author refers to his earlier discussion in the book where he established that the mutawatir report produces necessary knowledge, and he declines to repeat that argument. The passage concludes with a prayer for divine guidance.

Key Terms
مُعجِزات (miracles)
العادة (custom, habitual course)
التواتر (concurrent testimony)
العلم الضروري (necessary knowledge)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: All human knowledge originates from sensory experience or rational deduction alone.
Correction: The author argues that certain types of knowledge (e.g., sorcery, warfare) cannot be explained by senses or intellect, pointing to a divine source.

Checkpoint
According to the author, why do the various sciences listed (procreation, warfare, etc.) serve as evidence for divine revelation?
A) They are all based on sensory experience.
B) They are derived from rational deduction alone.
C) They cannot be attained by senses or intellect, so their existence points to a divine source.
D) They are all mentioned in the Quran.

Key Takeaway
The existence of certain sciences that humans cannot discover on their own proves that God teaches through revelation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Can you honestly point to an area in your life where you have trusted human reason over divine revelation, and what has that cost you?
?
Think of a specific piece of knowledge you rely on daily—does it ultimately come from revelation? If not, how does that affect your reliance on God?
?
If you truly believed that every beneficial science is a gift from God through revelation, how would your attitude toward learning and gratitude change starting today?

Miracles as Proof of Prophethood
Definition and examples of miracles as evidence for prophethood.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how miracles that break the customary course of nature serve as evidence for the truthfulness of a prophet.

Core Idea
Miracles break custom — that is what makes them signs of divine support.

The author now turns to the main evidence for specific prophetic claims: miracles. He defines them as events that break the normal, habitual patterns of nature. He then lists a series of miracles from various prophets, showing that such extraordinary events confirm the messenger's truthfulness.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice the definition of miracles.
2
Understand the definition
The author calls miracles 'الناقضات للعادات' – events that break customs. This is the key concept.
Custom (al-‘adah) means the regular pattern of nature.
3
Examine the examples
Go through each miracle listed: from Salih, Ibrahim, Musa, Sulayman, Dawud, Isa, and Muhammad.
Each miracle is associated with a specific prophet.
4
Grasp the argumentative role
These miracles are proofs of the truthfulness of the claim to prophethood. They are beyond human capacity and confirm the divine message.
The author refers to an earlier explanation of how miracles indicate truth.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وكذا العلم بوجوه أسباب التناسل، والعلم بكيفية تربية الصغار والعلم بتدابير أغذية ما ليس له نطق. وكذا العلم بالسحر وتغيير جواهر الأشياء بأنواع المعالجات. وعلوم محاربة الأعداء. فكان ثبوت العلم بهذه الأشياء مع استنساخ حصول ذلك بشيء من الحواس أو العقل، دليلاً أن العلم بها كلها توقيف من عند العليم الخبير الذي لا يعزب عنه شيء ولا يخفى عليه خافية، وذلك يكون بالوحي إلى من اصطفاه لرسالته والله الموفق. المعجزات دليل لثبوت الرسالة ثم الدليل على ثبوت الرسالة لبعض الرسل على التعيين ظهور المعجزات الناقضات للعادات على أيدي كثير منهم كخروج الناقة من الصخر، وصيرورة النار بردًا وسلامًا على إبراهيم، وقلب العصا حية، وتسخير الريح والجن والشياطين وتسبيح الجبال، وإلانة الحديد، وإحياء الموتى، وحنين الأسطوانة وشكاية الناقة، وكلام الجمل المسموم، ونبع الماء من بين الأصابع وغير ذلك مما هي أدلة صدق إدعائهم الرسالة على ما بينا من كيفية وجه الدلالة. ثم ثبوت ذلك لأهل زمانهم بالمشاهدة ولمن بعدهم بالخبر المتواتر الذي يوجب العلم الضروري، كما أثبت ذلك بالبلدان النائية والأمم الخالية، ولا مجال للتهمة فيه لا بالفسق ولا بالانتفاع لامتناع إجماع الناس الذين لا يتصور تواطؤهم على الكذب على خبر واحد هو في نفسه كذب، لاستحالة اجتماع دواعي الكذب أناس مختلفين جبلوا على أهواء مختلفة، وآراء مشتتة، وهمم متفرقة، وطبائع متباينة، ولهذا قال طفيل الغنوي وهو يذكر موت رجل من قومه: وجاء من الأخبار ما لا يكذب تأويني هم من الليل منصب تظاهرن حتى لم تكن لي ريبة ولم يك غما أخبروا متعقب ألا نراه قال وجاء من الأخبار ما لا يكذب ثم نبه عن العلة فقال: تظاهرن حتى لم تكن لي ريبة ولم يك عما أخبروا متعقب وقال سويد بن صبغي من الأخبار عين جلية ترادفن حتى ما لقلبك صارف وهذا ظاهر، وقد أقمنا الدلالة في أول الكتاب على كون الخبر المتواتر موجبا للعلم الضروري جاعلاً المخبر عنه كالمنظور إليه للسامع، فلا نشتغل بإعادة ذلك، والله الموفق.
Likewise, knowledge of the aspects of procreation, and knowledge of the method of raising young, and knowledge of the management of the nourishment of those without speech. Likewise, knowledge of sorcery and changing the essences of things by various treatments. And the sciences of warfare against enemies. So the establishment of knowledge of these things, despite the impossibility of obtaining that by any of the senses or intellect, is evidence that knowledge of all of them is a divine teaching from the All-Knowing, the All-Aware, from whom nothing is hidden nor any secret concealed, and that is by revelation to the one He has chosen for His message. And God is the Guide. Miracles are evidence for the establishment of prophethood. Then the evidence for the establishment of prophethood for some messengers in particular is the appearance of miracles that break customs at the hands of many of them, such as the emergence of the she-camel from the rock, the becoming of fire as cool and safe for Abraham, the turning of the staff into a serpent, the subjugation of the wind and the jinn and the devils, the glorification of the mountains, the softening of iron, the reviving of the dead, the groaning of the pillar and the complaint of the she-camel, the speech of the poisoned camel, the gushing of water from between the fingers, and other things that are proofs of the truthfulness of their claim to prophethood, according to what we have explained regarding the manner of the indication. Then its establishment for the people of their time is by direct observation, and for those after them by the mutawatir report which necessitates necessary knowledge, just as that is established for distant lands and past nations. There is no room for suspicion in it, neither due to sin nor due to self-interest, because of the impossibility of the consensus of people whose collusion on falsehood cannot be conceived regarding a single report that is inherently false, due to the impossibility of the coming together of motives for falsehood among diverse people who are naturally disposed to different inclinations, scattered opinions, divergent ambitions, and varying temperaments. Hence Tufayl al-Ghanawi said, mentioning the death of a man from his people: 'And there came from the news what does not lie / it sheltered me from the night's distress / they were successive until I had no doubt / and no grief over what they reported was followed up' – do you not see that he said 'And there came from the news what does not lie' then he pointed out the reason and said: 'they were successive until I had no doubt' and 'no grief over what they reported was followed up'? And Suwayd ibn Sab'i said: 'From the news came a clear eye / successive until your heart has no diversion.' This is evident. And we have established the proof at the beginning of the book that the mutawatir report necessitates necessary knowledge, making the reported thing like that which is seen by the listener, so we will not busy ourselves with repeating that. And God is the Guide.

Commentary
This passage is a combined proof for the divine origin of certain sciences and for the establishment of prophethood through miracles transmitted via tawatur. The author first lists several branches of knowledge—such as the sciences of procreation, child rearing, animal husbandry, sorcery, alchemy, and warfare—that human beings could not have acquired through sensory perception or rational inference alone. This sets the stage for the main topic: miracles as evidence for specific prophetic claims. The author defines miracles as events that break customary patterns (nawaqid li'l-‘adat). He cites well-known examples from various prophets: the she-camel from rock (Prophet Salih), the fire becoming cool (Prophet Ibrahim), the staff turning into a serpent (Prophet Musa), the subjugation of wind, jinn, and devils (Prophet Sulayman), the glorification of mountains and softening of iron (Prophet Dawud), reviving the dead (Prophet Isa), and several from Prophet Muhammad (the groaning pillar, the complaint of the camel, the speech of the poisoned camel, and water gushing from fingers). These miracles serve as proof of the truthfulness of their claimants because they are beyond human capacity and confirm the divine message. The author then explains how these miracles are known to later generations: those who witnessed them directly had certain knowledge through observation, while later people rely on the mutawatir report—a report transmitted by such a large number of trustworthy narrators that collusion on falsehood is impossible. This type of report yields necessary knowledge (al-‘ilm al-daruri), rendering the reported event as certain as if the listener had seen it himself. The author argues that there is no possibility of intentional falsification because the narrators are too numerous and diverse in their inclinations, opinions, ambitions, and temperaments to agree on a lie. He supports this with two lines of Arabic poetry: the first by Tufayl al-Ghanawi, who describes news that is reliable because it comes from multiple independent sources, and the second by Suwayd ibn Sab‘i, who likewise emphasizes the cumulative certainty of repeated reports. Finally, the author refers to his earlier discussion in the book where he established that the mutawatir report produces necessary knowledge, and he declines to repeat that argument. The passage concludes with a prayer for divine guidance.

Tawatur: The Certain Transmission of Miracles
Argument for tawatur as the means of transmitting miracle reports.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the mutawatir report ensures that miracles are reliably transmitted to later generations, providing certainty equal to direct observation.

Core Idea
Tawatur makes miracles as certain as if you saw them yourself.

Having established that miracles prove prophethood for those who witnessed them, the author now addresses how later generations can be certain. He explains that these reports are transmitted via tawatur — a mass of narrators that cannot possibly have colluded on a lie. This yields necessary knowledge, just like seeing the event firsthand.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic and its translation. Note the two ways of knowing miracles: direct observation and tawatur.
2
Understand the argument for tawatur
The author argues that a mutawatir report yields necessary knowledge, with no possibility of collusion due to the diversity of narrators.
This is a standard argument in Islamic epistemology.
3
Examine the poetic evidence
Two poets are quoted to illustrate the certainty that comes from multiple independent reports.
The poetry reinforces the logical argument.
4
Note the reference to previous discussion
The author reminds that the proof that tawatur produces necessary knowledge was already established earlier in the book.
This shows the systematic nature of the work.

According to the passage, what makes it impossible for narrators to collude on a false report?
A) They are all truthful individuals.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You have just read that the mutawatir report makes the reported miracle as certain as if you saw it yourself. Do you actually live with that certainty? When you recall the splitting of the moon or the water flowing from the Prophet's ﷺ fingers, do you feel the same conviction as if you had witnessed them? What would change in your life if you truly internalized that these events are as real as anything you have seen with your own eyes? Commit to reciting one of these miracle narrations with full presence of heart today, asking Allah to grant you certainty.
?
The author argues that the diversity of transmitters – different inclinations, opinions, ambitions, and temperaments – makes collusion impossible. Yet, your own soul may still entertain doubts about some reports. Where do these doubts truly stem from? Is it from a lack of faith in the preservation of the Sunnah, or from a desire to avoid the implications of those miracles? Confront your doubt directly: choose one miracle you have questioned, research its multiple chains, and ask yourself whether the doubt is rational or from your own whims.
?
If tawatur gives you the same certainty about past miracles as direct sight, then the same tawatur conveys the promise of the Hereafter. Are you living with that same certainty about Paradise and Hell? When you sin, do you act as though you are absolutely certain of the punishment? If not, what is the barrier in your heart? Today, take one concrete action – whether in prayer, charity, or avoiding a sin – that reflects the certainty that the Hereafter is as real as the world you see.

Refutation of the Doubt on the Possibility of Miracles
Refutation of a doubt against miracles via mass witness.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the structure of a classical doubt against miracles and how Maturidi theologians refute it by appealing to mass testimony.

Core Idea
Miracles are proven by direct witness, not by philosophical debates about nature.

In this passage, Imam al-Nasafi presents a doubt raised by those who deny prophethood: either miracles follow nature (so no proof) or violate it (impossible), hence no evidence. He then offers a sharp refutation, dismissing the argument as feeble and pointing to the undeniable testimony of multitudes who witnessed the miracles firsthand.

Guided Path
1
Read the doubt carefully
Read the Arabic passage and translation, focusing on the dilemma presented: if a miracle follows nature, it is not evidence; if it violates nature, it is impossible. Understand the logical trap.
The doubt tries to eliminate any possibility of evidence for prophethood.
2
Note the author's dismissal
Observe the strong language: the author calls the argument 'feeble' (wah) and says even a madman would be ridiculed for uttering it. This shows the author's confidence.
This is a rhetorical move to undermine the opponent's credibility.
3
Grasp the refutation
The author refutes by citing direct observation (mu'aayana) by a large multitude. He argues that such widespread testimony overrides any abstract doubt about the fixity of natures.
The refutation relies on empirical certainty from consensus of witnesses.
4
Consider the incomplete ending
The text cuts off at 'bila'. Reflect on what the author might have said next, given the context of mass testimony.
The full argument likely continued to elaborate on the value of tawatur (mass transmission).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فأما شبهة من زعم أن لا ثبوت للرسالة إلا بالدليل ولا ثبوت للدليل، فإنه لو كان خارجًا على ما عليه العادة ومجرى الطبيعة فلا دليل فيه، وإن خرج عن العادة ومجرى الطبيعة فهو محال إذ لا تغير للطبائع. فكلام واه لو تفوه به مجنون لتعجب منه، وذلك لما مر أن كل ذلك معاينه من لا يجوز خفاء أمره عليهم لكثرتهم، فكان ما أنكروه من الخروج عن الطبيعة بلا
As for the doubt of one who claims that there is no establishment of prophethood except through evidence, and there is no evidence, because if the miracle occurs in accordance with custom and the natural course, then there is no evidence in it; but if it deviates from custom and the natural course, then it is impossible, since natures do not change. [The author says:] This is a feeble statement; if a madman uttered it, people would be amazed at it. And that is because, as has passed, all of that was witnessed by those whose state could not be hidden from them due to their multitude. So what they denied—the departure from nature—[the refutation continues]...
Source pages p. 703

Commentary
This passage presents a doubt (shubha) raised by opponents of prophethood, followed by a brief refutation. The doubt is constructed as a dilemma: either the alleged miracle occurs according to the normal course of nature and custom, in which case it is not actually a miracle and provides no evidence; or it violates the normal course, but such violation is impossible because natural laws are fixed and unchangeable. Therefore, no valid evidence for prophethood exists. The author dismisses this argument as extremely weak ('kalam wah')—so weak that even a madman would be ridiculed for uttering it. The reason for its weakness, he explains, is that these events were directly witnessed ('mu‘ayana') by large groups of people whose testimony cannot be ignored. The multitude of witnesses precludes any doubt about the occurrence of the violation of nature. The argument here is cut off, but the author was likely about to elaborate that the consensus of witnesses proves the reality of the miracle, regardless of philosophical objections about the fixity of natures. The refutation relies on the principle that widespread direct observation provides certainty that overrides a priori objections about natural laws.

Key Terms
شُبهة
طبيعة
عادات
معاينة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that the doubt requires a detailed philosophical response about the nature of causality and the possibility of change in natural laws.
Correction: The author refutes it not by engaging with the philosophy of nature, but by appealing to empirical certainty from mass testimony, which overrides theoretical objections.

Checkpoint
What is the core of the doubt that the author refutes?
A) Prophethood is impossible because prophets never existed.
B) Either a miracle is natural (no proof) or unnatural (impossible), so no proof.
C) The reports of miracles are not trustworthy.
D) Prophethood is only for past generations.

Key Takeaway
Miracles are proven by the direct, mass witness of reliable witnesses, not by theoretical arguments about the fixity of natural laws.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you encounter a claim that seems impossible from a scientific perspective, do you instinctively reject it, or do you consider the possibility that reliable testimony might override your assumptions? What does your reaction reveal about your trust in Allah's power versus your trust in your own understanding?
?
This lesson says a weak argument is dismissed 'as if uttered by a madman.' Are there beliefs you hold that, if examined honestly, rest on similar shaky reasoning? What would it cost you to admit that?
?
The certainty of mass witness is enough to overthrow a theoretical doubt. Is your faith based on inherited assumptions or on the solid testimony of the prophets and their companions that has reached you through tawatur? What steps will you take to move from passive acceptance to active certainty?

Refutation of the Doubt That Miracles Are Impossible
The author refutes the claim that miracles are impossible because nature cannot change.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the author refutes the doubt that miracles are impossible by appealing to sensory knowledge and God's omnipotence.

Core Idea
Miracles are known by necessary sensory knowledge, not fallible reason.

In this passage, the author addresses a key doubt against prophethood: miracles either follow nature (thus not proof) or break nature (impossible because natures do not change). He refutes this by arguing that miracles are witnessed by many, providing sensory necessary knowledge, and that denying God's power to change nature is tantamount to attributing incapability to Him.

Guided Path
1
Understand the doubt presented
Read the opening doubt carefully: the denial of miracles based on the impossibility of nature changing.
2
Analyze the first refutation
Notice how the author contrasts sensory necessary knowledge (from witnessing) with discursive rational knowledge, showing that sensory knowledge takes precedence.
3
Examine the theological argument
See how the author argues from the agreed premise of God's omnipotence to show that denying miracles limits His power.
4
Synthesize the refutation
Understand how the combination of epistemological and theological arguments refutes the doubt.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فأما شبهة من زعم أن لا ثبوت للرسالة إلا بالدليل ولا ثبوت للدليل، فإنه لو كان خارجًا على ما عليه العادة ومجرى الطبيعة فلا دليل فيه، وإن خرج عن العادة ومجرى الطبيعة فهو محال إذ لا تغير للطبائع. فكلام واه لو تفوه به مجنون لتعجب منه، وذلك لما مر أن كل ذلك معاينه من لا يجوز خفاء أمره عليهم لكثرتهم، فكان ما أنكروه من الخروج عن الطبيعة بلا حجة شبهة اعتمدوا عليها ثابتا بالحس الذي هو أوضح طريق العلم وأعلى سبل المعرفة فكان إنكارهم مردودا ، وجواز انقلاب الطبيعة ثابتا. يحققه أنهم لو اعتمدوا في ذلك على دليل يتراءى أنه معقول ولا يهتدي بالعقل إلى كيفية رده كان ذلك مردودًا لما أن الدليل العقلي يوجب العلم الاستدلالي والخطأ على الاستدلالي جائز ممكن، وما أنكروه ثابت بالحس الموجب للعلم الضروري الذي لا يجوز عليه الخطأ والغلط، ولابد من رد أحدهما ورد ما يجوز عليه الخطأ والغلط أولى من رد ما لا يجوز عليه ذلك. يحققه أن معرفة ثبوت ما أنكروه ثابت بالحس فكان بطلان دليلهم بالحس، وكل دليل عرف بطلانه ضرورة كان باطلاً أو كان شبهة لا دليلاً فكيف وهم لم يبنوا إنكارهم على شبهة. معلومًا ثم نقول لهم : أنكم ساعدتمونا على أن جميع ما وجد في العالم مخلوق الله تعالى عرضا كان ذلك أو جوهرًا، وأنه تعالى موصوف بالقدرة على ما أراد إيجاده م إن النار جسم خلقه الله تعالى وخلق فيه الحرارة واليبوسة، فمن زعم أنه لا يقدر على أن يخلق هو بدل الحرارة فيها البرودة وبدل اليبوسة الرطوبة، فقد وصف الله تعالى بالعجز، وجعل أفعاله ضرورية لا اختيارية، إذ المختار والفعل كان سبيل من فعل ضد ما فعله إذ هو بذلك يمتاز عن المضطر، ووصف الله تعالى بالعجز والاضطرار جهل فاحش وكذا الله تعالى لما كان قادرًا على اختراع العالم لا عن أصل، لماذا لا يوصف بالقدرة على إخراج الناقة من الحجر، وإخراج الماء من بين
As for the doubt of one who claims that there is no establishment of prophethood except through proof, and no establishment of the proof, for if it were occurring in accordance with habit and the course of nature, then there is no proof in it, and if it departs from habit and the course of nature, it is impossible because natures do not change. This is weak speech that even a madman would be astonished at if he uttered it. That is because, as has passed, all of that is witnessed by those whose state cannot be hidden due to their multitude, so what they denied—the departure from nature—is established without a proof that they relied on, but is established by sensory perception, which is the clearest path of knowledge and the highest means of cognition. Thus their denial is rejected, and the possibility of the transformation of nature is established. This is verified: if they relied in that on an argument that appears to be rational and the intellect cannot find a way to refute it, that would be rejected because rational argument necessitates discursive knowledge (al-ʿilm al-istidlālī), and error in discursive knowledge is possible and permissible. What they denied is established by sensory perception, which necessitates necessary knowledge (al-ʿilm al-ḍarūrī) upon which error and mistake are not allowed. It is necessary to reject one of them, and rejecting that which error and mistake are possible upon is more appropriate than rejecting that which is not subject to that. This is verified because the knowledge of the establishment of what they denied is established by sensory perception, so their proof is invalidated by sensory perception. Every proof whose invalidity is known necessarily is either invalid or a doubt, not a proof. How [can it be] when they did not base their denial on a doubt? Then we say to them: You have agreed with us that everything that exists in the world is created by Allah, whether it is an accident or a substance, and that He is described with power over what He wills to bring into existence. Indeed, fire is a body that Allah created and created in it heat and dryness. Whoever claims that He is not able to create cold instead of heat and moisture instead of dryness has described Allah with incapability and made His actions necessary not voluntary, for the one who acts and does something has the way of doing the opposite of what he does, because thereby he is distinguished from the compelled. Describing Allah with incapability and compulsion is gross ignorance. Likewise, since Allah is powerful over inventing the world without an origin, why should He not be described with power to bring forth the she-camel from the rock and water from between [the rock]?
Source pages p. 703

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of a doubt raised by those who deny the possibility of miracles and thus prophethood. The doubt states that if a claimed miracle (e.g., a prophet's sign) occurs according to natural habits, it cannot serve as a proof; if it breaks the natural course, it is impossible because natures are immutable. The author dismisses this as worthless even from a madman. He argues that such miracles are witnessed by multitudes, so they are known by sensory perception (al-ḥiss), which is the clearest way of knowledge. The deniers rely on a rational argument that yields only discursive knowledge (istidlālī), which is fallible, whereas sensory knowledge is necessary (ḍarūrī) and infallible. Therefore, the sensory evidence takes precedence. Furthermore, the author points out that the deniers already agree that everything is created by Allah, who is omnipotent. If they deny that Allah can change the properties of fire, they are attributing incapability to Him. He concludes by analogy: if Allah can create the world from nothing, why can He not bring forth a camel from a rock or water from stone (referring to the miracles of Prophets Salih and Moses)? The argument shows that denying miracles implies limiting God's power, which is impermissible.

Key Terms
شبهة
علم استدلالي
علم ضروري
حس
انقلاب الطبيعة
قدرة الله

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Rational arguments about the impossibility of nature changing override any claim of miracles.
Correction: The author shows that sensory necessary knowledge (from widespread witness) is superior to fallible rational inference, so the denial is invalid.

Checkpoint
According to the author, why is the denial of miracles based on the immutability of nature rejected?
A) Because nature can change on its own
B) Because miracles are witnessed by many, giving necessary sensory knowledge
C) Because rational arguments are always invalid
D) Because the deniers are mad

Key Takeaway
Miracles are rationally possible because they are known through necessary sensory knowledge and because God's omnipotence is unlimited.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you rely more on your own reasoning or on the clear signs Allah has placed before you? When have you dismissed something as 'impossible' even though it was clearly from Allah?
?
If you truly believed that Allah can change any situation in your life, how would your daily worries and fears change? What would it look like to live with that certainty?
?
When you hear of a miracle—whether in the past or in your own life—do you find yourself looking for a 'natural explanation' rather than accepting it as a direct act of Allah? What does that reveal about your heart's trust in His power over your intellect?

Refutation of the Claim that Prophets Brought Impossibilities
Nasafi refutes a sect and categorizes prophetic teachings.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that prophetic teachings are not impossible but are grounded in pure reason and practical wisdom.

Core Idea
Prophets brought pure reason and wisdom, not impossibilities.

Imam Nasafi addresses a sect that falsely claims prophets brought impossible things. He asserts that their teachings are actually pure wisdom, truth, and sound ethics. This lesson explores his refutation and classification of prophetic messages, showing how they are both rationally necessary and practically beneficial.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing, then read the translation. Notice how Nasafi begins by rejecting a false claim and then positively describes what prophets actually brought.
The passage ends mid-sentence at the page break; this does not affect the core argument.
2
Identify the two main categories of teachings
The passage divides prophetic teachings into practical aspects (worship, gratitude, morals, politics, courtesy) and doctrinal aspects (required by pure reason). Find these in the text.
Practical aspects are listed with 'some of that... some of it...'
3
Reflect on the role of reason
Consider why Nasafi emphasizes that doctrinal matters are necessitated by pure reason (al-ʿaql al-ṣarīḥ). How does this refute the claim of impossibilities?
Think about the relationship between reason and revelation.

وما زعمت الفرقة الأخيرة: أن الرسل أتوا بما هو محال على ما حكينا، قول باطل ودعوى فاسدة، بل أتوا بما هو الحكمة المحضة والحق البين والصواب الخالص ولولا التأيد بالبرهان لكان تعاطي ما أتوا به ودعوا إليه حقا وصوابًا إذ بعض ذلك من باب التقرب إلى الصانع وأداء شكر ما أسدى إليهم، وبعضه من مكارم الأخلاق، وبعضه من السياسات الفاضلة التي لا قيام للعالم ولا سكون للدهماء إلا بها، وبعضه من باب المجاملة وحسن العشرة والمعاملة. فأما ما أتوا به من الأبواب الاعتقادية فمما يوجبه العقل الصريح، ولا يطلق على ما يضاده من الاعتقاد بل يشهد ببطلان كل ما وراءه من العقائد، وفساد ما يقابله من الآراء والديانات على ما نكشف عن حقيقة ذلك إذا انتهينا إلى إثبات نبوة نبينا محمد عليه السلام - إن شاء الله تعالى. إثبات رسالة سيدنا محمد ثم بعد قيام الدليل على صحة الرسالة وثبوتها فيما مضى من الجملة وتعين من قامت على يده المعجزات الناقضات للعادة كقلب العصا حية، وتفجير عيون
And what the last sect claimed – that the messengers brought what is impossible, according to what we have narrated – is a false statement and a corrupt claim. Rather, they brought pure wisdom, clear truth, and sound correctness. Without support by proof, undertaking what they brought and called to would be truth and correctness, since some of that is of the category of drawing near to the Creator and performing gratitude for what He has bestowed upon them, and some of it is of noble character, and some of it is of excellent policies without which the world would not be established nor the common people settle, and some of it is of the category of courteousness and good fellowship and dealing. As for what they brought concerning doctrinal matters (al-abwāb al-iʿtiqādiyya), it is among what pure reason (al-ʿaql al-ṣarīḥ) necessitates, and it does not validate opposing beliefs but rather testifies to the falsehood of all beliefs beyond it, and the corruption of opposing opinions and religions, according to what we will uncover of the reality of that when we reach the establishment of the prophethood of our Prophet Muhammad (peace be upon him) – God willing. Establishment of the message of our master Muhammad. Then, after the proof of the truth of the message (al-risāla) and its establishment in what has passed from the general, and the identification of those at whose hands the miracle signs (al-muʿjizāt al-nāqiḍāt li-l-ʿādah) occurred, such as the turning of the staff into a serpent, and the gushing of springs
Source pages p. 709

Commentary
This passage refutes a sect that claims the prophets brought impossible things. The author asserts that the prophets brought wisdom, truth, and ethics. The passage ends by transitioning to the proof of Muhammad's prophethood, stating that after establishing the general truth of prophethood and identifying miracle-workers, we turn to the specific proof of Muhammad.

Refutation of the False Claim and Prophetic Practical Teachings
Refutes the false claim and enumerates practical and ethical teachings.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that prophets brought wisdom, moral virtues, and social systems, not impossible things.

Core Idea
Prophets brought what is necessary for human well-being: wisdom, ethics, and social order.

Some skeptics claim that prophets brought impossible or irrational demands. The author refutes this by showing that prophetic teachings are deeply rational and beneficial. This lesson explores the practical and ethical dimensions of what prophets actually conveyed.
