Equality in Evidence: Miracles as Proof of Prophethood
Establishes the principle of equal evidence leading to equal conclusions and applies it to Moses and Jesus.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why miracles of different prophets are equally valid proofs of prophethood based on their shared supernatural nature, not their specific forms.

Core Idea
Miracles prove prophethood by their supernatural nature, not by their form.

This passage establishes a crucial logical principle: if two claims rest on the same type of evidence, they are equally proven. Imam al-Nasafi applies this to show that the miracles of Moses, Jesus, and Muhammad all serve as equal proofs of prophethood because they share the essential quality of breaking natural laws. As you read, notice how he moves from a general rule to specific examples, grounding the argument in primary knowledge that admits no doubt.

Guided Path
1
Grasp the logical principle
Read the opening sentence carefully. It states that equal evidence and cause lead to equal conclusion and effect. This is the foundation of the entire argument.
2
See how the principle applies to Moses and Jesus
The passage then applies this principle to Moses and Jesus, showing that their prophethood was established by miracles that break customs, witnessed directly or reliably transmitted.
3
Understand the primary cognition
The author asserts a self-evident truth: equality in evidence is based on the meaning that makes something evidence, not its outward form. This is key to the analogy.
4
Examine the examples and reasoning
Consider the listed miracles (staff, water from rock, raising dead, healing). Note that their evidential value comes from breaking customs and exceeding created power, not their specific shapes.
5
Reflect on the conclusion
The passage ends by affirming that miracles occur after the claim of prophethood and are not given to support falsehood. This completes the case for Muhammad by analogy.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
التدليل على ثبوت رسالة سيدنا محمد عليه الصلاة والسلام] وبعد الوقوف على هذه المقدمة نقول : لا شك أن من ساوى غيره في الدليل والعلة ساواه في المدلول والمعلول. ثم إن موسى عليه السلام ثبتت رسالته لقيام الدلالة على ثبوتها وهي المعجزات الناقضات للعادات على يديه عاينها من شهدها وبلغ من لم يشاهدها على ألسنة قوم لم يجز عليهم التواطؤ في العادات الجارية، فصار ذلك كالمعاين المشاهد لهم. وكذلك رسالة عيسى عليه السلام ثبتت أيضًا بهذا الطريق. ثم من المعارف الأولية التى لا يداخلها شك ولا يخالطها ريبة ولا شبهة، أن الاستواء في الأدلة يطلب من حيث المعنى الذي به صارت الأدلة أدلة له من حيث الصور التي لم تكن الأدلة أدلة لأجلها ، ثم قلب العصا حية وتفجير الماء من الصخرة الصماء وإحياء الموتى، وإبراء الأكمة والأبرص ، وغير ذلك مما كانت دلائل وحججًا لصحة الرسالة لا لصورها بل لخروجها عن العادات، وامتناع دخولها تحت القدرة المحدثة، واختصاصها بدخولها تحت قدرة الصانع الحكيم الذي لا يعجزه شيء، ولا يقيم الدلالة على صحة الفاسد وصدق الكاذب وثبوتها عقيب دعوى الرسالة.
[Proof of the establishment of the messengership of our master Muhammad, peace and blessings be upon him] And after understanding this premise, we say: There is no doubt that whoever equals another in the evidence and the cause is equal to him in the conclusion and the effect. Then indeed, the messengership of Moses, peace be upon him, was established due to the existence of evidence for its establishment, which are the miracles that break customs, witnessed by those who saw them and conveyed to those who did not witness them through the tongues of people upon whom collusion in the customary practices is impossible. So that became like being seen and witnessed by them. Likewise, the messengership of Jesus, peace be upon him, was also established through this way. Then it is among the primary cognitions that admit no doubt, no uncertainty, and no suspicion, that equality in evidences is sought in terms of the meaning by which the evidences became evidences for him, not in terms of the forms for which the evidences were not evidences. Then the turning of the staff into a serpent, the splitting of water from the solid rock, the giving of life to the dead, the healing of the blind and the leper, and other such things were proofs and arguments for the correctness of messengership — not because of their forms, but because of their breaking of customs, their impossibility of falling under the power of the created, and their being specific to falling under the power of the wise Maker whom nothing incapacitates. And He does not establish evidence for the correctness of the corrupt or the truthfulness of the liar, and their occurrence after the claim of messengership.
Source pages p. 717

Commentary
This passage is a proof for the prophethood of Muhammad by way of analogy with earlier prophets. It begins with a logical principle: if two things share the same evidence and cause, they share the same conclusion. Then it applies this to Moses and Jesus: their prophethood was established by miracles that break customs, witnessed directly or transmitted reliably. These miracles are evidence not because of their specific forms, but because they break customs and are beyond created power, indicating divine intervention. The passage then asserts that this is a primary knowledge (ma‘rifa awwaliyya) that cannot be doubted. The key point is that the evidential value lies in the meaning (al-ma‘na) of breaking customs, not in the particular forms (as-suwar). Therefore, any prophet who performs such miracles is equally proven. The passage ends by stating that miracles are not given to support falsehood or lies, and they occur after the claim of prophethood.

Key Terms
الدليل والعلة
المدلول والمعلول
المعجزات الناقضات للعادات
المعارف الأولية
الخروج عن العادات

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Miracles prove prophethood because of their specific forms (e.g., raising the dead is more impressive than turning a staff into a snake).
Correction: The passage emphasizes that evidential value is from the supernatural nature (breaking customs), not the form. All miracles that break customs are equally proof.

Checkpoint

Key Takeaway
Miracles of different prophets are equal proofs because their evidential value lies in breaking customs, not in their specific forms.

Is there a specific command you have been neglecting that you now feel more urgency to follow?
?
The author calls it a 'primary cognition' that equality in evidence leads to equality in conclusion. When you think about your certainty in Muhammad's prophethood, is it built on this rational foundation, or have you relied on emotional or cultural reasons? Are you willing to be honest with yourself about what truly convinces you, and if your evidence is weak, what will you do to strengthen it?

Application to Muhammad: Equality and Causes of Rejection
Applies equality principle to Muhammad and lists causes of rejection.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the equality principle applies to Prophet Muhammad and the three causes that lead people to reject his prophethood despite the evidence.

Core Idea
Rejecting Muhammad is not due to lack of evidence but to blind imitation, envy, or Satanic distraction.

This passage directly applies the earlier argument about the equality of prophets to Muhammad. It asserts that Muhammad is equal to all other prophets in the evidence of prophethood, so anyone who accepts other prophets must accept him. The author then identifies three reasons why some people reject him, none of which have to do with insufficient miracles. Finally, he announces that he will present Muhammad's miracles to prove his claim.

Guided Path
1
Understand the equality claim
Read the opening sentences where the author states that Muhammad equals other prophets in the evidence of prophethood. Notice that this implies his claim is equally valid and obligatory to accept.
The term 'خواص النبوة' refers to the specific properties of prophethood, primarily miracles.
2
Identify the three causes of rejection
The passage lists three reasons why someone might reject Muhammad after accepting other prophets: being turned away by Satan, blind imitation of ancestors, and transgression/envy leading to partisanship. Reflect on each cause.
These are psychological and social factors, not rational ones.
3
Recognize the transition
The passage ends by stating that to prove Muhammad's equality, one must present his signs (miracles). The author announces that he will begin doing so. This sets up the next section.
The word 'فنقول' indicates the start of the list of miracles.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم إن رسولنا المصطفى محمد ساوى غيره من الأنبياء فيما هو دلالة النبوة والرسالة وفيما هو من خواص النبوة، فيساويهم في صحة دعواه ووجوب قبول ما ادعى أنه من عند الله، وتصديقه في جميع ذلك، فمن أقر بنبوة غيره وأنكر نبوته وكذبه في دعواه فقد وقع في ذلك، إما لصد الشيطان إياه عن التأمل في آياته وإما لتمسكه بما ورثه من آبائه تقليدًا لهم، وإما لسلوكه سبيل البغي والحسد واشتغاله بالتعصب لجيل من الأجيال وأمة من الأمم عصمنا الله تعالى عن الوقوع في الضلالة لسلوك سبيل الجهالة. ثم لا وقوف على صحة ما ادعينا من مساواته غيره من الرسل إلا بعد إبانة آياته، وإثبات اختصاصه فيما هو من خواص النبوة، فنبدأ بالإبانة عن آياته فنقول :
Then indeed, our chosen Messenger Muhammad equaled other prophets in what is evidence of prophethood and messengership and in what is among the specific properties of prophethood. So he equals them in the correctness of his claim and the obligation to accept what he claimed to be from God, and to believe him in all of that. So whoever acknowledges the prophethood of another and denies his prophethood and calls him a liar in his claim has fallen into that, either due to Satan turning him away from reflecting on his signs, or due to his clinging to what he inherited from his fathers by way of blind imitation, or due to his following the path of transgression and envy and engaging in partisanship for a generation of generations or a nation of nations. May Allah protect us from falling into misguidance by following the path of ignorance. Then there is no knowledge of the correctness of what we claim—that he equals other messengers—except after exhibiting his signs and proving his distinction in what is among the specific properties of prophethood. So we begin with exhibiting his signs and we say:
Source pages p. 718

Commentary
This passage applies the previous argument to Muhammad directly. It states that Muhammad equaled other prophets in the evidence of prophethood—namely miracles—and in the specific properties of prophethood. Therefore, he is equal in the truth of his claim and the obligation to accept it. The passage then identifies three causes for rejecting his prophethood: (1) Satan distracting one from reflecting on his signs, (2) blind imitation of ancestral traditions, and (3) transgression and envy leading to partisanship. The author prays for protection from such misguidance. Finally, the passage declares that to prove Muhammad's equality with other prophets, one must present his miracles. This section ends by announcing the beginning of listing those signs.

The Principle: Miracles Prove Prophethood by Breaking Natural Laws
The author states the principle that miracles are proofs by their supernatural nature and gives examples.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the evidentiary value of miracles lies in their supernatural nature, not their specific form.

Core Idea
Miracles prove prophethood by breaking habitual patterns, not by their form.

The author begins by establishing a foundational principle: the proof of a miracle is not in its specific form, but in its departure from natural laws. He illustrates this with examples from earlier prophets, showing that miracles are beyond created power. This principle is essential for understanding the consistency of prophethood across all messengers.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the first paragraph of the source. Focus on the author's main claim about what makes a proof a proof.
Notice the phrase 'not because of their forms, but because of their departure from habitual occurrences.'
2
Identify the examples of miracles
List the miracles mentioned: staff turning into a serpent, water gushing from rock, reviving the dead, healing the blind and leprous. Ask: what do they have in common?
3
Understand the logical reason
The author argues miracles are proofs because they break habit and are beyond created power. Why does this make them reliable signs of truth?
Reflect on the impossibility of these acts being performed by anyone other than the Creator.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم من المعارف الأولية التي لا يداخلها شك ولا يخالطها ريبة ولا شبهة، أن الاستواء في الأدلة يطلب من حيث المعنى الذي به صارت الأدلة أدلة له من حيث الصور التي لم تكن الأدلة أدلة لأجلها، ثم قلب العصا حية وتفجير الماء من الصخرة الصماء وإحياء الموتى، وإبراء الأكمة والأبرص، وغير ذلك مما كانت دلائل وحججًا لصحة الرسالة لا لصورها بل لخروجها عن العادات، وامتناع دخولها تحت القدرة المحدثة، واختصاصها بدخولها تحت قدرة الصانع الحكيم الذي لا يعجزه شيء، ولا يقيم الدلالة على صحة الفاسد وصدق الكاذب وثبوتها عقيب دعوى الرسالة.

ثم إن رسولنا المصطفى محمد ساوى غيره من الأنبياء فيما هو دلالة النبوة والرسالة وفيما هو من خواص النبوة، فيساويهم في صحة دعواه ووجوب قبول ما ادعى أنه من عند الله، وتصديقه في جميع ذلك، فمن أقر بنبوة غيره وأنكر نبوته وكذبه في دعواه فقد وقع في ذلك، إما لصد الشيطان إياه عن التأمل في آياته وإما لتمسكه بما ورثه من آبائه تقليدًا لهم، وإما لسلوكه سبيل البغي والحسد واشتغاله بالتعصب لجيل من الأجيال وأمة من الأمم عصمنا الله تعالى عن الوقوع في الضلالة لسلوك سبيل الجهالة.

ثم لا وقوف على صحة ما ادعينا من مساواته غيره من الرسل إلا بعد إبانة آياته، وإثبات اختصاصه فيما هو من خواص النبوة، فنبدأ بالإبانة عن آياته فنقول:
Then among the primary cognitions that admit no doubt, nor is any uncertainty or misgiving mixed with them, is that equality in the proofs is sought from the perspective of the meaning by which the proofs became proofs, not from the perspective of the forms for the sake of which the proofs were not proofs. Then the turning of the staff into a serpent, the gushing forth of water from the solid rock, the reviving of the dead, the healing of the blind and the leprous, and other such things, were proofs and evidences for the validity of the message—not because of their forms, but because of their departure from habitual occurrences, and the impossibility of their falling under created power, and their being exclusively within the power of the Wise Maker whom nothing renders incapable. And neither does He establish evidence for the validity of the corrupt nor the truthfulness of the liar, and their occurrence in close succession to the claim of messengership.

Then our chosen Messenger Muhammad (peace be upon him) equaled other prophets in that which is the proof of prophethood and messengership, and in that which is among the special characteristics of prophethood. Thus he equals them in the validity of his claim and the obligation to accept what he claimed to be from God, and to believe him in all of that. So whoever acknowledges the prophethood of others but denies his prophethood and calls him a liar in his claim has fallen into that—either due to Satan diverting him from reflecting on his signs, or due to his clinging to what he inherited from his forefathers by way of blind imitation, or due to his following the path of transgression and envy and occupying himself with partisanship for a generation of generations or a nation of nations. May God Almighty protect us from falling into misguidance by following the path of ignorance.

Then there is no verifying the validity of what we have claimed concerning his equality with other messengers except after expounding his signs and establishing his special distinction in that which is among the special characteristics of prophethood. So we begin the exposition of his signs and say:
Source pages p. 718

Commentary
This passage is a proof for the consistency of prophethood. The author states that it is a primary knowledge that the evidentiary value of miracles lies not in their form but in their meaning—i.e., their supernatural character. He gives examples of miracles from previous prophets (Moses, Jesus). Then he argues that Muhammad's miracles are analogous; therefore, denying his prophethood while accepting others is inconsistent, and he attributes such denial to three causes: Satanic diversion, blind imitation, or envy. He then announces that he will proceed to enumerate Muhammad's signs to prove his equal standing.

Key Terms
المعارف الأولية
الاستواء في الأدلة
المعجزات

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The specific form (e.g., staff turning to snake) is what makes a miracle a proof.
Correction: The author states that miracles are proofs not because of their forms but because they depart from habitual occurrences and are beyond created power.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the primary reason miracles serve as proofs for prophethood?
A) Their specific forms
B) Their departure from habitual occurrences and being beyond created power
C) Their being numerous
D) Their being mentioned in previous scriptures

Key Takeaway
Miracles are proofs of prophethood because they break the normal course of nature and can only be performed by divine power, not because of their outward form.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

The lesson teaches that Allah's power is above all habits. Right now, what is one 'locked' area of your life where you need to trust in His power over the normal? Will you make a du'a tonight specifically asking for a breakthrough that only He can bring?
?
The lesson says miracles are proofs because they occur after a claim of prophethood. Have you truly accepted the proof of the Prophet Muhammad (peace be upon him) through the Quran and his other miracles? Examine your heart: is there any doubt you are clinging to? What step will you take today to strengthen your certainty in his truthfulness?
?
The author stresses that the form of a miracle is not what makes it a proof, but its meaning. In your spiritual life, do you sometimes focus on the outward forms of worship (how they look) rather than the inner meaning and sincerity? How can you shift your focus today to seek the deeper purpose behind the acts of worship you perform?

Muhammad's Equality with Other Prophets and the Causes of Denial
The author asserts Muhammad's equality with other prophets in proof of prophethood and lists causes for denial.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why denying Muhammad's prophethood while accepting other prophets is logically inconsistent, and the three reasons people fall into such denial.

Core Idea
Denying Muhammad's prophethood while accepting others contradicts the very evidence of prophethood.

Having established that miracles prove prophethood by breaking natural law, the author now applies this to Muhammad. He argues that Muhammad equals all other prophets in the essential proof of prophethood, so rejecting his mission while accepting others is inconsistent. He attributes such denial to three causes: satanic diversion, blind imitation, or envy. He then announces that he will enumerate Muhammad's signs to confirm his equal standing.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage focusing on equality
Read the second and third paragraphs. Identify the author's claim: Muhammad equals other prophets in the proof of prophethood.
Notice the phrase 'equaled other prophets in that which is the proof of prophethood.'
2
Identify the three causes of denial
The author lists three reasons why some people accept other prophets but reject Muhammad. List them: satanic diversion, blind imitation, envy/partisanship.
3
Reflect on the logical inconsistency
If all prophets are validated by the same type of evidence (supernatural miracles), then accepting some and rejecting others is irrational. Why do you think people still do it?
4
Note the author's plan
The author says he will now enumerate Muhammad's miracles to prove his equal standing. This sets up the next section of the book.
The phrase 'So we begin the exposition of his signs' signals a transition.

ثم من المعارف الأولية التي لا يداخلها شك ولا يخالطها ريبة ولا شبهة، أن الاستواء في الأدلة يطلب من حيث المعنى الذي به صارت الأدلة أدلة له من حيث الصور التي لم تكن الأدلة أدلة لأجلها، ثم قلب العصا حية وتفجير الماء من الصخرة الصماء وإحياء الموتى، وإبراء الأكمة والأبرص، وغير ذلك مما كانت دلائل وحججًا لصحة الرسالة لا لصورها بل لخروجها عن العادات، وامتناع دخولها تحت القدرة المحدثة، واختصاصها بدخولها تحت قدرة الصانع الحكيم الذي لا يعجزه شيء، ولا يقيم الدلالة على صحة الفاسد وصدق الكاذب وثبوتها عقيب دعوى الرسالة.

ثم إن رسولنا المصطفى محمد ساوى غيره من الأنبياء فيما هو دلالة النبوة والرسالة وفيما هو من خواص النبوة، فيساويهم في صحة دعواه ووجوب قبول ما ادعى أنه من عند الله، وتصديقه في جميع ذلك، فمن أقر بنبوة غيره وأنكر نبوته وكذبه في دعواه فقد وقع في ذلك، إما لصد الشيطان إياه عن التأمل في آياته وإما لتمسكه بما ورثه من آبائه تقليدًا لهم، وإما لسلوكه سبيل البغي والحسد واشتغاله بالتعصب لجيل من الأجيال وأمة من الأمم عصمنا الله تعالى عن الوقوع في الضلالة لسلوك سبيل الجهالة.

ثم لا وقوف على صحة ما ادعينا من مساواته غيره من الرسل إلا بعد إبانة آياته، وإثبات اختصاصه فيما هو من خواص النبوة، فنبدأ بالإبانة عن آياته فنقول:
Then among the primary cognitions that admit no doubt, nor is any uncertainty or misgiving mixed with them, is that equality in the proofs is sought from the perspective of the meaning by which the proofs became proofs, not from the perspective of the forms for the sake of which the proofs were not proofs. Then the turning of the staff into a serpent, the gushing forth of water from the solid rock, the reviving of the dead, the healing of the blind and the leprous, and other such things, were proofs and evidences for the validity of the message—not because of their forms, but because of their departure from habitual occurrences, and the impossibility of their falling under created power, and their being exclusively within the power of the Wise Maker whom nothing renders incapable. And neither does He establish evidence for the validity of the corrupt nor the truthfulness of the liar, and their occurrence in close succession to the claim of messengership.

Then our chosen Messenger Muhammad (peace be upon him) equaled other prophets in that which is the proof of prophethood and messengership, and in that which is among the special characteristics of prophethood. Thus he equals them in the validity of his claim and the obligation to accept what he claimed to be from God, and to believe him in all of that. So whoever acknowledges the prophethood of others but denies his prophethood and calls him a liar in his claim has fallen into that—either due to Satan diverting him from reflecting on his signs, or due to his clinging to what he inherited from his forefathers by way of blind imitation, or due to his following the path of transgression and envy and occupying himself with partisanship for a generation of generations or a nation of nations. May God Almighty protect us from falling into misguidance by following the path of ignorance.

Then there is no verifying the validity of what we have claimed concerning his equality with other messengers except after expounding his signs and establishing his special distinction in that which is among the special characteristics of prophethood. So we begin the exposition of his signs and say:

The Twofold Division of Prophetic Signs
The author divides proofs into sensory and intellectual and defines sensory miracles.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the Prophet's miracles are divided into sensory and intellectual, and how sensory miracles are defined as marvels breaking natural laws.

Core Idea
Prophetic signs are either seen with the eyes or grasped by the mind.

The author begins by establishing the foundational classification of the proofs of prophethood. He divides them into two primary categories: sensory (visible) and intellectual (rational). He then defines sensory miracles as extraordinary events that defy the normal course of nature and habit. This lesson focuses on grasping that division and the definition of sensory signs.

Guided Path
1
Read the initial classification
Read the Arabic passage where the author states that signs are divided into sensory and intellectual. Notice the straightforward assertion.
2
Understand the definition of sensory signs
Focus on the definition: 'what God makes appear to the eyes of marvels contrary to natural laws and habits.' This is the core of sensory miracles.
The author emphasizes that such signs are abundant for the Prophet.
3
Reflect on the two categories
Consider why both sensory and intellectual signs are needed. Sensory signs convince the eyes, intellectual signs convince the mind.
The intellectual signs are not detailed in this passage.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الآيات الدالة على رسالته حسية وعقلية
آيات رسالته لا تنقسم أولا إلى قسمين حسية وعقلية.
أما الحسية منها: وهي ما يظهره الله تعالى للأعين من العجائب المباينة لمجرى الطبائع والبدائع المفارقة للمعهود من العادة وكان له من ذلك ما لا يحصى كثرة.
أقسام الأدلة الحسية:
وهي أقسام ثلاثة: فمنها ما كان خارج ذاته، ومنها ما كان في ذاته ومنها ما كان في أخلاقه.
أولاً: ما كان خارج ذاته:
فأما ما كان خارج ذاته فمن نحو انشقاق القمر، واجتذاب الشجرة، وتسليم الحجر عليه، وشرب الكثير من الشرب القليل من الماء، ونبع الماء من بين أصابعه، وحنين الخشب، وشكاية الناقة وشهادة الشاة المصلية، وما كان من السحاب الذي كان يظله قبل مبعثه، وما كان من حال أبي جهل عليه اللعنة وصخرته حين هوى بها إلى رأسه، وما كان من شأن الشاه الحابل ودرها حين مسح بيده الكريمة على ضرعها على ما ذكر في حديث أم معبد.
ثانيًا: ما كان في ذاته:
وأما ما كان في ذاته فنحو النور الذي كان ينتقل من ظهر إلى بطن إلى ظهر إلى أن خرج، وما كان من الخاتم بين كتفيه، وما وصف أنه كان ربعة ثم كان لا يزاحم طويلين إلا فاقهما، وما روى أنه نظر إلى وجهه وإلى البدر فكان هو أحسن، وأنه كان أطيب ريحًا من المسك وألين من الحرير، وكان يؤخذ عرقه فينتفع به في الطيب، وقد وصفت خلقته بما لا يعرف أحد يوصف بمثله حسنًا وجمالاً، وروى في
The verses (signs) indicating his messengership are sensory and intellectual.
The signs of his messengership are divided, first, into two categories: sensory and intellectual.
As for the sensory ones: they are what God Almighty makes appear to the eyes of marvels that are contrary to the course of natural laws, wonders that are different from what is customary by habit. And he had of that what cannot be counted due to its abundance.
Divisions of sensory proofs:
And they are three divisions: among them are those that are external to his person; among them are those that are in his person; and among them are those that are in his character.
First: What is external to his person:
As for what is external to his person, examples include the splitting of the moon, the drawing of the tree, the greeting of the stone to him, the drinking of many by a small group of water, the gushing of water from between his fingers, the moaning of the wood, the complaint of the she-camel, the testimony of the roasted sheep, the cloud that shaded him before his mission, the incident of Abu Jahl (curse be upon him) and his rock when he threw it at his head, and the incident of the tied-up goat and its milk when he wiped his noble hand on its udder, as mentioned in the hadith of Umm Ma'bad.
Second: What is in his person:
As for what is in his person, examples include the light that was transmitted from back to womb to back until he came out, the seal between his shoulders, the description that he was of medium height and that he would not stand with tall people except that he would surpass them, the narration that he looked at his face and at the full moon and he was more beautiful, that he was more fragrant than musk and softer than silk, and his sweat was taken and used as perfume, and his physique was described in a way that no one is known to be described with such beauty and handsomeness, and it is narrated in
Source pages p. 719

Commentary
This passage is a classification of the prophet's signs. The author divides them first into sensory (hissiyya) and intellectual (aqliyya). Then he focuses on sensory signs, defining them as marvels that break natural laws. He then divides sensory signs into three categories: external to the prophet, in his person, and in his character. He begins listing examples of external signs (moon splitting, tree, stone, water, etc.) and personal signs (light transmission, seal, physique, beauty, fragrance). The text ends mid-sentence.

The Three Kinds of Sensory Miracles
The author divides sensory proofs into three categories and provides examples of the first two.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that sensory miracles are further divided into three categories: external to the Prophet, in his person, and in his character, and you will learn various examples of the first two categories.

Core Idea
Sensory miracles touch the Prophet from outside, inside, and through his character.

After defining sensory signs, the author breaks them down into three subcategories. He first lists examples of external miracles—those that occurred outside the Prophet's own body—such as the splitting of the moon and the gushing of water from his fingers. Then he turns to miracles in his person, like his light and beauty. Although the passage cuts off before finishing the second category, we see the richness of these divine signs.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three categories
Read the Arabic: 'they are three divisions: external to his person, in his person, and in his character.' Note the structure.
2
Examine examples of external miracles
The passage lists many: splitting of the moon, tree drawing near, stone greeting, water from fingers, etc. Notice how each breaks natural law.
These are clear sensory events witnessed by people.
3
Examine examples of personal miracles
Examples include the light transmitted from back to womb, the seal between his shoulders, his surpassing beauty, fragrance, and softness. These are within his own body.
The passage cuts off before completing this list.
4
Note the missing third category
The author mentions miracles in his character, but the passage ends before giving examples. Reflect on what those might be.
Character miracles could include his exemplary conduct and moral perfection.

The Physiognomy Argument for the Prophet's Truthfulness
Argues from physiognomy that the Prophet's physical perfection proves his truthfulness.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Prophet's physical perfection serves as a rational argument for his truthfulness, based on the science of physiognomy.

Core Idea
The Prophet's flawless physique is a rare sign that only a truthful soul could possess.

In this passage, Imam al-Nasafi presents a unique argument for the Prophet's truthfulness based on the science of physiognomy (firasa). He argues that the rare combination of perfect physical traits in the Prophet's body indicates the nobility of his soul, and thus his veracity. The passage then supports this with testimonies from early Muslims who recognized his truthfulness from his appearance.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its literal translation once to get the overall flow. Notice how the argument moves from a general principle to specific testimonies.
The passage is dense but rewarding.
2
Understand the physiognomy proof
Identify the core claim: that the rarity of perfect physical attributes indicates the nobility of the soul. Ask yourself why rarity is a sign of truthfulness.
This is the rational backbone of the argument.
3
Examine the supporting quotations
Study the words of Abu Mansur al-Maturidi, Abdullah ibn Rawaha, and Abdullah ibn Salam. How do they reinforce the main argument?
Each adds a different perspective: theological, poetic, and personal testimony.
4
Reflect on the common misunderstanding
Consider that this is not mere face-reading but a logical inference from rare perfection. Think about why such an argument would be convincing.
This helps avoid dismissing the argument as superstitious.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم إن أصحاب علم الفراسة يجمعون معترفون أن اجتماع هذه الصفات في البدن الواحد مما يقل وجوده، ويعز اتفاقه، وهو مع ذلك دال على أن النفس المختصة بمثل هذا التركيب تكون لا محالة أشرف النفوس وأتمها، فتكون دلالة صادقة بشهادة علم الفراسة أنه صادق خير غير شرير ولا كاذب. والشيخ أبو منصور رحمه الله عبر عن هذا المعنى فقال بعدما وصفه عليه السلام بهذه المعاني المختصة ببدنه : وجل الفتن تراها تهيج في الخبرة بذي الآفات في الخلقة، فدلت براءته عن كل الآفات، وزينه بكل زين على استيجابه أعلى الدرجات في الخلق وأفضل الأقدار ، ولهذا قال عبد الله بن رواحة له: لو لم تكن فيه آيات مبينة كانت بديهته تنبيك بالخير. وروى عن عبد الله بن سلام أنه قال: لما قدم رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم المدينة فقال الناس قدم رسول الله، فخرجت إليه فلما نظرت إليه عرفت أن وجهه ليس بوجه كذاب، وكان أول ما سمعته من كلامه أنه قال: أيها الناس أفشوا السلام، وصلوا الأرحام، وأطعموا الطعام، وصلوا بالليل والناس نيام تدخلوا الجنة بسلام.
Then the practitioners of physiognomy are unanimous and acknowledge that the gathering of these attributes in one body is something whose occurrence is rare and whose combination is difficult; and despite that, it indicates that the soul specialized with such a composition is necessarily the noblest and most perfect of souls. Thus it is a true indication, by the testimony of physiognomy, that he is truthful, good, not evil nor a liar. And the Shaykh Abu Mansur (may Allah have mercy on him) expressed this meaning, saying after he described him (peace be upon him) with these meanings specific to his body: 'And most trials you see emerge from experience with one who has defects in creation; so his freedom from all defects, and his adornment with every adornment, indicated his deserving the highest ranks in character and the best of destinies.' And for this, Abdullah ibn Rawaha said to him: 'If there were no clear signs in him, his very presence would inform you of goodness.' And it was narrated from Abdullah ibn Salam that he said: 'When the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) arrived in Madinah, the people said, 'The Messenger of Allah has come.' I went out to him, and when I looked at him, I recognized that his face was not the face of a liar. And the first thing I heard from his speech was that he said: 'O people, spread peace, maintain ties of kinship, feed the food, pray at night while people sleep, you will enter Paradise in peace.'
Source pages p. 721

Commentary
This passage presents a proof from physiognomy (firasa) for the Prophet's truthfulness. It begins by stating the consensus of physiognomists that the combination of such perfect physical traits in one body is extremely rare; and this rarity indicates that the soul possessing such a body is the noblest and most complete. Therefore, physiognomy testifies that the Prophet is truthful, good, and free from evil and falsehood. The author then quotes the scholar Abu Mansur al-Maturidi, who elaborates that defects in bodily form usually arouse trials, but the Prophet's freedom from all defects and his complete adornment show that he deserves the highest degrees. Then two anecdotal proofs are cited: Abdullah ibn Rawaha's statement that the Prophet's very presence conveyed goodness even without clear miracles, and Abdullah ibn Salam's testimony that upon first seeing the Prophet's face he knew it was not the face of a liar, and he then heard the Prophet's words inviting to peace and good deeds. These support the rational argument from physiognomy.

Key Terms
فِرَاسَة
نفس
أشرف النفوس
دلالة صادقة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The physiognomy argument is based on superstitious face-reading or mere physical appearance.
Correction: This is a rational argument: the extreme rarity of perfect physical attributes points logically to the nobility of the soul, and is supported by the testimony of experts and the recognition of early Companions.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what does the rarity of the Prophet's physical attributes indicate?
A) That he was destined for wealth
B) That his soul is the noblest and most perfect
C) That he was physically weak
D) That he was an ordinary person

Key Takeaway
The Prophet's rare physical perfection is a rational sign of his truthful soul, recognized by physiognomy and early Companions.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The argument links rare physical perfection to a truthful soul. Look at yourself: what does your outward appearance and conduct reveal about your inner faith? Are there any mismatches that you need to correct in order to better reflect the truth you claim to believe?
?
Abdullah ibn Salam recognized the Prophet's truthfulness at first sight. If someone saw you for the first time, would they suspect you of being a liar or a truthful person? What specific changes in your daily behavior would make your face and presence more honest witnesses to your faith?
?
The Prophet's freedom from physical defects was a sign of his spiritual perfection. In contrast, your imperfections—both physical and character—can lead others to doubt your sincerity. Which personal defect most undermines your testimony to others? What concrete step will you take this week to begin removing it?

The Vastness of the Prophet's Moral Character
Introduces the discussion of the Prophet's extensive moral character.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the author introduces the Prophet's moral character with an acknowledgement of its vastness and the need for selective mention.

Core Idea
The Prophet's character is too vast to fully describe; we can only capture a glimpse.

This lesson opens a new section on the Prophet's moral character. The author immediately humbles his endeavor by noting that the topic is inexhaustible. This sets the tone for a selective, yet profound, exploration of the Prophetic example.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once, then the English translation. Notice the author's humility and the key terms he uses to express the boundless nature of the Prophet's character.
The passage is brief but dense in meaning.
2
Reflect on the difficulty of enumeration
Consider why the author says 'its counting is difficult' and 'its enumeration exceeds capacity and vision.' What does this imply about the Prophet's moral stature?
This sets the expectation that we will only sample from a vast treasure.
3
Understand the purpose of selective mention
The author does not deny the importance of the topic; rather, he selects some traits to give a taste of the whole. Reflect on why this approach is effective in teaching.
Selective mention is a common pedagogical tool when the subject is too vast.
4
Connect to Prophethood
The Prophet's moral character is a sign of his prophethood. Consider how this passage invites us to reflect on the perfection of his character as part of his divine mission.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثالثًا: ما كان من أخلاقه عليه السلام: وأما ما كان من أخلاقه عليه السلام فكثير جدًا يتعذر إحصاؤه ويفوت الوسع والطرف تعداده فنذكر بعضًا من ذلك.
Thirdly: his character (peace be upon him). As for his character (peace be upon him), it is very abundant; its counting is difficult, and its enumeration exceeds capacity and vision, so we will mention some of that.
Source pages p. 721

Commentary
This brief passage serves as a section header introducing the topic of the Prophet's moral character (akhlaq). The author acknowledges the immense depth and breadth of his character, stating that it is impossible to fully enumerate or encompass. Therefore, he will only present a selection. This sets realistic expectations and highlights the Prophet's unparalleled moral excellence.

Key Terms
أخلاق
إحصاء
الوسع والطرف

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The author is minimizing the importance of moral character by only mentioning some.
Correction: On the contrary, the author is exalting it by stating that it is too vast to fully enumerate; he selects only a portion as a sample of its greatness.

Checkpoint

B) Because they are too many to count
C) Because he does not know them
D) Because they are controversial

Key Takeaway
The Prophet's moral character is so immense that it defies complete enumeration, so scholars present select examples to illustrate his unparalleled excellence.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
The author humbly admits he can only mention some of the Prophet's virtues. When you reflect on your own efforts to follow the Prophet, are you content with a mere glimpse, or do you strive to embody even the parts that are hard to practice?
?
The phrase 'its enumeration exceeds capacity and vision' reminds us that we cannot fully grasp the Prophet's moral excellence. Does this realization humble you, or do you assume you already know enough? What one change can you make today to better align your character with his?

Proof from Physiognomy and Testimonies
Physiognomy argument and two testimonies

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the rare combination of physical attributes and direct testimonies from companions serve as evidence for the Prophet's truthfulness.

Core Idea
Physiognomy and witness confirm the Prophet's truthfulness beyond doubt.

The author begins with a proof from the science of physiognomy (firasa), which holds that certain bodily traits indicate the nobility of the soul. He then supports this with two eyewitness accounts. This lesson explores these interconnected proofs.

Guided Path
1
Read the physiognomy argument
Read the passage from the beginning to understand the claim that the gathering of specific attributes in one body is rare and indicates a noble soul.
Notice the use of the science of physiognomy as a recognized discipline.
2
Examine Sheikh Abu Mansur's expression
Read the quote from Sheikh Abu Mansur al-Maturidi, which ties physical perfection to high rank.
3
Study the two testimonies
Read the testimonies of Abdullah ibn Rawaha and Abdullah ibn Salam. Note how each confirms the Prophet's truthfulness based on direct observation.
Abdullah ibn Salam's testimony includes a practical example of the Prophet's teachings.
4
Synthesize the proofs
Consider how the rare physical traits and the witness accounts together form a strong cumulative argument.
This combination addresses potential objections to relying on appearance alone.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم إن أصحاب علم الفراسة يجمعون معترفون أن اجتماع هذه الصفات في البدن الواحد مما يقل وجوده، ويعز اتفاقه، وهو مع ذلك دال على أن النفس المختصة بمثل هذا التركيب تكون لا محالة أشرف النفوس وأتمها، فتكون دلالة صادقة بشهادة علم الفراسة أنه صادق خير غير شرير ولا كاذب. والشيخ أبو منصور رحمه الله عبر عن هذا المعنى فقال بعدما وصفه عليه السلام بهذه المعاني المختصة ببدنه : وجل الفتن تراها تهيج في الخبرة بذي الآفات في الخلقة، فدلت براءته عن كل الآفات، وزينه بكل زين على استيجابه أعلى الدرجات في الخلق وأفضل الأقدار ، ولهذا قال عبد الله بن رواحة له: لو لم تكن فيه آيات مبينة كانت بديهته تنبيك بالخير. وروى عن عبد الله بن سلام أنه قال : لما قدم رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم المدينة فقال الناس قدم رسول الله، فخرجت إليه فلما نظرت إليه عرفت أن وجهه ليس بوجه كذاب، وكان أول ما سمعته من كلامه أنه قال: أيها الناس أفشوا السلام، وصلوا الأرحام، وأطعموا الطعام، وصلوا بالليل والناس نيام تدخلوا الجنة بسلام. ثالثًا: ما كان من أخلاقه عليه السلام: وأما ما كان من أخلاقه عليه السلام فكثير جدًا يتعذر إحصاؤه ويفوت الوسع والطرف تعداده فنذكر بعضًا من ذلك. أعدائه فمنه أنه لا لو لم يؤخذ عليه كذب قط، ولا عرفت منه هفوة ولا منه عن فرار، بل كان في الشجاعة بمحل، ما ولى دبره قط في حرب على ما أصاب أتباعه من النكبات والشدائد ، ولذلك أمكنه الركون إلى وعد الله تعالى بقوله: ﴿ وَاللَّهُ يَعْصِمُكَ مِنَ النَّاسِ ﴾ فلم يخف أعداءه بعد ذلك، ولم يعرف في أخلاقه سوء. كان على وصفه لا يداري ولا يماري، ولا يعرف فحاشا ولا صخابا، وكان لا ينتصر لنفسه، وكان في الإشفاق بالمحل الذي عوتب عليه بقوله تعالى: ﴿فَلَا تَذْهَبْ نَفْسُكَ عَلَيْهِمْ حَسَرَاتٍ﴾ وقوله تعالى: ﴿ فَلَعَلَّكَ بَاخِعٌ نَفْسَكَ ﴾ وفي التحزن عما به هلاك الخلق كما وصفه الله تعالى بقوله: ﴿وَلَا تَحْزَنْ عَلَيْهِمْ﴾ وقال : ﴿عَزِيزٌ عَلَيْهِ مَا عَنِتُّمْ﴾ وكان في السخاء والكرم بحيث عوتب عليه بقوله تعالى: ﴿وَلَا تَبْسُطْهَا كُلَّ الْبَسْطِ﴾ وقيل : إنه عليه السلام لم يدخر شيئًا لغد وقد عرض عليه أعلى يرغب فيه من متاع الدنيا والرياسة بأن يداهن قليلاً فما أجاب، بل عادى الله تعالى ما الأقرباء والملوك والسادات حتى أكرمه الله تعالى بالرعب في قلوب الخلق. وفي الجملة كان عليه الصلاة والسلام في حلمه ووفائه وزهده وسخائه وأمانته وسداده، وشجاعته، وعفافه، وصادق في صبره، وذكاء فهمه وقلة تلونه، وبارع حفظه، وقوله بجوامع الكلم إذا قال، ومراعاته لشرائط الصمت إذا
Then the practitioners of physiognomy (firasa) unanimously acknowledge that the gathering of these attributes in a single body is rare in existence, and its occurrence is infrequent, and it nonetheless indicates that the soul specific to such a composition is inevitably the noblest of souls and the most complete. So its indication is truthful by the testimony of the science of physiognomy that he is truthful, good, not evil, nor a liar. And Sheikh Abu Mansur, may Allah have mercy on him, expressed this meaning by saying—after describing him, peace be upon him, with these meanings specific to his body: 'And you see the trials arise in experience due to one with defects in creation, so his innocence from every defect and his adornment with every adornment indicate his entitlement to the highest ranks in character and the best of destinies.' And because of this, Abdullah ibn Rawaha said to him: 'If there were no clear signs in him, his intuitive insight would tell you of goodness.' And it is narrated from Abdullah ibn Salam that he said: 'When the Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, arrived in Medina, the people said: "The Messenger of Allah has come." So I went out to him, and when I looked at him, I knew that his face was not the face of a liar. And the first thing I heard from his speech was that he said: "O people, spread peace, maintain kinship ties, feed food, pray at night while people sleep, and you will enter Paradise in peace."' Third: Regarding his character, peace be upon him: As for his character, peace be upon him, it is very abundant, its enumeration is impossible, and counting it surpasses capacity and scope, so we mention some of that. His enemies: Among it is that he was never known to lie, nor was any lapse known from him, nor was he [known to] flee from battle, but he was in such a degree of courage that he never turned his back in battle despite what befell his followers of calamities and hardships. Therefore, he was able to rely on the promise of Allah Almighty, by His saying: 'And Allah will protect you from the people.' So he did not fear his enemies after that, and no evil was known in his character. He was as described: he neither flattered nor disputed, nor was he known to be obscene or clamorous. He did not take revenge for himself. He was in such compassion that he was rebuked for it by Allah's saying: 'So do not destroy yourself over them with grief,' and His saying: 'Perhaps you would kill yourself with grief.' And in sorrow over the destruction of creation, as Allah described him: 'And do not grieve over them,' and He said: 'Grievous to him is your suffering.' And he was in generosity and munificence to the degree that he was rebuked for it by Allah's saying: 'And do not spread it completely.' And it is said that he, peace be upon him, did not store anything for the morrow, and he was offered the highest desires of worldly goods and leadership, with the condition that he compromise a little, but he did not accept. Rather, he opposed the close relatives, kings, and leaders until Allah honored him with awe in the hearts of the creation. In summary, he, peace and blessings be upon him, was in his forbearance, loyalty, asceticism, generosity, trustworthiness, rectitude, courage, chastity, truthfulness in patience, intelligence of understanding, constancy, excellence of memory, and his speech with comprehensive words when he spoke, and his observance of the conditions of silence when...
Source pages p. 721

Commentary
This passage presents a multi-layered proof of the Prophet's prophethood through his character and physical appearance. It begins with an argument from the science of physiognomy: the combination of certain physical traits in one person is rare and indicates a noble soul, thus the Prophet's appearance testifies to his truthfulness. Then it quotes Sheikh Abu Mansur al-Maturidi, who explains that the Prophet's freedom from any physical defect and his perfect adornment signify his high rank and destiny. The passage then provides two testimonies: Abdullah ibn Rawaha's statement that the Prophet's very presence would convey goodness even without clear signs, and Abdullah ibn Salam's report that upon seeing the Prophet he knew he was not a liar, and heard his initial teaching of spreading peace and maintaining ties. The third section explicitly lists the Prophet's moral virtues: he never lied, fled, or showed cowardice despite hardships; he trusted God's protection; he was free from flattery, disputation, obscenity, and clamor; he did not seek revenge; he was compassionate, generous (even rebuked for excessive generosity), and content with little; he endured hardship steadfastly; and he possessed forbearance, loyalty, asceticism, trustworthiness, courage, chastity, patience, intelligence, consistency, excellent memory, eloquent speech, and proper silence. The combination of these perfections, despite opposition from enemies and temptations of the world, demonstrates that he was a true prophet. The passage follows a clear structure: first the physiognomic proof, then testimonies, then a detailed enumeration of virtues, each serving as evidence.

Key Terms
علم الفراسة
بديهته
آيات مبينة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think that outward beauty alone is proof of prophethood.
Correction: The author combines physiognomy with testimonies and moral virtues as mutual support, showing that it is not merely appearance but the combination of rare traits and witness that confirms truthfulness.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what did Abdullah ibn Salam conclude upon seeing the Prophet?
A) He was a wealthy merchant.
B) His face was not the face of a liar.
C) He was a fierce warrior.
D) He was a poet.

Key Takeaway
The rare physical traits of the Prophet, combined with direct testimonies, form a compelling proof of his truthfulness.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you examine the evidence for the Prophet's truthfulness presented here—from rare physical traits to direct testimonies—does your heart respond with the same certainty that Abdullah ibn Salam felt, or do you find yourself demanding more signs? What is holding you back from that immediate recognition?
?
The practitioners of physiognomy judged by external appearance; but you know that many people deceive with their appearance. How can you be sure that your own heart is not deceived when it comes to recognizing truth? What are you doing to cultivate a discerning eye that sees beyond the surface?
?
Abdullah ibn Rawaha said that even without clear signs, the Prophet's intuitive insight would tell you of goodness. If you were in his presence, would your own intuition recognize truth? Or has your inner sense been dulled by doubt, distraction, or sin? What will you do today to sharpen that spiritual intuition?

The Prophet's Moral Virtues as Proof of Prophethood
Enumeration of Prophet's moral virtues

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Prophet's unparalleled moral and spiritual character serves as evidence of his prophethood.

Core Idea
The Prophet's perfect character, despite trials, proves his prophethood.

After the proofs from physiognomy and testimonies, the author turns to the Prophet's moral character, listing virtues such as courage, generosity, forbearance, and compassion, and noting that these were accompanied by divine correction. This lesson examines these qualities as evidence.

The author uses divine rebukes as proof of the Prophet's exceptionality.
3
Reflect on the summary
Read the concluding summary that lists many virtues, emphasizing their perfection.
4
Consider the overall argument
Think about how the combination of these virtues, especially in the face of persecution, points to divine guidance.

ينتصر لنفسه، وكان في الإشفاق بالمحل الذي عوتب عليه بقوله تعالى: ﴿فَلَا تَذْهَبْ نَفْسُكَ عَلَيْهِمْ حَسَرَاتٍ﴾ وقوله تعالى: ﴿ فَلَعَلَّكَ بَاخِعٌ نَفْسَكَ ﴾ وفي التحزن عما به هلاك الخلق كما وصفه الله تعالى بقوله: ﴿وَلَا تَحْزَنْ عَلَيْهِمْ﴾ وقال : ﴿عَزِيزٌ عَلَيْهِ مَا عَنِتُّمْ﴾ وكان في السخاء والكرم بحيث عوتب عليه بقوله تعالى: ﴿وَلَا تَبْسُطْهَا كُلَّ الْبَسْطِ﴾ وقيل : إنه عليه السلام لم يدخر شيئًا لغد وقد عرض عليه أعلى يرغب فيه من متاع الدنيا والرياسة بأن يداهن قليلاً فما أجاب، بل عادى الله تعالى ما الأقرباء والملوك والسادات حتى أكرمه الله تعالى بالرعب في قلوب الخلق. وفي الجملة كان عليه الصلاة والسلام في حلمه ووفائه وزهده وسخائه وأمانته وسداده، وشجاعته، وعفافه، وصادق في صبره، وذكاء فهمه وقلة تلونه، وبارع حفظه، وقوله بجوامع الكلم إذا قال، ومراعاته لشرائط الصمت إذا
Then the practitioners of physiognomy (firasa) unanimously acknowledge that the gathering of these attributes in a single body is rare in existence, and its occurrence is infrequent, and it nonetheless indicates that the soul specific to such a composition is inevitably the noblest of souls and the most complete. So its indication is truthful by the testimony of the science of physiognomy that he is truthful, good, not evil, nor a liar. And Sheikh Abu Mansur, may Allah have mercy on him, expressed this meaning by saying—after describing him, peace be upon him, with these meanings specific to his body: 'And you see the trials arise in experience due to one with defects in creation, so his innocence from every defect and his adornment with every adornment indicate his entitlement to the highest ranks in character and the best of destinies.' And because of this, Abdullah ibn Rawaha said to him: 'If there were no clear signs in him, his intuitive insight would tell you of goodness.' And it is narrated from Abdullah ibn Salam that he said: 'When the Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, arrived in Medina, the people said: "The Messenger of Allah has come." So I went out to him, and when I looked at him, I knew that his face was not the face of a liar. And the first thing I heard from his speech was that he said: "O people, spread peace, maintain kinship ties, feed food, pray at night while people sleep, and you will enter Paradise in peace."' Third: Regarding his character, peace be upon him: As for his character, peace be upon him, it is very abundant, its enumeration is impossible, and counting it surpasses capacity and scope, so we mention some of that. His enemies: Among it is that he was never known to lie, nor was any lapse known from him, nor was he [known to] flee from battle, but he was in such a degree of courage that he never turned his back in battle despite what befell his followers of calamities and hardships. Therefore, he was able to rely on the promise of Allah Almighty, by His saying: 'And Allah will protect you from the people.' So he did not fear his enemies after that, and no evil was known in his character. He was as described: he neither flattered nor disputed, nor was he known to be obscene or clamorous. He did not take revenge for himself. He was in such compassion that he was rebuked for it by Allah's saying: 'So do not destroy yourself over them with grief,' and His saying: 'Perhaps you would kill yourself with grief.' And in sorrow over the destruction of creation, as Allah described him: 'And do not grieve over them,' and He said: 'Grievous to him is your suffering.' And he was in generosity and munificence to the degree that he was rebuked for it by Allah's saying: 'And do not spread it completely.' And it is said that he, peace be upon him, did not store anything for the morrow, and he was offered the highest desires of worldly goods and leadership, with the condition that he compromise a little, but he did not accept. Rather, he opposed the close relatives, kings, and leaders until Allah honored him with awe in the hearts of the creation. In summary, he, peace and blessings be upon him, was in his forbearance, loyalty, asceticism, generosity, trustworthiness, rectitude, courage, chastity, truthfulness in patience, intelligence of understanding, constancy, excellence of memory, and his speech with comprehensive words when he spoke, and his observance of the conditions of silence when...
Source pages p. 721

Commentary
This passage presents a multi-layered proof of the Prophet's prophethood through his character and physical appearance. It begins with an argument from the science of physiognomy: the combination of certain physical traits in one person is rare and indicates a noble soul, thus the Prophet's appearance testifies to his truthfulness. Then it quotes Sheikh Abu Mansur al-Maturidi, who explains that the Prophet's freedom from any physical defect and his perfect adornment signify his high rank and destiny. The passage then provides two testimonies: Abdullah ibn Rawaha's statement that the Prophet's very presence would convey goodness even without clear signs, and Abdullah ibn Salam's report that upon seeing the Prophet he knew he was not a liar, and heard his initial teaching of spreading peace and maintaining ties. The third section explicitly lists the Prophet's moral virtues: he never lied, fled, or showed cowardice despite hardships; he trusted God's protection; he was free from flattery, disputation, obscenity, and clamor; he did not seek revenge; he was compassionate, generous (even rebuked for excessive generosity), and content with little; he endured hardship steadfastly; and he possessed forbearance, loyalty, asceticism, trustworthiness, courage, chastity, patience, intelligence, consistency, excellent memory, eloquent speech, and proper silence. The combination of these perfections, despite opposition from enemies and temptations of the world, demonstrates that he was a true prophet. The passage follows a clear structure: first the physiognomic proof, then testimonies, then a detailed enumeration of virtues, each serving as evidence.

Key Terms
الشجاعة
السخاء
الحلم
الوفاء
الزهد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that moral character alone is subjective and not a strong proof.
Correction: The author uses divine rebukes as evidence that the Prophet's virtues were so exceptional that even God commented on them, showing they are not ordinary.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following virtues is mentioned as being so strong that the Prophet was rebuked for it?
A) Courage
B) Generosity
C) Truthfulness
D) Trust in God

Key Takeaway
The Prophet's perfect character, evidenced by divine correction and refusal of worldly gain, confirms his prophethood.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The Prophet was offered the highest worldly leadership if he would compromise even slightly. You have likely faced a situation where you could gain something by bending your principles. Which compromise are you still holding onto, and what is stopping you from letting it go today?
?
The Prophet's compassion was so intense that Allah rebuked him for grieving too much over those who rejected him. When was the last time you truly grieved for someone's spiritual state? Is your heart more burdened by your own comfort or by the loss of others to guidance?
?
The Prophet never lied, not even to his enemies. Think of an area in your life where you tell 'small' lies—to get out of trouble, to avoid embarrassment, or to gain an advantage. How would your life change if you committed to absolute truthfulness starting this moment?

Prophethood

The Prophet's Moral Virtues as Proof of Prophethood
Nasafi enumerates the Prophet's consistent virtues as evidence of divine support for his prophethood.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Prophet's consistent moral virtues serve as a proof of his prophethood, specifically why their unwavering nature indicates divine support rather than human pretense.

Core Idea
The Prophet's unchanging virtues reveal divine support, not human effort.

Nasafi presents a unique proof of prophethood based on the Prophet's character. He first lists specific virtues and then argues that their consistency over a lifetime cannot be faked. This lesson unpacks that argument and shows why it is compelling.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the translation. Let the author's own description of the Prophet's virtues come through.
Notice the extensive list of virtues.
2
Identify the core argument
Nasafi argues that these virtues were constant over time and circumstances. This constancy is key to proving they were not pretense (takalluf).
3
Examine the supporting evidence
The author uses poetry and logic: a pretender eventually reverts to his nature. The Prophet never did.
Poetic references reinforce the point.
4
Reflect on the conclusion
The unwavering virtues are divine gifts (mawāhib) indicating heavenly support, confirming his prophethood.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فمنه أنه لا لو لم يؤخذ عليه كذب قط، ولا عرفت منه هفوة ولا منه عن فرار، بل كان في الشجاعة بمحل، ما ولى دبره قط (في حرب) على ما أصاب أتباعه من النكبات والشدائد، ولذلك أمكنه الركون إلى وعد الله تعالى بقوله: ﴿ وَاللَّهُ يَعْصِمُكَ مِنَ النَّاسِ ﴾ فلم يخف أعداءه بعد ذلك، ولم يعرف في أخلاقه سوء. كان على وصفه لا يداري ولا يماري، ولا يعرف فحاشا ولا صخابا، وكان لا ينتصر لنفسه، وكان في الإشفاق بالمحل الذي عوتب عليه بقوله تعالى: ﴿فَلَا تَذْهَبْ نَفْسُكَ عَلَيْهِمْ حَسَرَتٍ﴾ وقوله تعالى: ﴿ فَلَعَلَّكَ بَاخِعٌ نَفْسَكَ ﴾ وفي التحزن عما به هلاك الخلق كما وصفه الله تعالى بقوله: ﴿وَلَا تَحْزَنْ عَلَيْهِمْ﴾ وقال: ﴿عَزِيزٌ عَلَيْهِ مَا عَنِتُّمْ﴾ وكان في السخاء والكرم بحيث عوتب عليه بقوله تعالى: ﴿ وَلَا تَبْسُطْهَا كُلَّ الْبَسْطِ ﴾ وقيل: إنه عليه السلام لم يدخر شيئًا لغد وقد عرض عليه أعلى يرغب فيه من متاع الدنيا والرياسة بأن يداهن قليلاً فما أجاب، بل عادى الله تعالى الأقرباء والملوك والسادات حتى أكرمه الله تعالى بالرعب في قلوب الخلق. وفي الجملة كان عليه الصلاة والسلام في حلمه ووفائه وزهده وسخائه وأمانته وسداده، وشجاعته، وعفافه، وصادق في صبره، وذكاء فهمه وقلة تلونه، وبارع حفظه، وقوله بجوامع الكلم إذا قال، ومراعاته لشرائط الصمت إذا صمت، وتصديقه المواعيد إذا وعد وطهارة أخلاقه كلها صبيًّا وناشئًا وكهلاً، بحيث تتبع آثاره أعداؤه الذين تأمروا على معاداته، وتجانبوا عن مسالمته ومداراته، بل ناصبوه الحرب، وداوموا على قصد إطفاء نوره وطمس آثاره وإبادة أتباعه وأشياعه بالطمس والضرب. كانت هذه الأخلاق الفاضلة والشمائل الشريفة موجودة فيه على طول الأيام وتصاريف الأحوال لم تتغير عن شيء منها في حالة، ولا وجد منه ضد من أضدادها طول عمره البتة، فكان ذلك دليلاً أن شيئًا منها لم يكن عن تكلف، إذ المتكلف لما ليس في طباعه لا يستمر على ما يتكلفه بل لابد أن يرجع في كثير من الأحايين إلى ما جبل عليه من الخلق ولهذا قيل: إن التخلق يأتي دونه الخلق. وقال بعض الشعراء: يتخلق بغير خلق يرجع بصفر إلى الطبيعة. وما أحسن ما قال المتنبي: وأسرع مفعول صنعت تغيرا تكلف شيء في طباعك ضده. فكان جريه على السلام على طريقة واحدة في تساوي الأخلاق على امتداد الأزمنة والدهور، واختلاف الأحوال والأمور دليلاً أنها مواهب من مواهب الله تعالى؛ ليكون اجتماعها كلها وانتفاء أضدادها التي هي رذائل بأسرها عنه دلالة صادقة، أنه المؤيد بقوة سماوية، والمكرم بمعونة إلهية، ليشتغل بالقيام بما فرض إليه، وتحمل أعباء ما حمل عليه من أمور الرسالة إلى أصناف الخليقة والأمة والرياسة على جميع طبقات البرية.
So among them (the evidences) is that he was never caught in a lie, nor was any slip known from him, nor fleeing from battle; rather he was in bravery in a rank—he never turned his back in war despite what befell his followers of calamities and hardships. Therefore he was able to rely on the promise of Allah the Exalted in His saying: 'And Allah will protect you from the people' (Quran 5:67), so he did not fear his enemies after that, and no evil was known in his character. He was as described: he did not flatter nor dispute, nor was he known for obscenity or clamor. He did not avenge himself, and he was in compassion such that he was rebuked for it in His saying: 'So do not let your soul be destroyed over them in regret' (Quran 35:8) and His saying: 'Perhaps you will kill yourself with grief' (Quran 18:6), and in grief over that which causes the destruction of creation as Allah described him: 'And do not grieve over them' (Quran 16:127) and He said: 'Grievous to him is what you suffer' (Quran 9:128). He was in generosity and munificence such that he was rebuked for it in His saying: 'And do not spread it all out completely' (Quran 17:29). And it is said: He, peace be upon him, did not store anything for tomorrow; and the most excellent that one desires of worldly goods and leadership was offered to him—that he compromise a little—but he did not accept. Rather he opposed Allah regarding relatives, kings, and nobles, until Allah honored him with awe in the hearts of creation. In summary, he, may peace and blessings be upon him, was in his forbearance, faithfulness, asceticism, generosity, trustworthiness, rectitude, bravery, chastity, truthfulness in his patience, intelligence of understanding, lack of changeableness, excellent memory, speech with comprehensive expressions when he spoke, observance of the conditions of silence when he was silent, fulfillment of promises when he promised, and purity of all his morals—child, youth, and adult—such that his enemies followed his footsteps, those who conspired against him, who avoided peace with him and leniency, rather they waged war against him and persisted in seeking to extinguish his light, obliterate his traces, and annihilate his followers and partisans by obliteration and striking. These virtuous characters and noble traits existed in him over the length of days and the vicissitudes of circumstances, not changing from any of them in any state, nor was any opposite of them found from him throughout his entire life ever. So that was evidence that none of them was from pretense, for one who pretends what is not in his nature does not persist in what he pretends; rather he must eventually return in many instances to the nature he was created upon. Hence it is said: 'Adopted character falls short of innate character.' And some poets said: 'He who adopts a character not his own returns empty-handed to his nature.' And how excellent is what al-Mutanabbi said: 'The quickest thing to change is a manufactured effect; feigning something contrary to your nature is hard.' So his continuance on a single path in the equality of his morals over the extension of times and ages, and the difference of circumstances and affairs, is evidence that they are gifts from the gifts of Allah the Exalted; so that their combination all together and the absence of their opposites—which are vices—entirely from him is a truthful indication that he is supported by a heavenly power and honored by divine assistance, to occupy himself with fulfilling what was enjoined upon him and bearing the burdens of what he was charged with of the affairs of the message to all kinds of creation and the community and leadership over all classes of humanity.
Source pages p. 722

Commentary
This passage presents a proof of prophethood based on the Prophet Muhammad's moral virtues. The author, Imam Nasafi, first enumerates specific excellent traits: truthfulness (never lying), bravery (never fleeing), compassion (grieving for the community), generosity (not storing for tomorrow), and opposition to worldly compromise. He then summarizes a longer list including forbearance, faithfulness, asceticism, trustworthiness, rectitude, chastity, patience, intelligence, consistency, excellent memory, eloquent speech, observance of silence, and fulfillment of promises. Importantly, these traits were constant throughout his life, from childhood to old age, even as circumstances changed. The author argues that such unvarying excellence cannot be mere pretense (takalluf), because a pretender eventually slips back to his innate nature. He supports this with poetic sayings. The conclusion is that these consistently held virtues are divine gifts (mawāhib) that indicate divine support and heavenly power, confirming that the Prophet was truly aided by God to carry out his mission. Thus, the perfect and unwavering character of the Prophet becomes a clear sign of his prophethood.

Key Terms
تكلف (takalluf)
مواهب (mawāhib)
دليل (dalīl)
أخلاق فاضلة (akhlāq fāḍilah)
قوة سماوية (quwwa samāwiyya)
معونة إلهية (maʿūna ilāhiyya)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that the Prophet's excellent character alone is insufficient as a proof of prophethood, but the author argues that its unwavering consistency and absence of pretense show its divine origin.
Correction: The constancy of virtues over a lifetime, despite all circumstances, is what makes them a proof. A mere human cannot maintain such perfection without divine aid.

Checkpoint
According to Nasafi, what is the key indication that the Prophet's moral virtues were not due to pretense (takalluf)?
A) The Prophet's virtues were described in poetry.
B) The virtues remained consistent throughout his life without change.
C) The Prophet was rebuked for some of these virtues.
D) The Prophet's enemies also possessed similar virtues.

Key Takeaway
The Prophet's unwavering moral virtues over a lifetime are a sign of divine support for his prophethood, as they cannot be maintained by human pretense.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The Prophet never changed his virtues despite all trials. Think of one area in your life where you have been inconsistent in a good quality. What is holding you back from being steadfast like the Prophet? What will you do today to take a step towards that consistency?
?
The passage says the Prophet did not avenge himself. Is there someone you need to forgive or a wrong you need to let go of for the sake of Allah? How can the Prophet's example help you take that step?
?
The Prophet was offered worldly gain to compromise, but he refused. What worldly comfort or reputation are you holding onto that might be compromising your faith? Are you willing to give it up for the sake of Allah? What concrete action can you take this week?
