Prophecies of the Romans and Future Conquests
Nasafi presents two Quranic prophecies: Romans and future conquests.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how two Quranic prophecies—the Roman victory after defeat and the conquests of Persia and Mecca—were historically fulfilled and serve as evidence for prophethood.

Core Idea
Fulfilled predictions confirm the Prophet's truthfulness.

Imam al-Nasafi continues his argument from prophecy by presenting two more examples from the Quran. The first is the surprising prediction that the Romans would be victorious after being defeated, which came true. The second is the verse about showing signs in the horizons and within themselves, interpreted by scholars as the conquests of Persia and Mecca. Both were fulfilled exactly as foretold.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic and translation side by side. Notice how each prophecy is introduced with 'وكقوله تعالى' and ends with 'وكان كما أخبر'.
2
Identify the two prophecies
Find the first prophecy about the Romans (Surah Ar-Rum) and the second about signs in horizons and self (Surah Fussilat). Note the specific predictions.
3
Understand the interpretation
For the second prophecy, note that the verse is interpreted as future conquests rather than general signs of creation. The author cites the tafsir tradition.
4
Reflect on the argument
Ask: How do these fulfilled prophecies prove that Muhammad is a true prophet? Consider that only Allah knows the unseen future.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وكقوله تعالى: ( الم ٥ غُلِبَتِ الرُّومُ فِي أَدْنَى الْأَرْضِ وَهُمْ مِنْ بَعْدِ غَلَبِهِمْ سَيَغْلِبُونَ وكان كما أخبر. وكقوله تعالى: ﴿ سَنُرِيهِمْ آيَاتِنَا فِي الْآفَاقِ وَفِي أَنْفُسِهِمْ والمراد منه معنى في المستقبل بدلالة حرف السين، وقد أراهم الآيات الدالة على حدوثهم وثبوت الصانع الحكيم لهم في أنفسهم وفي الآفاق، فلم تكن الآية منصرفة إلى ذلك، وكان المراد ما قال أهل التأويل أن المراد بالآيات في الآفاق فتح الفرس، وفي أنفسهم فتح مكة، وكان كما أخبر. وكقوله تعالى لرسوله: إِنَّ الَّذِي فَرَضَ عَلَيْكَ الْقُرْآنَ لَرَادُّكَ إِلَى مَعَادٍ أي مكة، وقد رد إليها. وكقوله تعالى: هُوَ الَّذِي أَرْسَلَ رَسُولَهُ بِالْهُدَى وَدِينِ الْحَقِّ لِيُظْهِرَهُ عَلَى الدِّينِ كُلِّهِ وقد أظهره. وكقوله تعالى: وَعَدَ اللَّهُ الَّذِينَ آمَنُوا مِنْكُمْ وَعَمِلُوا الصَّالِحَاتِ لَيَسْتَخْلِفَنَّهُمْ فِي الْأَرْضِ الآية، والمراد من ذلك الصحابة بدلالة قوله تعالى: وَلَيُبَدِّلَنَّهُمْ مِنْ بَعْدِ خَوْفِهِمْ أَمْنًا وكانوا هم الخائفين في صدر الإسلام وقبل الهجرة وقد استخلفهم، وفي الآية دلالة على خلافة أبي بكر رضي الله عنه إذ لا يجوز أن يكون المستخلف مقهورا. وكقوله تعالى في شأن اليهود: قُلْ يَا أَيُّهَا الَّذِينَ هَادُوا إِنْ زَعَمْتُمْ أَنَّكُمْ أَوْلِيَاءُ لِلَّهِ مِنْ دُونِ النَّاسِ إلى أن قال: وَلَا يَتَمَنَّوْنَهُ أَبَدًا وكان كما أخبر، ولم يتمن أحد منهم الموت، وفي الآية دليل أنهم كانوا يعلمون صحة رسالته، وكانوا وجدوا ذكره في كتبهم حيث لم يتجاسروا على التمني.
And like His saying, exalted: 'Alif Lam Mim. The Romans have been defeated in the nearest land, and they, after their defeat, will be victorious' and it was as he informed. And like His saying, exalted: 'We will show them Our signs in the horizons and within themselves' and what is meant by it is a future meaning, indicated by the letter sin. And He showed them the signs indicating their origination and the establishment of the Wise Maker for them within themselves and in the horizons. So the verse was not referring to that, and what was meant was what the people of tafsir said: that what is meant by the signs in the horizons is the conquest of Persia, and within themselves is the conquest of Mecca, and it was as he informed. And like His saying, exalted, to His Messenger: 'Indeed, He who imposed the Quran upon you will surely return you to a place of return' meaning Mecca, and He returned him to it. And like His saying, exalted: 'It is He who sent His Messenger with guidance and the religion of truth to manifest it over all religion' and He manifested it. And like His saying, exalted: 'Allah has promised those who have believed among you and done righteous deeds that He will surely grant them succession upon the earth' the verse, and what is meant by that are the Companions, indicated by His saying, exalted: 'and He will surely substitute for them, after their fear, security' and they were the fearful ones in early Islam and before the Hijra, and He gave them succession. And in the verse there is an indication of the caliphate of Abu Bakr (may Allah be pleased with him), since it is not permissible for the one given succession to be overpowered. And like His saying, exalted, concerning the Jews: 'Say, O you who are Jews, if you claim that you are allies of Allah to the exclusion of the people' until He said: 'and they will not wish for it ever' and it was as he informed, and none of them wished for death. And in the verse there is evidence that they knew the truth of his message, and they found his mention in their books, where they did not dare to wish for death.
Source pages p. 736

Commentary
This passage continues the proof from future prophecies by giving more Quranic examples. The first example is the prophecy of the Romans' defeat and subsequent victory (Quran 30:1-3), which was fulfilled. The second is the verse 'We will show them Our signs in the horizons and within themselves' (Quran 41:53), interpreted by scholars as the conquest of Persia (horizons) and the conquest of Mecca (within themselves), and it was fulfilled. The third is the promise to return to Mecca (Quran 28:85), which was fulfilled when the Prophet conquered Mecca. The fourth is the promise that Islam would prevail over all religions (Quran 61:9), which was fulfilled. The fifth is the promise of succession and security for the believers (Quran 24:55), which was fulfilled with the caliphates, especially Abu Bakr's. The sixth is regarding the Jews: the verse challenging them to wish for death if they claim to be Allah's favorites (Quran 62:6-7); they never wished for death, proving they knew Muhammad was true, as they had his description in their scriptures.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the verse 'We will show them Our signs in the horizons and within themselves' refers only to general signs of creation, not specific future events.
Correction: Nasafi clarifies that the verse is about future prophecies, as indicated by the future tense, and scholars interpret it as the conquests of Persia and Mecca.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what did the scholars interpret 'آيَاتِنَا فِي الْآفَاقِ' to mean?
A) The conquest of Persia
B) The conquest of Mecca
C) The defeat of the Romans
D) The creation of the heavens and earth

Key Takeaway
The fulfillment of Quranic prophecies about the Romans and future conquests demonstrates that the Quran's knowledge of the unseen comes from Allah.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The Quran promised the Romans victory after defeat, and it happened. In your own life, what situation feels like a defeat right now? Are you willing to trust that Allah's promise of victory or relief is as certain as this prophecy? What would change in your daily actions if you truly believed that?
?
The signs in the horizons and within yourself include future victories. But the verse also says 'We will show them Our signs.' Have you seen Allah's signs in your own life and surroundings? What is one sign you have witnessed that left no doubt in your heart? If you cannot think of any, does that mean you have not been looking? Today, commit to noticing one sign of Allah's power or mercy before you sleep.
?
The conquest of Mecca was foretold before it happened. Allah knows the outcome of every struggle. When you strive for something good, do you worry about the result as if Allah does not know? Or do you work with certainty that the end is already written and good? Put your worry aside and name one struggle you will hand over to Allah's knowledge today.

Prophecies of Return to Mecca and Islam's Prevalence
Nasafi presents two prophecies: return to Mecca and Islam's prevalence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the prophecies of the Prophet's return to Mecca and Islam's dominance over all religions were fulfilled and serve as evidence for prophethood.

Core Idea
Divine promises about the Prophet's return and Islam's victory came true.

This passage presents two more Quranic prophecies: the promise that the Prophet would return to Mecca (his birthplace) after being forced to leave, and the promise that Islam would be made prevalent over all religions. Both were fulfilled exactly as foretold, providing clear evidence of the truth of his prophethood.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic and translation. Note the two prophecies introduced with 'وكقوله تعالى'.
2
Identify the prophecies
The first is from Surah Al-Qasas (28:85) about returning to 'ma'ad' (Mecca). The second is from Surah As-Saff (61:9) about manifesting Islam over all religions.
3
Confirm the fulfillments
Recall that the Prophet indeed returned to Mecca in the year of the conquest (8 AH) and that Islam spread rapidly, becoming dominant over other religions in Arabia and beyond.
4
Appreciate the argument
These predictions were made at a time when the Prophet was weak and outnumbered. Their fulfillment shows divine support.

Prophecies of Succession and the Jews' Death Wish
Nasafi presents prophecies of succession and Jewish death wish.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the prophecies of caliphate succession for the believers and the Jews' inability to wish for death serve as evidence for prophethood.

Core Idea
Future events about the community and the Jews' disbelief were foretold and fulfilled.

In this final part, Imam al-Nasafi presents two more powerful prophecies. The first is the promise of succession and security for the believers, which was fulfilled with the caliphate of Abu Bakr and the expansion of Islam. The second is the challenge to the Jews to wish for death if they are Allah's favorites, which they never did, proving their knowledge of the Prophet's truth.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic and translation. Notice the two separate prophecies: one about succession, one about the Jews.
2
Understand the succession prophecy
The verse (Quran 24:55) promises that believers will be made successors on earth and will have security. The author specifies this refers to the Companions and particularly to the caliphate of Abu Bakr.
The phrase 'لا يجوز أن يكون المستخلف مقهورا' argues that Abu Bakr was not overpowered, establishing his legitimate caliphate.
3
Reflect on the Jewish prophecy
The verse (Quran 62:6-7) challenges Jews to wish for death if they are Allah's favorites, but they never do. This shows they knew Muhammad was true and feared judgment.
4
Connect to the overall proof
Both prophecies were fulfilled in history and could not have been known by human guessing.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وكقوله تعالى: ( الم ٥ غُلِبَتِ الرُّومُ فِي أَدْنَى الْأَرْضِ وَهُمْ مِنْ بَعْدِ غَلَبِهِمْ سَيَغْلِبُونَ وكان كما أخبر. وكقوله تعالى: ﴿ سَنُرِيهِمْ آيَاتِنَا فِي الْآفَاقِ وَفِي أَنْفُسِهِمْ والمراد منه معنى في المستقبل بدلالة حرف السين، وقد أراهم الآيات الدالة على حدوثهم وثبوت الصانع الحكيم لهم في أنفسهم وفي الآفاق، فلم تكن الآية منصرفة إلى ذلك، وكان المراد ما قال أهل التأويل أن المراد بالآيات في الآفاق فتح الفرس، وفي أنفسهم فتح مكة، وكان كما أخبر. وكقوله تعالى لرسوله: إِنَّ الَّذِي فَرَضَ عَلَيْكَ الْقُرْآنَ لَرَادُّكَ إِلَى مَعَادٍ أي مكة، وقد رد إليها. وكقوله تعالى: هُوَ الَّذِي أَرْسَلَ رَسُولَهُ بِالْهُدَى وَدِينِ الْحَقِّ لِيُظْهِرَهُ عَلَى الدِّينِ كُلِّهِ وقد أظهره. وكقوله تعالى: وَعَدَ اللَّهُ الَّذِينَ آمَنُوا مِنْكُمْ وَعَمِلُوا الصَّالِحَاتِ لَيَسْتَخْلِفَنَّهُمْ فِي الْأَرْضِ الآية، والمراد من ذلك الصحابة بدلالة قوله تعالى: وَلَيُبَدِّلَنَّهُمْ مِنْ بَعْدِ خَوْفِهِمْ أَمْنًا وكانوا هم الخائفين في صدر الإسلام وقبل الهجرة وقد استخلفهم، وفي الآية دلالة على خلافة أبي بكر رضي الله عنه إذ لا يجوز أن يكون المستخلف مقهورا. وكقوله تعالى في شأن اليهود: قُلْ يَا أَيُّهَا الَّذِينَ هَادُوا إِنْ زَعَمْتُمْ أَنَّكُمْ أَوْلِيَاءُ لِلَّهِ مِنْ دُونِ النَّاسِ إلى أن قال: وَلَا يَتَمَنَّوْنَهُ أَبَدًا وكان كما أخبر، ولم يتمن أحد منهم الموت، وفي الآية دليل أنهم كانوا يعلمون صحة رسالته، وكانوا وجدوا ذكره في كتبهم حيث لم يتجاسروا على التمني.
And like His saying, exalted: 'Alif Lam Mim. The Romans have been defeated in the nearest land, and they, after their defeat, will be victorious' and it was as he informed. And like His saying, exalted: 'We will show them Our signs in the horizons and within themselves' and what is meant by it is a future meaning, indicated by the letter sin. And He showed them the signs indicating their origination and the establishment of the Wise Maker for them within themselves and in the horizons. So the verse was not referring to that, and what was meant was what the people of tafsir said: that what is meant by the signs in the horizons is the conquest of Persia, and within themselves is the conquest of Mecca, and it was as he informed. And like His saying, exalted, to His Messenger: 'Indeed, He who imposed the Quran upon you will surely return you to a place of return' meaning Mecca, and He returned him to it. And like His saying, exalted: 'It is He who sent His Messenger with guidance and the religion of truth to manifest it over all religion' and He manifested it. And like His saying, exalted: 'Allah has promised those who have believed among you and done righteous deeds that He will surely grant them succession upon the earth' the verse, and what is meant by that are the Companions, indicated by His saying, exalted: 'and He will surely substitute for them, after their fear, security' and they were the fearful ones in early Islam and before the Hijra, and He gave them succession. And in the verse there is an indication of the caliphate of Abu Bakr (may Allah be pleased with him), since it is not permissible for the one given succession to be overpowered. And like His saying, exalted, concerning the Jews: 'Say, O you who are Jews, if you claim that you are allies of Allah to the exclusion of the people' until He said: 'and they will not wish for it ever' and it was as he informed, and none of them wished for death. And in the verse there is evidence that they knew the truth of his message, and they found his mention in their books, where they did not dare to wish for death.
Source pages p. 736

Commentary
This passage continues the proof from future prophecies by giving more Quranic examples. The first example is the prophecy of the Romans' defeat and subsequent victory (Quran 30:1-3), which was fulfilled. The second is the verse 'We will show them Our signs in the horizons and within themselves' (Quran 41:53), interpreted by scholars as the conquest of Persia (horizons) and the conquest of Mecca (within themselves), and it was fulfilled. The third is the promise to return to Mecca (Quran 28:85), which was fulfilled when the Prophet conquered Mecca. The fourth is the promise that Islam would prevail over all religions (Quran 61:9), which was fulfilled. The fifth is the promise of succession and security for the believers (Quran 24:55), which was fulfilled with the caliphates, especially Abu Bakr's. The sixth is regarding the Jews: the verse challenging them to wish for death if they claim to be Allah's favorites (Quran 62:6-7); they never wished for death, proving they knew Muhammad was true, as they had his description in their scriptures.

خوف
أمن
خلافة
أبو بكر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that the Jews simply ignored the challenge, but the author argues their failure itself is evidence of their knowledge.
Correction: The passage states that the Jews did not dare to wish for death because they knew the Prophet's truth from their scriptures, making their inaction a fulfillment of the prophecy.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what does the Jews' failure to wish for death indicate?
A) They were not serious about their claim
B) They knew Muhammad was a true prophet
C) They did not read the Quran
D) They preferred life over death

Key Takeaway
The precise fulfillment of prophecies about succession and the Jews' behavior demonstrates the divine origin of Islam and the truth of Muhammad's prophethood.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You have just read that the Jews knew the truth of Muhammad's prophethood from their scriptures but did not act. Where in your own life do you know something is true from Allah but hesitate to embrace it fully? What fear drives that hesitation, and what would it cost you to act on that truth today?
?
The Companions moved from fear to security through trust in Allah's promise. In what area of your life are you still living in fear—whether of failure, people, or the future—instead of trusting Allah's guarantee of succession and security? What is one concrete step you can take this week to replace that fear with faith?
?
If Allah challenged you to wish for death to prove your sincerity, would you dare? What does your honest answer reveal about the strength of your certainty in His promise? How can you strengthen that certainty starting today?

Prophethood
beginner

Predictions of Conquest: Romans, Persia, and Mecca
Two fulfilled predictions: Romans' victory and conquests of Persia and Mecca.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Quran's predictions of the Romans' victory and the conquests of Persia and Mecca confirm Muhammad's prophethood.

Core Idea
Fulfilled predictions prove that the Quran's knowledge is divine.

Nasafi begins by presenting two concrete examples of Quranic predictions that came true exactly as foretold. The first is the well-known prophecy of the Romans' victory after defeat; the second is the interpretation of the 'signs in the horizons' as the conquest of Persia and Mecca. These examples establish a pattern: the Quran's specific, verifiable predictions could not have been guesswork, and they point directly to divine revelation.

Guided Path
1
Read the two predictions
Carefully read the Arabic and translation for the Romans verse and the horizons verse. Notice the specific wording and the author's claim that each was fulfilled.
The Romans prediction is famously cited as a miracle of the Quran.
2
Understand the logical inference
Ask yourself: Why does the fulfillment of these predictions prove prophethood? The author implies that only Allah could know such future events with certainty.
This is a standard argument in Islamic theology known as dalāʾil al-nubuwwa.
3
Reflect on the second prediction
Note how the verse about 'signs in the horizons and in themselves' is interpreted specifically as the conquests. This shows that the Quran's meanings are not vague but point to actual historical events.
The author cites 'people of interpretation' to ground his reading.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

ٱلْءَافَاقِ وَفِىٓ أَنفُسِهِمْ﴾ وَالْمُرَادُ مِنْهُ مَعْنًى فِى الْمُسْتَقْبَلِ بِدَلَالَةِ حَرْفِ السِّينِ وَقَدْ أَرَاهُمُ الْآيَاتِ الدَّالَّةَ عَلَى حُدُوثِهِمْ وَثُبُوتِ الصَّانِعِ الْحَكِيمِ إِلَيْهَا. وَكَقَوْلِهِ تَعَالَى: ﴿هُوَ الَّذِىٓ أَرْسَلَ رَسُولَهُۥ بِالْهُدَىٰ وَدِينِ الْحَقِّ لِيُظْهِرَهُۥ عَلَى ٱلدِّينِ كُلِّهِۦ﴾ وَقَدْ أَظْهَرَهُ. وَكَقَوْلِهِ تَعَالَى: ﴿وَعَدَ ٱللَّهُ ٱلَّذِينَ ءَامَنُوا۟ مِنكُمْ وَعَمِلُوا۟ ٱلصَّٰلِحَٰتِ لَيَسْتَخْلِفَنَّهُمْ فِى ٱلْأَرْضِ﴾ الْآيَةَ وَالْمُرَادُ مِن ذَٰلِكَ الصَّحَابَةُ بِدَلَالَةِ قَوْلِهِ تَعَالَى: ﴿وَلَيُبَدِّلَنَّهُم مِّنۢ ٱلنَّاسِ﴾ إِلَىٰٓ أَن قَالَ: ﴿وَلَا يَتَمَنَّوْنَهُۥٓ أَبَدًا﴾ وَكَانَ كَمَا أَخْبَرَ، وَلَمْ يَتَمَنَّ أَحَدٌ مِّنْهُمُ الْمَوْتَ، وَفِى الْآيَةِ دَلِيلٌ أَنَّهُمْ كَانُوا۟ يَعْلَمُونَ صِحَّةَ رِسَالَتِهِ، وَكَانُوا۟ وَجَدُوا۟ ذِكْرَهُ فِى كُتُبِهِمْ حَيْثُ لَمْ يَتَجَاسَرُوا۟ عَلَى التَّمَنِّى لَوْلَا ذَٰلِكَ لَفَعَلُوا۟ إِظْهَارًا لِخَلَفِهِ. ثُمَّ قَالَ تَعَالَى فِى الْيَهُودِ: ﴿ضُرِبَتْ وَلَا ثَبَتَ لَهُمْ سُلْطَانٌ، وَكَانَتْ أَمَارَةُ الذُّلِّ وَالصَّغَارِ وَالْمَسْكَنَةِ عَلَيْهِمْ بَادِيَةً، وَعَلَامَةُ السَّخَطِ وَاللَّعْنَةِ ظَاهِرَةً وَإِنْ كَانُوا۟ يَرْجِعُونَ إِلَى ثَرْوَةٍ مِّنَ الْمَالِ وَكَثْرَةٍ مِّنَ الْعُدَّةِ وَالْعَتَادِ.
And like His statement, the Exalted: (Alif Lam Meem. The Romans have been defeated in the nearest land, and they, after their defeat, will overcome) and it was as He informed. And like His statement, the Exalted: (We will show them Our signs in the horizons and in themselves) and the intended meaning from it is a meaning in the future, indicated by the letter sin (future tense), and He showed them the signs indicating their originatedness and the existence of the Wise Maker for them in themselves and in the horizons, so the verse was not directed to that, and the intended meaning was what the people of interpretation said: that the intended meaning by the signs in the horizons is the conquest of Persia, and in themselves is the conquest of Mecca, and it was as He informed. And like His statement, the Exalted, to His Messenger: (Indeed, He who imposed upon you the Qur'an will surely return you to a place of return) i.e., Mecca, and He returned him to it. And like His statement, the Exalted: (He is the One who sent His Messenger with guidance and the religion of truth to make it prevail over all religion) and He has made it prevail. And like His statement, the Exalted: (Allah has promised those who have believed among you and done righteous deeds that He will surely grant them succession upon the earth) the verse, and the intended by that are the Companions, as indicated by His statement, the Exalted: (And He will surely substitute for them, after their fear, security) and they were the fearful ones in the early days of Islam and before the Hijrah, and they were given succession, and in the verse is an indication of the caliphate of Abu Bakr, may Allah be pleased with him, since it is not permissible for the one given succession to be overcome. And like His statement, the Exalted, concerning the Jews: (Say, O you who are Jews, if you claim that you are allies of Allah, excluding the people) until He said: (And they will not wish for it ever) and it was as He informed, and none of them wished for death, and in the verse is proof that they knew the truth of his message, and they had found his mention in their scriptures, because they did not dare to wish for it; if not for that, they would have done so to show [that] his information was false. Then He said, the Exalted, concerning the Jews: (Humiliation has been imposed upon them wherever they are found, except through a rope from Allah) and the confirmation of this among the Jews is clear in every age and region; since no banner has been raised for them since that day, nor has any authority been established for them, and the mark of humiliation, degradation and abasement is evident upon them, and the sign of wrath and curse is apparent, even if they possess wealth and numerous equipment and armaments.
Source pages p. 736

Commentary
This passage is a proof of prophethood from predictions (akhbār bil-ghayb). The author lists several Quranic verses that contain predictions of future events that came true. Each example shows that the Quran's information about the future could not have come from human knowledge and thus confirms Muhammad's prophethood. The author begins with the Romans' victory (Sūrat al-Rūm), then the general verse about showing signs (Sūrat Fuṣṣilat), interpreted as specific future conquests. Then he mentions the promise of return to Mecca (Sūrat al-Qaṣaṣ), the dominance of Islam (Sūrat al-Ṣaff), the promise of caliphate (Sūrat al-Nūr) which he links to the caliphate of Abu Bakr (may Allah be pleased with him), and finally two verses about the Jews: their unwillingness to wish for death (Sūrat al-Jumuʿah) and their perpetual humiliation (Sūrat Āl ʿImrān). The author explains each verse's fulfillment as clear historical fact, reinforcing the argument that prophethood is proven through fulfilled prophecy.

Key Terms
إخبار بالغيب (akhbār bil-ghayb)
غُلِبَتِ الرُّومُ (ghulibat al-rūm)
الآيات في الآفاق (al-āyāt fī l-āfāq)
فتح الفرس (fatḥ al-furs)
فتح مكة (fatḥ makka)

Checkpoint
According to the author, what does the 'signs in the horizons' (Sūrat Fuṣṣilat) predict?
A) The creation of the universe
B) The conquest of Persia and the conquest of Mecca
C) The coming of the Day of Judgment
D) The defeat of the Romans

Key Takeaway
Specific, independently verifiable predictions like the Romans' victory and the conquest of Persia and Mecca demonstrate that the Quran's source is divine, not human.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The Quran foretold the Romans' victory and the conquests of Persia and Mecca with such precision that no human could have guessed. In what area of your life are you ignoring or downplaying the Quran's clear promises or warnings? What would it take for you to treat them as seriously as you treat proven historical facts?
?
These prophecies were fulfilled within the lifetime of the early Muslims, strengthening their faith. Has Allah shown you any sign—big or small—that confirms His guidance in your life? If so, why do you still doubt or hesitate in following His commands?
?
The conquest of Mecca was a sign 'in themselves'—something the early Muslims personally witnessed and benefited from. What signs has Allah placed in your own life or community that you have taken for granted? How can you turn that awareness into a deeper commitment to His message today?

Prophethood

Return to Mecca and Global Dominance
Two fulfilled predictions: return to Mecca and Islam's global dominance.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the prophecies of Muhammad's return to Mecca and the global spread of Islam serve as proofs of his prophethood.

Core Idea
Two more political/military predictions: return home and ultimate victory.

Nasafi continues his list of fulfilled predictions with two closely related examples: the promise that Muhammad would return to Mecca, and the promise that Islam would prevail over all other religions. Both were fulfilled within his lifetime or shortly after. These predictions are striking because at the time they were revealed, the Muslims were a small persecuted community with no political power.

Guided Path
1
Read the two verses
Read the Arabic and translation. Note that the first verse promises return to 'a place of return' (interpreted as Mecca), and the second promises dominance of Islam.
2
Consider the context
Think about the situation when these verses were revealed: Muhammad was in Medina, having been forced to leave Mecca. The Muslims were still vulnerable. Yet the Quran predicts his safe return and the global spread of Islam.
This context makes the predictions more powerful.
3
Reflect on the mechanism
Ask yourself: How does the author use these fulfilled predictions to build his argument? He simply states 'and He returned him to it' and 'and He has made it prevail', implying that the fulfillment is historical fact.
The author trusts that the reader knows these events occurred.

وَكَقَوْلِهِ تَعَالَى: (الٓمٓ غُلِبَتِ الرُّومُ فِيٓ أَدْنَى الْأَرْضِ وَهُم مِّنۢ بَعْدِ غَلَبِهِمْ سَيَغْلِبُونَ) وَكَانَ كَمَا أَخْبَرَ. وَكَقَوْلِهِ تَعَالَى: ﴿سَنُرِيهِمْ ءَايَٰتِنَا فِى ٱلْءَافَاقِ وَفِىٓ أَنفُسِهِمْ﴾ وَالْمُرَادُ مِنْهُ مَعْنًى فِى الْمُسْتَقْبَلِ بِدَلَالَةِ حَرْفِ السِّينِ وَقَدْ أَرَاهُمُ الْآيَاتِ الدَّالَّةَ عَلَى حُدُوثِهِمْ وَثُبُوتِ الصَّانِعِ الْحَكِيمِ لَهُمْ فِى أَنفُسِهِمْ وَفِى الْآفَاقِ فَلَمْ تَكُنِ الْآيَةُ مُنْصَرِفَةً إِلَى ذَٰلِكَ، وَكَانَ الْمُرَادُ مَا قَالَ أَهْلُ التَّأْوِيلِ أَنَّ الْمُرَادَ بِالْآيَاتِ فِى الْآفَاقِ فَتْحُ الْفُرْسِ، وَفِىٓ أَنفُسِهِمْ فَتْحُ مَكَّةَ، وَكَانَ كَمَا أَخْبَرَ. وَكَقَوْلِهِ تَعَالَى لِرَسُولِهِ: ﴿إِنَّ الَّذِى فَرَضَ عَلَيْكَ الْقُرْءَانَ لَرَآدُّكَ إِلَىٰ مَعَادٍ﴾ أَىْ مَكَّةَ. وَقَدْ رَدَّ إِلَيْهَا. وَكَقَوْلِهِ تَعَالَى: ﴿هُوَ الَّذِىٓ أَرْسَلَ رَسُولَهُۥ بِالْهُدَىٰ وَدِينِ الْحَقِّ لِيُظْهِرَهُۥ عَلَى ٱلدِّينِ كُلِّهِۦ﴾ وَقَدْ أَظْهَرَهُ. وَكَقَوْلِهِ تَعَالَى: ﴿وَعَدَ ٱللَّهُ ٱلَّذِينَ ءَامَنُوا۟ مِنكُمْ وَعَمِلُوا۟ ٱلصَّٰلِحَٰتِ لَيَسْتَخْلِفَنَّهُمْ فِى ٱلْأَرْضِ﴾ الْآيَةَ وَالْمُرَادُ مِن ذَٰلِكَ الصَّحَابَةُ بِدَلَالَةِ قَوْلِهِ تَعَالَى: ﴿وَلَيُبَدِّلَنَّهُم مِّنۢ بَعْدِ خَوْفِهِمْ أَمْنًا﴾ وَكَانُوا۟ هُمُ الْخَائِفِينَ فِى صَدْرِ الْإِسْلَامِ وَقَبْلَ الْهِجْرَةِ وَقَدِ اسْتُخْلِفُوا۟، وَفِى الْآيَةِ دَلَالَةٌ عَلَى خِلَافَةِ أَبِى بَكْرٍ رَضِىَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُ إِذْ لَا يَجُوزُ أَنْ يَكُونَ الْمُسْتَخْلَفُ مَقْهُورًا. وَكَقَوْلِهِ تَعَالَى فِى شَأْنِ الْيَهُودِ: ﴿قُلْ يَٰٓأَيُّهَا ٱلَّذِينَ هَادُوٓا۟ إِن زَعَمْتُمْ أَنَّكُمْ أَوْلِيَآءُ لِلَّهِ مِن دُونِ ٱلنَّاسِ﴾ إِلَىٰٓ أَن قَالَ: ﴿وَلَا يَتَمَنَّوْنَهُۥٓ أَبَدًا﴾ وَكَانَ كَمَا أَخْبَرَ، وَلَمْ يَتَمَنَّ أَحَدٌ مِّنْهُمُ الْمَوْتَ، وَفِى الْآيَةِ دَلِيلٌ أَنَّهُمْ كَانُوا۟ يَعْلَمُونَ صِحَّةَ رِسَالَتِهِ، وَكَانُوا۟ وَجَدُوا۟ ذِكْرَهُ فِى كُتُبِهِمْ حَيْثُ لَمْ يَتَجَاسَرُوا۟ عَلَى التَّمَنِّى لَوْلَا ذَٰلِكَ لَفَعَلُوا۟ إِظْهَارًا لِخَلَفِهِ. ثُمَّ قَالَ تَعَالَى فِى الْيَهُودِ: ﴿ضُرِبَتْ عَلَيْهِمُ ٱلذِّلَّةُ أَيْنَ مَا ثُقِفُوٓا۟ إِلَّا بِحَبْلٍ مِّنَ ٱللَّهِ﴾ وَمِصْدَاقُ هَٰذَا فِى الْيَهُودِ بَيِّنٌ فِى كُلِّ عَصْرٍ وَمِصْرٍ؛ إِذْ لَمْ تُرْفَعْ لَهُمْ رَايَةٌ مُنْذُ يَوْمَئِذٍ، وَلَا ثَبَتَ لَهُمْ سُلْطَانٌ، وَكَانَتْ أَمَارَةُ الذُّلِّ وَالصَّغَارِ وَالْمَسْكَنَةِ عَلَيْهِمْ بَادِيَةً، وَعَلَامَةُ السَّخَطِ وَاللَّعْنَةِ ظَاهِرَةً وَإِنْ كَانُوا۟ يَرْجِعُونَ إِلَى ثَرْوَةٍ مِّنَ الْمَالِ وَكَثْرَةٍ مِّنَ الْعُدَّةِ وَالْعَتَادِ.
And like His statement, the Exalted: (Alif Lam Meem. The Romans have been defeated in the nearest land, and they, after their defeat, will overcome) and it was as He informed. And like His statement, the Exalted: (We will show them Our signs in the horizons and in themselves) and the intended meaning from it is a meaning in the future, indicated by the letter sin (future tense), and He showed them the signs indicating their originatedness and the existence of the Wise Maker for them in themselves and in the horizons, so the verse was not directed to that, and the intended meaning was what the people of interpretation said: that the intended meaning by the signs in the horizons is the conquest of Persia, and in themselves is the conquest of Mecca, and it was as He informed. And like His statement, the Exalted, to His Messenger: (Indeed, He who imposed upon you the Qur'an will surely return you to a place of return) i.e., Mecca, and He returned him to it. And like His statement, the Exalted: (He is the One who sent His Messenger with guidance and the religion of truth to make it prevail over all religion) and He has made it prevail. And like His statement, the Exalted: (Allah has promised those who have believed among you and done righteous deeds that He will surely grant them succession upon the earth) the verse, and the intended by that are the Companions, as indicated by His statement, the Exalted: (And He will surely substitute for them, after their fear, security) and they were the fearful ones in the early days of Islam and before the Hijrah, and they were given succession, and in the verse is an indication of the caliphate of Abu Bakr, may Allah be pleased with him, since it is not permissible for the one given succession to be overcome. And like His statement, the Exalted, concerning the Jews: (Say, O you who are Jews, if you claim that you are allies of Allah, excluding the people) until He said: (And they will not wish for it ever) and it was as He informed, and none of them wished for death, and in the verse is proof that they knew the truth of his message, and they had found his mention in their scriptures, because they did not dare to wish for it; if not for that, they would have done so to show [that] his information was false. Then He said, the Exalted, concerning the Jews: (Humiliation has been imposed upon them wherever they are found, except through a rope from Allah) and the confirmation of this among the Jews is clear in every age and region; since no banner has been raised for them since that day, nor has any authority been established for them, and the mark of humiliation, degradation and abasement is evident upon them, and the sign of wrath and curse is apparent, even if they possess wealth and numerous equipment and armaments.
Source pages p. 736

Commentary
This passage is a proof of prophethood from predictions (akhbār bil-ghayb). The author lists several Quranic verses that contain predictions of future events that came true. Each example shows that the Quran's information about the future could not have come from human knowledge and thus confirms Muhammad's prophethood. The author begins with the Romans' victory (Sūrat al-Rūm), then the general verse about showing signs (Sūrat Fuṣṣilat), interpreted as specific future conquests. Then he mentions the promise of return to Mecca (Sūrat al-Qaṣaṣ), the dominance of Islam (Sūrat al-Ṣaff), the promise of caliphate (Sūrat al-Nūr) which he links to the caliphate of Abu Bakr (may Allah be pleased with him), and finally two verses about the Jews: their unwillingness to wish for death (Sūrat al-Jumuʿah) and their perpetual humiliation (Sūrat Āl ʿImrān). The author explains each verse's fulfillment as clear historical fact, reinforcing the argument that prophethood is proven through fulfilled prophecy.

Key Terms
معاد (maʿād)
أظهره على الدين كله (aẓharahu ʿalā l-dīn kullihi)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What does the author identify as 'a place of return' (مَعَاد) in the verse from Sūrat al-Qaṣaṣ?
A) Paradise
B) Medina
C) Mecca
D) The grave

Key Takeaway
The promises of Muhammad's return to Mecca and Islam's ultimate prevalence were unlikely at the time but came true, reinforcing the divine origin of the Quran.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The Prophet endured years of persecution, trusting Allah's promise to return to Mecca. What painful situation are you facing right now that requires you to trust a specific promise from Allah? Write down one actionable step you can take this week to act on that trust.
?
If Islam's eventual global dominance is as certain as the return to Mecca, why do you sometimes feel hopeless when you see the state of Muslims today? What can you do today to strengthen your conviction in Allah's promise?
?
The Prophet’s return to Mecca was a peaceful conquest. In your own life, are you seeking to 'return' to Allah in a way that brings peace and reconciliation, or are you forcing things through aggression? How can you embody the Prophet’s example of magnanimity in victory?

Prophethood
intermediate
6 min
The Caliphate Prediction and Abu Bakr
Prediction of caliphate and its specific application to Abu Bakr.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Quranic promise of caliphate for the believers, especially its realization in the caliphate of Abu Bakr, serves as a proof of prophethood.

Core Idea
A specific political succession predicted and fulfilled.

Nasafi now cites a verse from Sūrat al-Nūr that promises the believers succession and security after fear. He interprets this as a prediction specifically about the Companions, and he finds in it a subtle indication of Abu Bakr's caliphate. This example shows that the Quran's predictions extend beyond immediate events to the future leadership of the community.

Guided Path
1
Read the verse and interpretation
Read the Arabic: Allah promises to grant succession (istikhlāf) and replace fear with security. The author says this refers to the Companions, who were fearful before the Hijrah.
The verse is Sūrat al-Nūr 24:55.
2
Understand the link to Abu Bakr
The author argues that the one given succession (the caliph) cannot be overcome or defeated. This implies that the first caliph, Abu Bakr, who was never conquered, is the intended referent.
This is an indirect proof that the prediction points to Abu Bakr.
3
Evaluate the argument
Consider how this deduction works: the promise of succession is general for all believers, but the author sees a specific implication for Abu Bakr's rightful caliphate.
This also touches on theological debates about the caliphate.

بَعْدِ خَوْفِهِمْ أَمْنًا﴾ وَكَانُوا۟ هُمُ الْخَائِفِينَ فِى صَدْرِ الْإِسْلَامِ وَقَبْلَ الْهِجْرَةِ وَقَدِ اسْتُخْلِفُوا۟، وَفِى الْآيَةِ دَلَالَةٌ عَلَى خِلَافَةِ أَبِى بَكْرٍ رَضِىَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُ ٱلنَّاسِ﴾ إِلَىٰٓ أَن قَالَ: ﴿وَلَا يَتَمَنَّوْنَهُۥٓ أَبَدًا﴾ وَكَانَ كَمَا أَخْبَرَ، وَلَمْ يَتَمَنَّ أَحَدٌ مِّنْهُمُ الْمَوْتَ، وَفِى الْآيَةِ دَلِيلٌ أَنَّهُمْ كَانُوا۟ يَعْلَمُونَ صِحَّةَ رِسَالَتِهِ، وَكَانُوا۟ وَجَدُوا۟ ذِكْرَهُ فِى كُتُبِهِمْ حَيْثُ لَمْ يَتَجَاسَرُوا۟ عَلَى التَّمَنِّى لَوْلَا ذَٰلِكَ لَفَعَلُوا۟ إِظْهَارًا لِخَلَفِهِ. ثُمَّ قَالَ تَعَالَى فِى الْيَهُودِ: ﴿ضُرِبَتْ عَلَيْهِمُ ٱلذِّلَّةُ أَيْنَ مَا ثُقِفُوٓا۟ إِلَّا بِحَبْلٍ مِّنَ ٱللَّهِ﴾ وَمِصْدَاقُ هَٰذَا فِى الْيَهُودِ بَيِّنٌ فِى كُلِّ عَصْرٍ وَمِصْرٍ؛ إِذْ لَمْ تُرْفَعْ لَهُمْ رَايَةٌ مُنْذُ يَوْمَئِذٍ، وَلَا ثَبَتَ لَهُمْ سُلْطَانٌ، وَكَانَتْ أَمَارَةُ الذُّلِّ وَالصَّغَارِ وَالْمَسْكَنَةِ عَلَيْهِمْ بَادِيَةً، وَعَلَامَةُ السَّخَطِ وَاللَّعْنَةِ ظَاهِرَةً وَإِنْ كَانُوا۟ يَرْجِعُونَ إِلَى ثَرْوَةٍ مِّنَ الْمَالِ وَكَثْرَةٍ مِّنَ الْعُدَّةِ وَالْعَتَادِ.
And like His statement, the Exalted: (Alif Lam Meem. The Romans have been defeated in the nearest land, and they, after their defeat, will overcome) and it was as He informed. And like His statement, the Exalted: (We will show them Our signs in the horizons and in themselves) and the intended meaning from it is a meaning in the future, indicated by the letter sin (future tense), and He showed them the signs indicating their originatedness and the existence of the Wise Maker for them in themselves and in the horizons, so the verse was not directed to that, and the intended meaning was what the people of interpretation said: that the intended meaning by the signs in the horizons is the conquest of Persia, and in themselves is the conquest of Mecca, and it was as He informed. And like His statement, the Exalted, to His Messenger: (Indeed, He who imposed upon you the Qur'an will surely return you to a place of return) i.e., Mecca, and He returned him to it. And like His statement, the Exalted: (He is the One who sent His Messenger with guidance and the religion of truth to make it prevail over all religion) and He has made it prevail. And like His statement, the Exalted: (Allah has promised those who have believed among you and done righteous deeds that He will surely grant them succession upon the earth) the verse, and the intended by that are the Companions, as indicated by His statement, the Exalted: (And He will surely substitute for them, after their fear, security) and they were the fearful ones in the early days of Islam and before the Hijrah, and they were given succession, and in the verse is an indication of the caliphate of Abu Bakr, may Allah be pleased with him, since it is not permissible for the one given succession to be overcome. And like His statement, the Exalted, concerning the Jews: (Say, O you who are Jews, if you claim that you are allies of Allah, excluding the people) until He said: (And they will not wish for it ever) and it was as He informed, and none of them wished for death, and in the verse is proof that they knew the truth of his message, and they had found his mention in their scriptures, because they did not dare to wish for it; if not for that, they would have done so to show [that] his information was false. Then He said, the Exalted, concerning the Jews: (Humiliation has been imposed upon them wherever they are found, except through a rope from Allah) and the confirmation of this among the Jews is clear in every age and region; since no banner has been raised for them since that day, nor has any authority been established for them, and the mark of humiliation, degradation and abasement is evident upon them, and the sign of wrath and curse is apparent, even if they possess wealth and numerous equipment and armaments.

Commentary
This passage is a proof of prophethood from predictions (akhbār bil-ghayb). The author lists several Quranic verses that contain predictions of future events that came true. Each example shows that the Quran's information about the future could not have come from human knowledge and thus confirms Muhammad's prophethood. The author begins with the Romans' victory (Sūrat al-Rūm), then the general verse about showing signs (Sūrat Fuṣṣilat), interpreted as specific future conquests. Then he mentions the promise of return to Mecca (Sūrat al-Qaṣaṣ), the dominance of Islam (Sūrat al-Ṣaff), the promise of caliphate (Sūrat al-Nūr) which he links to the caliphate of Abu Bakr (may Allah be pleased with him), and finally two verses about the Jews: their unwillingness to wish for death (Sūrat al-Jumuʿah) and their perpetual humiliation (Sūrat Āl ʿImrān). The author explains each verse's fulfillment as clear historical fact, reinforcing the argument that prophethood is proven through fulfilled prophecy.

Key Terms
الاستخلاف (al-istikhlāf)
خلافة أبي بكر (khilāfat Abī Bakr)
مقهور (maqhūr)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think the caliphate prediction refers only to general leadership, not to a specific person.
Correction: The author draws a specific implication for Abu Bakr by reasoning that the successor cannot be defeated, which Abu Bakr was not.

Checkpoint
According to the author, what indicates that the verse about succession refers to the Companions specifically?
A) The mention of 'righteous deeds'
B) The reference to fear and subsequent security
C) The phrase 'on the earth'
D) The use of the word 'promised'

Key Takeaway
The Quran's promise of caliphate was fulfilled in the early Islamic caliphate, and the author finds a specific proof for Abu Bakr's rightful succession.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
This verse shows that Allah's promises are fulfilled with precision. Is there a promise of Allah you are struggling to trust? What would change in your daily life if you truly believed it will come to pass exactly as He said?
?
The caliph must not be overcome. In what areas of your life are you allowing yourself to be subdued by your lower desires, fear of people, or worldly concerns rather than standing firm as a successor of Allah on earth?
?
The Companions transformed from fear to security through faith and righteous deeds. What specific fear holds you back from fulfilling your role as a successor? What one righteous deed can you commit to today to begin that transformation?

Predictions About the Jews: Death Wish and Humiliation
Two fulfilled predictions about Jewish disbelief and social state.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Quran's predictions about the Jews' unwillingness to wish for death and their perpetual humiliation serve as additional proofs of Muhammad's prophethood.

Core Idea
Two social/religious predictions about the Jewish community that came true.

Nasafi concludes his list with two predictions concerning the Jews. The first is the challenge that the Jews would never genuinely wish for death, proving they knew Muhammad was true. The second is the decree that humiliation would be their lot, which has been historically evident. These examples show that the Quran's predictions cover not only political events but also the inner states and societal conditions of specific groups.

Guided Path
1
Read the two Jewish predictions
Read the Arabic: first, the verse challenging the Jews to wish for death if they are allies of Allah; second, the verse declaring humiliation upon them. Note the author's comments on their fulfillment.
2
Analyze the first prediction
The author argues that the Jews' failure to wish for death is a proof that they knew Muhammad was a true prophet. If they were truly Allah's allies, they would have welcomed death to reach paradise, but they did not dare because they knew he spoke the truth.
This is a psychological and theological argument.
3
Analyze the second prediction
The author points to the historical and ongoing humiliation of the Jewish people, despite their wealth and resources, as a clear sign of the Quranic prophecy.
This prediction is seen as a permanent condition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَكَقَوْلِهِ تَعَالَى: (الٓمٓ غُلِبَتِ الرُّومُ فِيٓ أَدْنَى الْأَرْضِ وَهُم مِّنۢ بَعْدِ غَلَبِهِمْ سَيَغْلِبُونَ) وَكَانَ كَمَا أَخْبَرَ. وَكَقَوْلِهِ تَعَالَى: ﴿سَنُرِيهِمْ ءَايَٰتِنَا فِى ٱلْءَافَاقِ وَفِىٓ أَنفُسِهِمْ﴾ وَالْمُرَادُ مِنْهُ مَعْنًى فِى الْمُسْتَقْبَلِ بِدَلَالَةِ حَرْفِ السِّينِ وَقَدْ أَرَاهُمُ الْآيَاتِ الدَّالَّةَ عَلَى حُدُوثِهِمْ وَثُبُوتِ الصَّانِعِ الْحَكِيمِ لَهُمْ فِى أَنفُسِهِمْ وَفِى الْآفَاقِ فَلَمْ تَكُنِ الْآيَةُ مُنْصَرِفَةً إِلَى ذَٰلِكَ، وَكَانَ الْمُرَادُ مَا قَالَ أَهْلُ التَّأْوِيلِ أَنَّ الْمُرَادَ بِالْآيَاتِ فِى الْآفَاقِ فَتْحُ الْفُرْسِ، وَفِىٓ أَنفُسِهِمْ فَتْحُ مَكَّةَ، وَكَانَ كَمَا أَخْبَرَ. وَكَقَوْلِهِ تَعَالَى لِرَسُولِهِ: ﴿إِنَّ الَّذِى فَرَضَ عَلَيْكَ الْقُرْءَانَ لَرَآدُّكَ إِلَىٰ مَعَادٍ﴾ أَىْ مَكَّةَ. وَقَدْ رَدَّ إِلَيْهَا. وَكَقَوْلِهِ تَعَالَى: ﴿هُوَ الَّذِىٓ أَرْسَلَ رَسُولَهُۥ بِالْهُدَىٰ وَدِينِ الْحَقِّ لِيُظْهِرَهُۥ عَلَى ٱلدِّينِ كُلِّهِۦ﴾ وَقَدْ أَظْهَرَهُ. وَكَقَوْلِهِ تَعَالَى: ﴿وَعَدَ ٱللَّهُ ٱلَّذِينَ ءَامَنُوا۟ مِنكُمْ وَعَمِلُوا۟ ٱلصَّٰلِحَٰتِ لَيَسْتَخْلِفَنَّهُمْ فِى ٱلْأَرْضِ﴾ الْآيَةَ وَالْمُرَادُ مِن ذَٰلِكَ الصَّحَابَةُ بِدَلَالَةِ قَوْلِهِ تَعَالَى: ﴿وَلَيُبَدِّلَنَّهُم مِّنۢ بَعْدِ خَوْفِهِمْ أَمْنًا﴾ وَكَانُوا۟ هُمُ الْخَائِفِينَ فِى صَدْرِ الْإِسْلَامِ وَقَبْلَ الْهِجْرَةِ وَقَدِ اسْتُخْلِفُوا۟، وَفِى الْآيَةِ دَلَالَةٌ عَلَى خِلَافَةِ أَبِى بَكْرٍ رَضِىَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُ إِذْ لَا يَجُوزُ أَنْ يَكُونَ الْمُسْتَخْلَفُ مَقْهُورًا. وَكَقَوْلِهِ تَعَالَى فِى شَأْنِ الْيَهُودِ: ﴿قُلْ يَٰٓأَيُّهَا ٱلَّذِينَ هَادُوٓا۟ إِن زَعَمْتُمْ أَنَّكُمْ أَوْلِيَآءُ لِلَّهِ مِن دُونِ ٱلنَّاسِ﴾ إِلَىٰٓ أَن قَالَ: ﴿وَلَا يَتَمَنَّوْنَهُۥٓ أَبَدًا﴾ وَكَانَ كَمَا أَخْبَرَ، وَلَمْ يَتَمَنَّ أَحَدٌ مِّنْهُمُ الْمَوْتَ، وَفِى الْآيَةِ دَلِيلٌ أَنَّهُمْ كَانُوا۟ يَعْلَمُونَ صِحَّةَ رِسَالَتِهِ، وَكَانُوا۟ وَجَدُوا۟ ذِكْرَهُ فِى كُتُبِهِمْ حَيْثُ لَمْ يَتَجَاسَرُوا۟ عَلَى التَّمَنِّى لَوْلَا ذَٰلِكَ لَفَعَلُوا۟ إِظْهَارًا لِخَلَفِهِ. ثُمَّ قَالَ تَعَالَى فِى الْيَهُودِ: ﴿ضُرِبَتْ عَلَيْهِمُ ٱلذِّلَّةُ أَيْنَ مَا ثُقِفُوٓا۟ إِلَّا بِحَبْلٍ مِّنَ ٱللَّهِ﴾ وَمِصْدَاقُ هَٰذَا فِى الْيَهُودِ بَيِّنٌ فِى كُلِّ عَصْرٍ وَمِصْرٍ؛ إِذْ لَمْ تُرْفَعْ لَهُمْ رَايَةٌ مُنْذُ يَوْمَئِذٍ، وَلَا ثَبَتَ لَهُمْ سُلْطَانٌ، وَكَانَتْ أَمَارَةُ الذُّلِّ وَالصَّغَارِ وَالْمَسْكَنَةِ عَلَيْهِمْ بَادِيَةً، وَعَلَامَةُ السَّخَطِ وَاللَّعْنَةِ ظَاهِرَةً وَإِنْ كَانُوا۟ يَرْجِعُونَ إِلَى ثَرْوَةٍ مِّنَ الْمَالِ وَكَثْرَةٍ مِّنَ الْعُدَّةِ وَالْعَتَادِ.
And like His statement, the Exalted: (Alif Lam Meem. The Romans have been defeated in the nearest land, and they, after their defeat, will overcome) and it was as He informed. And like His statement, the Exalted: (We will show them Our signs in the horizons and in themselves) and the intended meaning from it is a meaning in the future, indicated by the letter sin (future tense), and He showed them the signs indicating their originatedness and the existence of the Wise Maker for them in themselves and in the horizons, so the verse was not directed to that, and the intended meaning was what the people of interpretation said: that the intended meaning by the signs in the horizons is the conquest of Persia, and in themselves is the conquest of Mecca, and it was as He informed. And like His statement, the Exalted, to His Messenger: (Indeed, He who imposed upon you the Qur'an will surely return you to a place of return) i.e., Mecca, and He returned him to it. And like His statement, the Exalted: (He is the One who sent His Messenger with guidance and the religion of truth to make it prevail over all religion) and He has made it prevail. And like His statement, the Exalted: (Allah has promised those who have believed among you and done righteous deeds that He will surely grant them succession upon the earth) the verse, and the intended by that are the Companions, as indicated by His statement, the Exalted: (And He will surely substitute for them, after their fear, security) and they were the fearful ones in the early days of Islam and before the Hijrah, and they were given succession, and in the verse is an indication of the caliphate of Abu Bakr, may Allah be pleased with him, since it is not permissible for the one given succession to be overcome. And like His statement, the Exalted, concerning the Jews: (Say, O you who are Jews, if you claim that you are allies of Allah, excluding the people) until He said: (And they will not wish for it ever) and it was as He informed, and none of them wished for death, and in the verse is proof that they knew the truth of his message, and they had found his mention in their scriptures, because they did not dare to wish for it; if not for that, they would have done so to show [that] his information was false. Then He said, the Exalted, concerning the Jews: (Humiliation has been imposed upon them wherever they are found, except through a rope from Allah) and the confirmation of this among the Jews is clear in every age and region; since no banner has been raised for them since that day, nor has any authority been established for them, and the mark of humiliation, degradation and abasement is evident upon them, and the sign of wrath and curse is apparent, even if they possess wealth and numerous equipment and armaments.
Source pages p. 736

Commentary
This passage is a proof of prophethood from predictions (akhbār bil-ghayb). The author lists several Quranic verses that contain predictions of future events that came true. Each example shows that the Quran's information about the future could not have come from human knowledge and thus confirms Muhammad's prophethood. The author begins with the Romans' victory (Sūrat al-Rūm), then the general verse about showing signs (Sūrat Fuṣṣilat), interpreted as specific future conquests. Then he mentions the promise of return to Mecca (Sūrat al-Qaṣaṣ), the dominance of Islam (Sūrat al-Ṣaff), the promise of caliphate (Sūrat al-Nūr) which he links to the caliphate of Abu Bakr (may Allah be pleased with him), and finally two verses about the Jews: their unwillingness to wish for death (Sūrat al-Jumuʿah) and their perpetual humiliation (Sūrat Āl ʿImrān). The author explains each verse's fulfillment as clear historical fact, reinforcing the argument that prophethood is proven through fulfilled prophecy.

Key Terms
تمني الموت (tamannī al-mawt)
الذلة (al-dhilla)
المسكنة (al-maskana)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the author, why did the Jews not wish for death when challenged in Sūrat al-Jumuʿah?
A) They were cowards
B) They knew that Muhammad was a true prophet from their scriptures
C) They did not understand the verse
D) They were not present at the time

Key Takeaway
The Quran's precise predictions about Jewish behavior and historical condition, which defy natural expectation, serve as powerful evidence of divine revelation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The Jews knew the truth but rejected it out of arrogance. Where in your own life have you known a truth from Allah—through the Quran, a sign, or a sincere reminder—yet hesitated or refused to act on it because of pride or convenience? Will you today surrender that one thing to Allah?
?
Humiliation is described as a consequence of defiance against the Prophet. Think of a time when you felt humiliated or 'small' after opposing a clear command of Allah. In that moment, did you double down in defiance or soften your heart? What would it take for you to truly internalize that honor comes only through obedience?
?
The Jews possessed wealth and arms but still bore the marks of divine wrath. If you were stripped of all your worldly resources tomorrow, would the signs of Allah's pleasure still be evident on you? What are those signs in your life right now?

Predicting the Spread of Islam
Nasafi cites the hadith of earth folding and its fulfillment as proof of prophethood.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Prophet's prediction about the earth being folded and the spread of his nation's dominion serves as a proof of his prophethood.

Core Idea
Prophecy fulfilled: the Prophet saw the earth's expanse, and Islam spread exactly as foretold.

Nasafi continues his argument for prophethood by turning to specific hadith predictions that were historically fulfilled. The first is a well-known hadith in which the Prophet described the earth being folded for him, showing him its east and west, and foretold that his nation would reach those lands. This prediction came true with the rapid expansion of the Islamic empire, confirming that only a true prophet could know such unseen events.

Guided Path
1
Read the hadith and translation
Read the Arabic text and the literal translation carefully. Notice the key term 'زُوِيَتْ' (folded up).
2
Understand the interpretation
The author explains that the hadith does not mean the entire literal east and west, but what people customarily refer to as such. Reflect on why this clarification is important.
This prevents literal misinterpretation.
3
Connect to fulfillment
Think about the historical spread of Islam after the Prophet's time. How does this show the truth of his prophecy?
4
Distinguish from miracle
Consider why this is a proof of prophethood rather than a miracle—it is a prediction of future events that came true.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَأَمَّا مَا هُوَ رَاجِعٌ إِلَى الْإِخْبَارِ عَنِ الْكَائِنَاتِ فِي الْمُسْتَقْبَلِ غَيْرِ الْكِتَابِ فَمِنْهُ قَوْلُهُ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ: زُوِيَتْ لِي الْأَرْضُ فَأُرِيتُ مَشَارِقَهَا وَمَغَارِبَهَا وَسَيَبْلُغُ مُلْكُ أُمَّتِي مَا زُوِيَ لِي مِنْهَا وَكَانَ كَمَا أَخْبَرَ إِذْ لَمْ يُرَدْ بِذَلِكَ جَمِيعُ الْمَشَارِقِ وَالْمَغَارِبِ، وَإِنَّمَا أَرَادَ مَا يَنْطَلِقُ فِي عُرْفِ النَّاسِ عَلَيْهِ اسْمُ الْمَشْرِقِ وَالْمَغْرِبِ لِانْصِرَافِ مُطْلَقِ الْكَلَامِ إِلَى مَا هُوَ الْمُسْتَعْمَلُ فِي مُخَاطَبَةِ الْمُتَعَارَفِ فِي مُفَاوَضَاتِهِمْ. وَمِنْ ذَلِكَ قَوْلُهُ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ لِعَدِيِّ بْنِ حَاتِمٍ الطَّائِيِّ: كَيْفَ بِكَ إِذَا خَرَجَتِ الظَّعِينَةُ مِنْ أَقْصَى قُصُورِ الْيَمَنِ إِلَى قُصُورِ الْحِيرَةِ لَا تَخَافُ إِلَّا اللَّهَ؟ قَالَ عَدِيٌّ: قُلْتُ يَا رَسُولَ اللَّهِ، فَكَيْفَ بِطَيِّئٍ وَمَقَامِهَا؟ قَالَ: يَكْفِيهَا اللَّهُ طَيَّئًا. وَهَذَا إِخْبَارٌ عَنِ الْأَمْرِ الَّذِي يَكُونُ بَعْدَهُمْ لِأَنَّهُمْ كَانُوا خَائِفِينَ فِي حَيَاتِهِ، فَكَانَ كَمَا أَخْبَرَ فِي زَمَنِ عُمَرَ فَكَانَتِ الْمَرْأَةُ تَخْرُجُ مِنْ قَبِيلَةِ طَيِّئٍ بِالْيَمَنِ وَتُجَاوِزُ الْبَادِيَةَ، وَلَا يَعْتَرِضُ لَهَا أَحَدٌ.
As for what relates to informing about future events other than the Book: among them is his statement, peace be upon him: 'The earth was folded up for me, so I was shown its east and west, and the dominion of my nation will reach what was folded up for me from it.' And it was as he informed, since by that he did not intend all east and west; rather, he intended what customarily among people is called east and west, because unrestricted speech turns to what is customarily used in addressing people in their discussions. And among that is his statement, peace be upon him, to ʿAdī ibn Ḥātim al-Ṭāʾī: 'How will it be for you when a woman on a camel litter goes out from the farthest palaces of Yemen to the palaces of Ḥīrah, fearing none but Allah?' ʿAdī said: 'I said, O Messenger of Allah, what about Ṭayyiʾ and their standing?' He said: 'Allah will suffice for her against Ṭayyiʾ.' And this is informing about an event that would occur after them, because they were fearful during his lifetime, and it was as he informed in the time of ʿUmar, for the woman would go out from the tribe of Ṭayyiʾ in Yemen and cross the desert, and no one would obstruct her.
Source pages p. 737

Commentary
This passage continues the proof of prophethood from predictions, now turning to hadith examples. The author first cites the hadith in which the Prophet (peace be upon him) said the earth was folded for him and he saw its east and west, and that the dominion of his nation would reach those places. This was fulfilled in the spread of Islam. The author clarifies that this does not mean every single region, but those areas commonly referred to as east and west. Then he mentions the hadith with ʿAdī ibn Ḥātim: the Prophet predicted that a woman would travel safely from Yemen to Ḥīrah fearing only Allah. This came true during the caliphate of ʿUmar, when the tribe of Ṭayyiʾ became Muslims and the roads became safe. Both hadiths are presented as clear historical fulfillments, strengthening the argument that Muhammad's knowledge of the unseen came from Allah, proving his prophethood.

Key Terms
زُوِيَتْ (zuwiyat)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The hadith about the earth being folded means the Prophet literally saw every inch of the earth instantly.
Correction: The author clarifies that the Prophet meant the lands customarily called east and west, and the vision was a spiritual insight indicating future conquest, not literal folding or exhaustive sight.

Checkpoint
Why does the author clarify that the Prophet's vision of east and west does not mean every single region?
A) To show the Prophet's limited vision
B) To prevent literal misinterpretation and show the prediction's fulfillment
C) To indicate that the earth was only partially shown
D) To emphasize the difficulty of the spread of Islam

Key Takeaway
The first hadith prediction about the spread of Islam was historically fulfilled, proving the Prophet's knowledge of the unseen.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The Prophet saw the east and west of the earth folded for him, and he promised that his nation would reach there. Do you truly believe that the global spread of Islam was a divine promise fulfilled, and not just historical accident? If so, what does that demand from you today regarding your role in supporting the truth?
?
The author clarifies that the prophecy was about customary regions, not every single place. Are there areas of your life where you avoid applying the Prophet's teachings because you think they are too demanding or not meant for you? What would it look like to take them as seriously as the early Muslims took the prophecy?
?
The fulfillment of this prophecy is a sign of the Prophet's truthfulness. Do you live with the weight of that sign, or do you treat it as a mere historical fact? If it is truly from Allah, then how should your actions today reflect that certainty? Write one specific change you will make this week.

Predicting Peace and Safety
Nasafi cites the hadith of the safe travel of the woman as another fulfilled prediction proving prophethood.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Prophet's prediction of safe travel for a woman from Yemen to Hira serves as a proof of his prophethood.

Core Idea
Prophecy fulfilled: the Prophet foretold a future of safety, and it came true in the time of Umar.

Nasafi now presents a second hadith prediction: the Prophet told Adi ibn Hatim that a woman would travel safely from Yemen to Hira, fearing only Allah. This was a remarkable prediction in a time of insecurity, but it was fulfilled during the reign of Umar when the tribe of Tayyi' embraced Islam and peace prevailed. This historical fulfillment further strengthens the case for Muhammad's prophethood.

Guided Path
1
Read the hadith account
Read the Arabic text of the exchange between the Prophet and Adi ibn Hatim.
2
Understand the context
Recognize that the tribe of Tayyi' was known for banditry, and the prediction of safe travel was against the norm.
3
See the fulfillment
Note that this came true in Umar's caliphate when the region became safe.
4
Connect to proof
Reflect on how this prediction, like the first, demonstrates knowledge of the unseen.

وَأَمَّا مَا هُوَ رَاجِعٌ إِلَى الْإِخْبَارِ عَنِ الْكَائِنَاتِ فِي الْمُسْتَقْبَلِ غَيْرِ الْكِتَابِ فَمِنْهُ قَوْلُهُ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ: زُوِيَتْ لِي الْأَرْضُ فَأُرِيتُ مَشَارِقَهَا وَمَغَارِبَهَا وَسَيَبْلُغُ مُلْكُ أُمَّتِي مَا زُوِيَ لِي مِنْهَا وَكَانَ كَمَا أَخْبَرَ إِذْ لَمْ يُرَدْ بِذَلِكَ جَمِيعُ الْمَشَارِقِ وَالْمَغَارِبِ، وَإِنَّمَا أَرَادَ مَا يَنْطَلِقُ فِي عُرْفِ النَّاسِ عَلَيْهِ اسْمُ الْمَشْرِقِ وَالْمَغْرِبِ لِانْصِرَافِ مُطْلَقِ الْكَلَامِ إِلَى مَا هُوَ الْمُسْتَعْمَلُ فِي مُخَاطَبَةِ الْمُتَعَارَفِ فِي مُفَاوَضَاتِهِمْ. وَمِنْ ذَلِكَ قَوْلُهُ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ لِعَدِيِّ بْنِ حَاتِمٍ الطَّائِيِّ: كَيْفَ بِكَ إِذَا خَرَجَتِ الظَّعِينَةُ مِنْ أَقْصَى قُصُورِ الْيَمَنِ إِلَى قُصُورِ الْحِيرَةِ لَا تَخَافُ إِلَّا اللَّهَ؟ قَالَ عَدِيٌّ: قُلْتُ يَا رَسُولَ اللَّهِ، فَكَيْفَ بِطَيِّئٍ وَمَقَامِهَا؟ قَالَ: يَكْفِيهَا اللَّهُ طَيَّئًا. وَهَذَا إِخْبَارٌ عَنِ الْأَمْرِ الَّذِي يَكُونُ بَعْدَهُمْ لِأَنَّهُمْ كَانُوا خَائِفِينَ فِي حَيَاتِهِ، فَكَانَ كَمَا أَخْبَرَ فِي زَمَنِ عُمَرَ فَكَانَتِ الْمَرْأَةُ تَخْرُجُ مِنْ قَبِيلَةِ طَيِّئٍ بِالْيَمَنِ وَتُجَاوِزُ الْبَادِيَةَ، وَلَا يَعْتَرِضُ لَهَا أَحَدٌ.
As for what relates to informing about future events other than the Book: among them is his statement, peace be upon him: 'The earth was folded up for me, so I was shown its east and west, and the dominion of my nation will reach what was folded up for me from it.' And it was as he informed, since by that he did not intend all east and west; rather, he intended what customarily among people is called east and west, because unrestricted speech turns to what is customarily used in addressing people in their discussions. And among that is his statement, peace be upon him, to ʿAdī ibn Ḥātim al-Ṭāʾī: 'How will it be for you when a woman on a camel litter goes out from the farthest palaces of Yemen to the palaces of Ḥīrah, fearing none but Allah?' ʿAdī said: 'I said, O Messenger of Allah, what about Ṭayyiʾ and their standing?' He said: 'Allah will suffice for her against Ṭayyiʾ.' And this is informing about an event that would occur after them, because they were fearful during his lifetime, and it was as he informed in the time of ʿUmar, for the woman would go out from the tribe of Ṭayyiʾ in Yemen and cross the desert, and no one would obstruct her.
Source pages p. 737

Commentary
This passage continues the proof of prophethood from predictions, now turning to hadith examples. The author first cites the hadith in which the Prophet (peace be upon him) said the earth was folded for him and he saw its east and west, and that the dominion of his nation would reach those places. This was fulfilled in the spread of Islam. The author clarifies that this does not mean every single region, but those areas commonly referred to as east and west. Then he mentions the hadith with ʿAdī ibn Ḥātim: the Prophet predicted that a woman would travel safely from Yemen to Ḥīrah fearing only Allah. This came true during the caliphate of ʿUmar, when the tribe of Ṭayyiʾ became Muslims and the roads became safe. Both hadiths are presented as clear historical fulfillments, strengthening the argument that Muhammad's knowledge of the unseen came from Allah, proving his prophethood.

Key Terms
الظعينة (al-ẓaʿīnah)
طيئ (Ṭayyiʾ)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The prediction about safe travel was meant to happen immediately or during the Prophet's lifetime.
Correction: The author explicitly says it was a future event after them, and it was fulfilled in the time of Umar, not instantly.

Checkpoint
What was the specific purpose of citing the hadith about the woman (ẓaʿīnah) traveling safely?
A) To show that women should travel alone
B) To prove that the Prophet predicted future safety and it came true
C) To criticize the tribe of Ṭayyiʾ
D) To explain the geography of Yemen

Key Takeaway
The second hadith prediction about safe travel was historically fulfilled, confirming the Prophet's knowledge of the unseen.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly believe the Prophet's promises about the afterlife with the same certainty as this fulfilled prophecy? What is holding you back from acting on that belief today?
?
In which areas of your life do you still fear people more than Allah, despite the clear evidence that true safety and security come only from Allah? Name one specific situation this week where you will choose to fear Allah alone.
?
The woman traveled alone, trusting only in Allah. When was the last time you did something solely for Allah's sake, disregarding the opinions and judgments of those around you? What one step can you take tomorrow to increase that reliance?

Prophetic Predictions on Dominion and Safety
Enumeration of three prophetic predictions with their fulfillments

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Prophet's predictions about the spread of Islamic dominion and the safety of believers serve as evidence for his prophethood.

Core Idea
The Prophet's precise knowledge of future events proves his prophethood.

This passage from Imam al-Nasafi's Tabsirat al-Adilla presents several examples of the Prophet Muhammad's predictions about future events that were later fulfilled. These predictions are presented as miracles demonstrating that he was truly sent by Allah. In this lesson, we examine the first set of predictions concerning the expansion of Islamic dominion and the safe travel of a woman.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the Arabic text carefully, noting the phrases 'زويت لي الارض' and 'الظعينة'. The passage uses the term 'إخبار عن الكائنات' to describe the type of miracle.
2
Identify the predictions
Find the three predictions in this passage: the earth folded showing dominion, the safety of a woman traveling, and the announcement of the Negus's death.
Each prediction is introduced with 'ومن ذلك'.
3
Reflect on the significance
Consider why these specific predictions were chosen as evidence. How do they demonstrate knowledge of the unseen? The accuracy and specificity of the predictions are key.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما ما هو راجع إلى الإخبار عن الكائنات في المستقبل غير الكتاب فمنه قوله عليه السلام زويت لي الارض فأريت مشارفها ومغاربها وسيبلغ ملك أمتي ما زوى لي منها وكان كما أخبر إذ لم يرد بذلك جميع المشارق والمغارب، وإنما أراد ما ينطلق في عرف الناس عليه اسم المشرق والمغرب لانصراف مطلق الكلام إلى ما هو المستعمل في مخاطبة المتعارف في مفاوضاتهم. ومن ذلك قوله عليه السلام لعدي بن حاتم الطائي : "كيف بك إذا خرجت الظعينة من أقصى قصور اليمن إلى قصور الحيرة لا تخاف إلا الله؟" قال عدي: قلت يا رسول الله، فكيف بطيئ ومقامها؟ قال: "يكفيها الله طيا" وهذا إخبار عن الأمر الذي يكون بعدهم لأنهم كانوا خائفين في حياته، فكان كما أخبر في زمن عمر فكانت المرأة تخرج من قبيلة طيئ باليمن وتجاوز البادية، ولا يعترض لها أحد بمكروه. ومن ذلك أنه نعى النجاشي وخبَّر أصحابه بموته وصلى عليه، فتتابعت الأخبار أنه مات في ذلك اليوم. ومن ذلك قوله لعمار : "تقتلك الفئة الباغية" فقتل يوم صفين مع علي. ومنها قوله عليه السلام لعلي : "أشقى الناس عاقر الناقة، والذي يخضب من هذا هذه" يعني الذي يضربك على رأسك فيخضب لحيتك من دم رأسك فضرب علي على رأسه حين قتل. ومن ذلك قوله عليه السلام لعلي: "أنك تقتل الناكثين والمارقين والقاسطين". ومن ذلك قوله عليه السلام: "اقتدوا باللذين من بعدي أبي بكر وعمر" فأعلمنا بهذا أن الخليفة بعده أبو بكر وبعد أبي بكر عمر رضي الله عنهما. ومن ذلك قوله: "الخلافة بعدي ثلاثون سنة ثم يؤتي الله الملك من يشاء" وكانت خلافة الخلفاء الراشدين ثلاثين.
And as for what pertains to informing about future occurrences other than the Book, among it is his saying, peace be upon him: 'The earth was folded for me, so I was shown its eastern and western parts, and the dominion of my nation will reach what was folded for me of it.' And it was as he informed, because he did not intend by that all the points of sunrise and sunset, but rather he intended what, in the common usage of people, is called east and west, due to the absolute speech being directed to what is customary in their mutual discourse. And among that is his saying, peace be upon him, to 'Adi ibn Hatim al-Ta'i: 'How will it be when a woman in a howdah travels from the farthest castles of Yemen to the castles of al-Hira, fearing none but Allah?' 'Adi said: I said, O Messenger of Allah, what about my tribe Tayyi' and their residence? He said: 'Allah will suffice for Tayyi'.' And this is an informing about a matter that would occur after them, because they were fearful during his lifetime, and it was as he informed during the time of 'Umar, for a woman would set out from the tribe of Tayyi' in Yemen and cross the desert, and no one would obstruct her with anything unpleasant. And among that is that he announced the death of the Negus and informed his companions of his death and prayed over him, and news followed consecutively that he had died on that day. And among that is his saying to 'Ammar: 'The rebellious faction will kill you,' and he was killed on the Day of Siffin with 'Ali. And among that is his saying, peace be upon him, to 'Ali: 'The most wretched of people is the one who hamstrung the she-camel, and the one who will stain these (i.e., this beard) with blood' meaning the one who will strike you on your head and stain your beard with blood from your head. And 'Ali was struck on his head when he was killed. And among that is his saying, peace be upon him, to 'Ali: 'You will kill the oath-breakers, the apostates, and the wrongdoers.' And among that is his saying, peace be upon him: 'Follow the two after me, Abu Bakr and 'Umar.' Thus he informed us that the caliph after him would be Abu Bakr, and after Abu Bakr, 'Umar, may Allah be pleased with them both. And among that is his saying: 'The caliphate after me will be thirty years, then Allah will give the kingdom to whomever He wills.' And the caliphate of the Rightly Guided Caliphs was thirty.
Source pages p. 737

Commentary
This passage is a collection of examples of prophetic predictions about future events that were fulfilled, presented as evidence for the truth of prophethood. The author lists them in sequence: first, the hadith about the earth being folded for the Prophet, indicating that his nation's dominion would reach far lands, which occurred. Then the prediction to 'Adi ibn Hatim about the safe travel of a woman from Yemen to al-Hira, which came true in 'Umar's time. Then the announcement of the Negus's death at the very moment he died. Then the prediction that 'Ammar would be killed by the rebellious faction, which happened at Siffin. Then the prediction about 'Ali being struck on the head and his beard stained with blood, which occurred when he was assassinated. Then the prediction that 'Ali would kill the oath-breakers, apostates, and wrongdoers, which he did during his caliphate. Then the instruction to follow Abu Bakr and 'Umar, implying their succession, which materialized. Finally, the prediction that the caliphate would last thirty years, which matched the period of the Rightly Guided Caliphs. Each example demonstrates the Prophet's knowledge of the unseen, a miracle proving his prophethood.

Key Terms
الإخبار عن الكائنات
النبوة
المعجزات
الظعينة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following predictions was fulfilled during the caliphate of 'Umar?
A) The dominion of the nation reaching the east and west
B) The safe travel of a woman from Yemen to al-Hira
C) The death of the Negus
D) The killing of 'Ammar

Key Takeaway
The Prophet's accurate predictions about the spread of Islam and safety of believers prove his knowledge came from divine revelation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You have just read about three specific predictions the Prophet made. If you had been alive and heard these predictions before their fulfillment, would you have believed the Prophet's claim of prophethood? What would it take for you to believe, and what does that reveal about your own standard for truth?
?
The Prophet predicted that his nation's dominion would spread, and it happened. Where is your heart when you see the global weakness of Muslims today? Do you truly believe that the same promise of dominion and protection applies to this community? Or do you doubt because you don't see it yet?
?
When you read about the woman traveling safely, fearing none but Allah, are you living with that kind of trust in Allah's protection? Or are you still afraid of people's judgment, loss, or harm? What is one step you will take this week to place your fear solely in Allah?

Prophetic Predictions about ‘Ali and the Caliphate
Enumeration of prophetic predictions about ‘Ali, Abu Bakr, ‘Umar, and the caliphate

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Prophet's predictions about ‘Ali ibn Abi Talib and the duration of the rightly guided caliphate serve as evidence for his prophethood.

Core Idea
Specific predictions about individuals and the caliphate confirm prophetic knowledge.

This lesson continues examining the prophetic predictions presented by Imam al-Nasafi. Here we focus on predictions concerning ‘Ali ibn Abi Talib, the caliphs Abu Bakr and ‘Umar, and the duration of the caliphate. Each of these was precisely fulfilled, demonstrating that the Prophet spoke from divine revelation.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the Arabic text, noting the phrases 'تقتلك الفئة الباغية', 'الذين يخضب من هذا هذه', 'تقتل الناكثين والمارقين والقاسطين'.
2
Identify the predictions
Find the five predictions: ‘Ammar's death, ‘Ali's beard stained with blood, ‘Ali killing three groups, following Abu Bakr and ‘Umar, and thirty-year caliphate.
3
Reflect on the significance
Consider why these predictions are compelling evidence. How do they show knowledge of future events that only Allah could reveal?

وأما ما هو راجع إلى الإخبار عن الكائنات في المستقبل غير الكتاب فمنه قوله عليه السلام زويت لي الارض فأريت مشارفها ومغاربها وسيبلغ ملك أمتي ما زوى لي منها وكان كما أخبر إذ لم يرد بذلك جميع المشارق والمغارب، وإنما أراد ما ينطلق في عرف الناس عليه اسم المشرق والمغرب لانصراف مطلق الكلام إلى ما هو المستعمل في مخاطبة المتعارف في مفاوضاتهم. ومن ذلك قوله عليه السلام لعدي بن حاتم الطائي : "كيف بك إذا خرجت الظعينة من أقصى قصور اليمن إلى قصور الحيرة لا تخاف إلا الله؟" قال عدي: قلت يا رسول الله، فكيف بطيئ ومقامها؟ قال: "يكفيها الله طيا" وهذا إخبار عن الأمر الذي يكون بعدهم لأنهم كانوا خائفين في حياته، فكان كما أخبر في زمن عمر فكانت المرأة تخرج من قبيلة طيئ باليمن وتجاوز البادية، ولا يعترض لها أحد بمكروه. ومن ذلك أنه نعى النجاشي وخبَّر أصحابه بموته وصلى عليه، فتتابعت الأخبار أنه مات في ذلك اليوم. ومن ذلك قوله لعمار : "تقتلك الفئة الباغية" فقتل يوم صفين مع علي. ومنها قوله عليه السلام لعلي : "أشقى الناس عاقر الناقة، والذي يخضب من هذا هذه" يعني الذي يضربك على رأسك فيخضب لحيتك من دم رأسك فضرب علي على رأسه حين قتل. ومن ذلك قوله عليه السلام لعلي: "أنك تقتل الناكثين والمارقين والقاسطين". ومن ذلك قوله عليه السلام: "اقتدوا باللذين من بعدي أبي بكر وعمر" فأعلمنا بهذا أن الخليفة بعده أبو بكر وبعد أبي بكر عمر رضي الله عنهما. ومن ذلك قوله: "الخلافة بعدي ثلاثون سنة ثم يؤتي الله الملك من يشاء" وكانت خلافة الخلفاء الراشدين ثلاثين.
And as for what pertains to informing about future occurrences other than the Book, among it is his saying, peace be upon him: 'The earth was folded for me, so I was shown its eastern and western parts, and the dominion of my nation will reach what was folded for me of it.' And it was as he informed, because he did not intend by that all the points of sunrise and sunset, but rather he intended what, in the common usage of people, is called east and west, due to the absolute speech being directed to what is customary in their mutual discourse. And among that is his saying, peace be upon him, to 'Adi ibn Hatim al-Ta'i: 'How will it be when a woman in a howdah travels from the farthest castles of Yemen to the castles of al-Hira, fearing none but Allah?' 'Adi said: I said, O Messenger of Allah, what about my tribe Tayyi' and their residence? He said: 'Allah will suffice for Tayyi'.' And this is an informing about a matter that would occur after them, because they were fearful during his lifetime, and it was as he informed during the time of 'Umar, for a woman would set out from the tribe of Tayyi' in Yemen and cross the desert, and no one would obstruct her with anything unpleasant. And among that is that he announced the death of the Negus and informed his companions of his death and prayed over him, and news followed consecutively that he had died on that day. And among that is his saying to 'Ammar: 'The rebellious faction will kill you,' and he was killed on the Day of Siffin with 'Ali. And among that is his saying, peace be upon him, to 'Ali: 'The most wretched of people is the one who hamstrung the she-camel, and the one who will stain these (i.e., this beard) with blood' meaning the one who will strike you on your head and stain your beard with blood from your head. And 'Ali was struck on his head when he was killed. And among that is his saying, peace be upon him, to 'Ali: 'You will kill the oath-breakers, the apostates, and the wrongdoers.' Thus he informed us that the caliph after him would be Abu Bakr, and after Abu Bakr, 'Umar, may Allah be pleased with them both. How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The Prophet foretold that ‘Ali would be killed by the most wretched person. How does that prophecy affect the way you view the sanctity of the Prophet’s family? Do you truly honor ‘Ali as his prophesied successor?
?

Are you prepared to accept that no system of government after that period can claim to be a perfect continuation of the prophetic model? What does that mean for your trust in current rulers?
?
These predictions demand that you believe in a Prophet who knows the future. But do you live as if every word he spoke is absolutely true? Is there any area of your life where you hesitate to fully submit to his teachings? Answer honestly – and find the courage to close that gap today.

Prophetic Predictions: The Negus, 'Ammar, and 'Ali's Death
Three specific examples of prophetic predictions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how specific predictions of deaths and events confirm the Prophet's divine knowledge.

Core Idea
Accurate predictions of unseen events prove the Prophet's prophethood.

The author begins by presenting instances where the Prophet ﷺ foretold specific deaths. These predictions were precise and came true exactly as described, demonstrating that his knowledge came from Allah, not from human guessing. The following examples illustrate this point.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic and translation, noting the three distinct predictions and their fulfillments.
Focus on the specificity of each prediction.
2
Identify each prediction
Find the prediction about the Negus, 'Ammar, and 'Ali. Reflect on how each was fulfilled exactly.
3
Consider the implications
Think about why accurate predictions of future events are considered strong evidence for prophethood, especially when they are precise and verifiable.
Contrast these with vague claims of soothsayers.
