ومن ذلك أنه نعى النجاشي وخبَّر أصحابه بموته وصلى عليه، فتتابعت الأخبار أنه مات في ذلك اليوم. ومن ذلك قوله لعمار : 'تقتلك الفئة الباغية' فقتل يوم صفين مع علي. ومنها قوله عليه السلام لعلي: 'أشقى الناس عاقر الناقة، والذي يخضب من هذا هذه' يعني الذي يضربك على رأسك فيخضب لحيتك من دم رأسك فضرب علي على رأسه حين قتل. ومن ذلك قوله عليه السلام لعلي: 'أنك تقتل الناكثين والمارقين والقاسطين'. ومن ذلك قوله عليه السلام: 'اقتدوا باللذين من بعدي أبي بكر وعمر' فأعلمنا بهذا أن الخليفة بعده أبو بكر وبعد أبي بكر عمر. ومن ذلك قوله: 'الخلافة بعدي ثلاثون سنة ثم يؤتي الله الملك من يشاء' وكانت خلافة الخلفاء الراشدين ثلاثين سنة. ومن ذلك حديث ليلة الإسراء وما أخبر من أخبار عير قريش، وكان كما أخبر. ومن ذلك أنه ضلت له عليه السلام ناقة فأقبل يسأل الناس عنها فقال المنافقون : هذا محمد يخبركم خبر السماء وهو لا يدري أين ناقته، فصعد المنبر وحمد الله وأثنى عليه، وحكى قولهم ثم قال: إني لا أعلم إلا ما أعلمني ربي وقد أخبرني أنها في وادي كذا متعلق زمامها بشجرة فبادر الناس فوجدوها كذلك. ومن ذلك قوله لخالد بن الوليد حين بعثه إلى أكيدر بدومة الجندل: 'أما أنكم ستأتونه فتجدونه يصيد البقر' فوجدوه كذلك. ومن ذلك قوله عليه السلام للعباس حين أسره: 'افد نفسك وابني أخيك' يعني عقيل بن أبي طالب ونوفل بن الحارث فإنك ذو مال فقال : لا مال عندي. قال: فأين المال الذي وضعته بمكة عند أم الفضل وليس معكما أحد، فقلت: إن أصبت في سفري فللفضل كذا، ولعبد الله كذا، ولفلان كذا ؟ فقال العباس والذي بعثك بالحق نبيا ما علم بهذا أحد غيري، وإنك لرسول الله وأسلم هو وعقيل. ومن ذلك ما كان يخبر أهل النفاق بما كانوا يقولون فيما بينهم ويبيتون ما لا يرضى من القول حتى كانوا من شدة تعنتهم يحذرون أن ينزل عليه سورة تنبئهم بما في قلوبهم ، وأمثال ذلك كثير، وكتابنا هذا يضيق عن ذكر عشر ذلك فضلاً عن كله ، والله الموفق. ثم إن جميع ما أخبر من الأخبار الكائنة في المستقبل خرج على ما أخبر من غير تمكن كذب أو حلف في شيء من ذلك لا كمثل أخبار الكهنة والمنجمين.
Among that is that he announced the death of the Negus and informed his Companions of his death and prayed over him, and the reports followed that he died on that day. And among that is his saying to 'Ammar: 'The rebellious group will kill you.' So he was killed on the day of Siffin with 'Ali. And among that is his saying, peace be upon him, to 'Ali: 'The most wretched of people is the one who hamstrung the she-camel, and the one who will dye this from this' meaning the one who will strike you on your head and dye your beard from the blood of your head. So 'Ali was struck on his head when he was killed. And among that is his saying, peace be upon him, to 'Ali: 'You will kill the oath-breakers, the renegades, and the deviators.' And among that is his saying, peace be upon him: 'Follow the two after me, Abu Bakr and 'Umar.' So by this we are informed that the caliph after him is Abu Bakr, and after Abu Bakr is 'Umar, may Allah be pleased with them. And among that is his saying: 'The caliphate after me will last thirty years, then Allah will give sovereignty to whom He wills.' And the caliphate of the Rightly Guided Caliphs was thirty years. And among that is the hadith of the Night Journey and what he informed of the news of the Quraysh caravan, and it was as he informed. And among that is that his, peace be upon him, she-camel was lost, so he began asking people about it. The hypocrites said: 'This Muhammad tells you news from heaven but does not know where his she-camel is.' So he ascended the pulpit, praised Allah and extolled Him, related their words, then said: 'I do not know except what my Lord has taught me, and He has informed me that it is in such-and-such valley, its reins caught on a tree.' So the people rushed and found it thus. And among that is his saying to Khalid ibn al-Walid when he sent him to Ukaydir of Dumah al-Jandal: 'Indeed, you will come to him and find him hunting cows.' So they found him thus. And among that is his saying, peace be upon him, to al-'Abbas when he was captured: 'Redeem yourself and your brother's sons' meaning 'Aqil ibn Abi Talib and Nawfal ibn al-Harith, for you are a man of wealth.' He said: 'I have no wealth.' He said: 'Where is the wealth that you deposited in Mecca with Umm al-Fadl when no one else was with you, and you said: If I am killed on my journey, then for al-Fadl such-and-such, for 'Abdullah such-and-such, and for so-and-so such-and-such?' So al-'Abbas said: 'By the One who sent you with the truth as a prophet, no one knows this except me, and indeed you are the Messenger of Allah.' So he and 'Aqil embraced Islam. And among that is that he would inform about the hypocrites what they said among themselves and what they concealed of speech that was displeasing, until they, due to the intensity of their obstinacy, would beware that a surah might be revealed informing them of what was in their hearts. And the like of that is many, and this our book is too narrow to mention a tenth of that, let alone all of it. And Allah is the Giver of success. Then, indeed, all that he informed of news occurring in the future came out as he informed, without any possibility of falsehood or lying in any of that, not like the news of soothsayers and astrologers.
Source pages p. 738

Commentary
This passage is a series of examples that serve as evidence for the truthfulness of the Prophet's prophethood. The author lists several instances where the Prophet Muhammad ﷺ accurately predicted future events. First, he announced the death of the Negus of Abyssinia, which occurred exactly as he said. Second, he told 'Ammar ibn Yasir that he would be killed by the rebellious party, which happened at the Battle of Siffin. Third, he predicted that 'Ali would be struck on the head, dyeing his beard with blood, which occurred when 'Ali was assassinated. Fourth, he told 'Ali that he would kill the oath-breakers (nakithun), renegades (mariqun), and deviators (qasitun), referring to the battles against the Khawarij and others. Fifth, he instructed to follow Abu Bakr and 'Umar, indicating the order of the caliphate. Sixth, he stated that the caliphate after him would be thirty years, which matched the combined reigns of the Rightly Guided Caliphs. Seventh, he accurately described the timing of the Quraysh caravan as related in the Isra' narrative. Eighth, he knew the location of his lost camel, which the hypocrites used to mock him, but he correctly specified its location. Ninth, he told Khalid ibn al-Walid that he would find Ukaydir hunting cows, which was exactly the case. Tenth, he confronted al-'Abbas about a secret deposit of money, leading to his conversion. Eleventh, he exposed the hidden conversations of the hypocrites. The author then concludes that all of the Prophet's future predictions came true without any falsehood, in contrast to the unreliable predictions of soothsayers and astrologers. Each example reinforces the argument that the Prophet's knowledge of the unseen is a clear sign of his prophethood.

النبوة
المعجزة
الكهانة
التنجيم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: These predictions could be coincidences or lucky guesses.
Correction: The passage emphasizes that they were specific, verifiable events that occurred exactly as foretold, unlike random guesses.

Checkpoint
Which prediction from this passage was fulfilled during the Battle of Siffin?
A) The death of the Negus
B) The killing of 'Ammar
C) The assassination of 'Ali
D) The lost camel incident

Key Takeaway
The Prophet's precise predictions of deaths demonstrate his knowledge of the unseen, a clear sign of prophethood.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Before reading this lesson, did you ever doubt that the Prophet had knowledge of the unseen? Consider the three predictions given. If you truly believe they happened exactly as predicted, what does that demand of you in terms of your obedience to his teachings? Are you living as if every word he spoke is true? If not, what needs to change starting today?
?
The Prophet predicted 'Ammar's death by the rebellious group. That group consisted of Muslims. How does this challenge your assumption that only non-Muslims can be wrong? Are you willing to examine your own group's actions against the Prophet's standards? Will you commit to seeking truth over blind loyalty, even if it means admitting error?
?
The prediction about 'Ali being struck on the head is extremely specific. Do you treat the Prophet's words with the same certainty you treat a verified historical fact? If you do, why do you still hesitate to act on some of his commands? What concrete step will you take today to align your life more closely with his guidance?

Prophetic Predictions: Ali's Battles, the Caliphate, and the Night Journey
Four examples: 'Ali's foes, succession, caliphate length, caravan news.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Prophet's predictions about leadership and historical events confirm his prophethood.

Core Idea
The Prophet's foretelling of political and historical events proves his divine knowledge.

The passage continues with predictions about the caliphate, the duration of the rightly guided caliphs, and the news of the Quraysh caravan. These predictions were all verifiably accurate, strengthening the case for prophethood.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic and translation, paying attention to each prediction and its fulfillment.
Notice the variety: from battles to caliphate to caravan.
2
Identify the three predictions
Find the predictions about 'Ali killing three groups, the succession of Abu Bakr and 'Umar, the thirty-year caliphate, and the news of the caravan.
Each is a distinct claim.
3
Reflect on the caliphate prediction
Note that the caliphate lasted exactly thirty years from Abu Bakr to 'Ali, as predicted.
This is a historical fact.
4
Contrast with human knowledge
Consider that such accurate long-term predictions are beyond human capability, indicating divine inspiration.

Commentary
This passage is a series of examples that serve as evidence for the truthfulness of the Prophet's prophethood. The author lists several instances where the Prophet Muhammad ﷺ accurately predicted future events. First, he announced the death of the Negus of Abyssinia, which occurred exactly as he said. Second, he told 'Ammar ibn Yasir that he would be killed by the rebellious party, which happened at the Battle of Siffin. Third, he predicted that 'Ali would be struck on the head, dyeing his beard with blood, which occurred when 'Ali was assassinated. Fourth, he told 'Ali that he would kill the oath-breakers (nakithun), renegades (mariqun), and deviators (qasitun), referring to the battles against the Khawarij and others. Fifth, he instructed to follow Abu Bakr and 'Umar, indicating the order of the caliphate. Sixth, he stated that the caliphate after him would be thirty years, which matched the combined reigns of the Rightly Guided Caliphs. Seventh, he accurately described the timing of the Quraysh caravan as related in the Isra' narrative. Eighth, he knew the location of his lost camel, which the hypocrites used to mock him, but he correctly specified its location. Ninth, he told Khalid ibn al-Walid that he would find Ukaydir hunting cows, which was exactly the case. Tenth, he confronted al-'Abbas about a secret deposit of money, leading to his conversion. Eleventh, he exposed the hidden conversations of the hypocrites. The author then concludes that all of the Prophet's future predictions came true without any falsehood, in contrast to the unreliable predictions of soothsayers and astrologers. Each example reinforces the argument that the Prophet's knowledge of the unseen is a clear sign of his prophethood.

Prophetic Predictions: Lost Camel, Ukaydir, al-'Abbas, and the Hypocrites
Four examples plus concluding contrast with soothsayers.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Prophet's knowledge of hidden and personal matters confirms his prophethood.

Core Idea
The Prophet's knowledge of the unseen in everyday matters proves his divine connection.

The author presents four more examples that demonstrate the Prophet's knowledge of hidden realities, including the location of his lost camel, the whereabouts of a distant king, a secret financial arrangement, and the inner thoughts of hypocrites. Each example reinforces the truth of his prophethood. The passage concludes that all predictions came true without error.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic and translation, noting each example of hidden knowledge.
These examples involve secrets and future events.
2
Identify the four examples
Find the lost camel, Ukaydir hunting, al-'Abbas's secret deposit, and exposing hypocrites.
3
Reflect on the secret deposit
Notice that the Prophet revealed a private conversation, leading to al-'Abbas's conversion.
This is a powerful demonstration of unseen knowledge.
4
Understand the conclusion
The author ends by contrasting the Prophet's perfect predictions with the unreliable guesses of soothsayers.
This summarizes the argument.

And among that is his saying to 'Ammar: 'The rebellious group will kill you.' So he was killed on the day of Siffin with 'Ali. And among that is his saying, peace be upon him, to 'Ali: 'The most wretched of people is the one who hamstrung the she-camel, and the one who will dye this from this' meaning the one who will strike you on your head and dye your beard from the blood of your head. So 'Ali was struck on his head when he was killed. And among that is his saying, peace be upon him, to 'Ali: 'You will kill the oath-breakers, the renegades, and the deviators.' And among that is his saying, peace be upon him: 'Follow the two after me, Abu Bakr and 'Umar.' So by this we are informed that the caliph after him is Abu Bakr, and after Abu Bakr is 'Umar, may Allah be pleased with them. And among that is his saying: 'The caliphate after me will last thirty years, then Allah will give sovereignty to whom He wills.' And the caliphate of the Rightly Guided Caliphs was thirty years. And among that is the hadith of the Night Journey and what he informed of the news of the Quraysh caravan, and it was as he informed. And among that is that his, peace be upon him, she-camel was lost, so he began asking people about it. The hypocrites said: 'This Muhammad tells you news from heaven but does not know where his she-camel is.' So he ascended the pulpit, praised Allah and extolled Him, related their words, then said: 'I do not know except what my Lord has taught me, and He has informed me that it is in such-and-such valley, its reins caught on a tree.' So the people rushed and found it thus. And among that is his saying to Khalid ibn al-Walid when he sent him to Ukaydir of Dumah al-Jandal: 'Indeed, you will come to him and find him hunting cows.' So they found him thus. And among that is his saying, peace be upon him, to al-'Abbas when he was captured: 'Redeem yourself and your brother's sons' meaning 'Aqil ibn Abi Talib and Nawfal ibn al-Harith, for you are a man of wealth.' He said: 'I have no wealth.' He said: 'Where is the wealth that you deposited in Mecca with Umm al-Fadl when no one else was with you, and you said: If I am killed on my journey, then for al-Fadl such-and-such, for 'Abdullah such-and-such, and for so-and-so such-and-such?' So al-'Abbas said: 'By the One who sent you with the truth as a prophet, no one knows this except me, and indeed you are the Messenger of Allah.' So he and 'Aqil embraced Islam. And among that is that he would inform about the hypocrites what they said among themselves and what they concealed of speech that was displeasing, until they, due to the intensity of their obstinacy, would beware that a surah might be revealed informing them of what was in their hearts. And the like of that is many, and this our book is too narrow to mention a tenth of that, let alone all of it. And Allah is the Giver of success. Then, indeed, all that he informed of news occurring in the future came out as he informed, without any possibility of falsehood or lying in any of that, not like the news of soothsayers and astrologers.
Source pages p. 738

Commentary
This passage is a series of examples that serve as evidence for the truthfulness of the Prophet's prophethood. The author lists several instances where the Prophet Muhammad ﷺ accurately predicted future events. First, he announced the death of the Negus of Abyssinia, which occurred exactly as he said. Second, he told 'Ammar ibn Yasir that he would be killed by the rebellious party, which happened at the Battle of Siffin. Third, he predicted that 'Ali would be struck on the head, dyeing his beard with blood, which occurred when 'Ali was assassinated. Fourth, he told 'Ali that he would kill the oath-breakers (nakithun), renegades (mariqun), and deviators (qasitun), referring to the battles against the Khawarij and others. Fifth, he instructed to follow Abu Bakr and 'Umar, indicating the order of the caliphate. Sixth, he stated that the caliphate after him would be thirty years, which matched the combined reigns of the Rightly Guided Caliphs. Seventh, he accurately described the timing of the Quraysh caravan as related in the Isra' narrative. Eighth, he knew the location of his lost camel, which the hypocrites used to mock him, but he correctly specified its location. Ninth, he told Khalid ibn al-Walid that he would find Ukaydir hunting cows, which was exactly the case. Tenth, he confronted al-'Abbas about a secret deposit of money, leading to his conversion. Eleventh, he exposed the hidden conversations of the hypocrites. The author then concludes that all of the Prophet's future predictions came true without any falsehood, in contrast to the unreliable predictions of soothsayers and astrologers. Each example reinforces the argument that the Prophet's knowledge of the unseen is a clear sign of his prophethood.

Key Terms
أخبار الغيب
النبوة
المعجزة
الكهانة
التنجيم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may claim the Prophet's predictions were akin to soothsaying or lucky guesses.
Correction: The passage explicitly states that all predictions came true without error, unlike the falsehoods of soothsayers and astrologers.

Checkpoint
Which prediction led to al-'Abbas embracing Islam?
A) The lost camel
B) Ukaydir hunting
C) The secret deposit
D) The hypocrites' secrets

Key Takeaway
The Prophet's knowledge of hidden matters, both personal and public, confirms his prophethood, unlike the guesses of soothsayers.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you are uncertain about something in your life, do you turn to Allah and His revelation, or do you rely on your own guessing and worldly opinions? What is one specific situation today where you need to trust the Prophet's guidance over your own limited knowledge?
?
The Prophet's knowledge exposed the secret hypocrisy of the hypocrites. Is there any area of your life where you are hiding your true intentions from others or from yourself? How will you let the truth of this lesson bring you to full sincerity before Allah today?
?
Al-Abbas was confronted with a secret he thought only Allah knew, and he submitted to the truth. What secret are you hiding that you know only Allah knows? Are you willing to come clean and embrace the truth, even if it costs you something?

Examples of the Prophet's Predictions of the Unseen
Al-Nasafi lists examples of the Prophet's predictions of the unseen during his lifetime.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Prophet's accurate predictions of future events serve as evidence of his prophethood, through several historical examples.

Core Idea
The Prophet's predictions always came true, proving divine knowledge.

Al-Nasafi presents a series of incidents from the Prophet's life where he accurately foretold future events. These examples demonstrate that his knowledge was not ordinary but came from Allah, distinguishing him from false prophets and soothsayers. Let's examine each case closely.

Guided Path
1
Read the examples of the Prophet's predictions
Read through each example: the night journey news, the lost camel, Ukaydir hunting cows, the secret wealth of al-Abbas, and the exposure of hypocrites' thoughts.
Notice how each prediction was verified exactly as told.
2
Identify the common pattern
In each case, the Prophet revealed specific information about the unseen that no one could know normally, and the events unfolded exactly as he said.
This consistency is key to proving divine origin.
3
Reflect on the purpose
Consider why al-Nasafi includes multiple examples. They build a cumulative argument that the Prophet's knowledge of the unseen was ongoing and reliable.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن ذلك حديث ليلة الإسراء وما أخبر من أخبار عير قريش، وكان كما . ومن ذلك أنه ضلت له عليه السلام ناقة فأقبل يسأل الناس عنها فقال المنافقون : هذا محمد يخبركم خبر السماء وهو لا يدري أين ناقته، فصعد المنبر وحمد الله وأثنى عليه، وحكى قولهم ثم قال: إني لا أعلم إلا ما أعلمني ربي وقد أخبرني أنها في وادي كذا متعلق زمامها بشجرة فبادر الناس فوجدوها كذلك. ومن ذلك قوله لخالد بن الوليد حين بعثه إلى أكيدر بدومة الجندل: "أما أنكم ستأتونه فتجدونه يصيد البقر" فوجدوه كذلك. ومن ذلك قوله عليه السلام للعباس حين أسره: "افد نفسك وابني أخيك" يعني عقيل بن أبي طالب ونوفل بن الحارثة- فإنك ذو مال فقال : لا مال عندي. قال: فأين المال الذي وضعته بمكة عند أم الفضل وليس معكما أحد، فقلت: إن أصبت في سفري فللفضل كذا، ولعبد الله كذا، ولفلان كذا ؟ فقال العباس والذي بعثك بالحق نبيا ما علم بهذا أحد غيري، وإنك لرسول الله وأسلم هو وعقيل. ومن ذلك ما كان يخبر أهل النفاق بما كانوا يقولون فيما بينهم ويبيتون ما لا يرضى من القول حتى كانوا من شدة تعنتهم يحذرون أن ينزل عليه سورة تنبئهم بما في قلوبهم ، وأمثال ذلك كثير، وكتابنا هذا يضيق عن ذكر عشر ذلك فضلاً عن كله ، والله الموفق . ثم إن جميع ما أخبر من الأخبار الكائنة في المستقبل خرج على ما أخبر من غير تمكن كذب أو حلف في شيء من ذلك لا كمثل أخبار الكهنة والمنجمين الذين يضل صدقهم في كذبهم وحقهم في باطلهم على أن حالته كانت تخالف حالة الكهنة في طهارته وطيبه واشتغاله بالطاعات والعبادات. وتقدر أولئك وتنجسهم وتقربهم إلى الشياطين والأرواح الخبيثة ، وكذا كانت أخباره صادرة عنه عن طريق الغيب الذي أعلمه الله تعالى من غير الاشتغال بالنظر في النجوم والتأمل في الطالع والارتفاع وتعرف ذلك من قبل الريح والإسطرلاب وغير ذلك من خلاف ما يفعله المنجمة، فكان ذلك من باب نقض العادة كإلانة الحديد واتخاذ الدروع بلا آلات ولا استعمال النار.
Among that is the hadith of the Night Journey and what he informed of the news of the Quraysh caravan, and it was as [he said]. And among that is that a she-camel of his, peace be upon him, was lost, so he began asking people about it, and the hypocrites said: 'This Muhammad tells you the news of heaven while he does not know where his she-camel is.' So he ascended the pulpit, praised God and thanked Him, and narrated their words, then said: 'I know only what my Lord has taught me, and He has informed me that she is in such-and-such a valley, her halter entangled in a tree.' So the people rushed and found her thus. And among that is his saying to Khalid ibn al-Walid when he sent him to Ukaydir of Dumah al-Jandal: 'You will come to him and find him hunting cows' and they found him thus. And among that is his saying, peace be upon him, to al-Abbas when he captured him: 'Ransom yourself and your two nephews' meaning Aqil ibn Abi Talib and Nawfal ibn al-Harith — 'for you are wealthy.' He said: 'I have no wealth.' He said: 'Then where is the wealth that you left in Mecca with Umm al-Fadl while no one else was with you, and you said: If I am killed on my journey, then so-and-so for al-Fadl, so-and-so for Abdullah, and so-and-so for so-and-so?' Al-Abbas said: 'By Him Who sent you with the truth as a prophet, no one knew this besides me. You are indeed the Messenger of God.' And he and Aqil embraced Islam. And among that is that he used to inform the people of hypocrisy about what they said among themselves and plotted of speech that does not please [God], until they, due to their obstinacy, feared that a surah would be revealed telling them what was in their hearts. And similar examples are many, and this book of ours is too narrow to mention a tenth of that, let alone all of it. And God is the Granter of success. Then indeed all the reports he gave of future events came out as he reported without any possibility of falsehood or error in any of that, unlike the reports of soothsayers and astrologers whose truth is mixed with falsehood and whose correctness is mixed with error, while his state was contrary to the state of soothsayers in his purity, goodness, and engagement in acts of obedience and worship, and their impurity, defilement, and closeness to devils and evil spirits. Likewise, his reports came from him through the unseen which God Almighty taught him, without engaging in observation of stars, contemplation of horoscopes and ascendants, and knowing that by means of wind and astrolabe and other things contrary to what astrologers do. Thus it was a breach of [natural] custom, like softening iron and making coats of mail without tools or use of fire.
Source pages p. 739

Commentary
This passage is a multi-part proof of prophethood through predictions of the unseen. The author, al-Nasafi, provides several concrete examples from the Prophet's life where he accurately foretold events, including the location of a lost camel, the hunting habits of a king, a secret wealth transfer, and the secret thoughts of hypocrites. He concludes that all such predictions came true without exception. He then contrasts this with the unreliable reports of soothsayers (kuhhan) and astrologers (munajjimun), who sometimes speak truth but are often wrong. The Prophet's state of purity and devotion also differs from theirs, as they seek closeness to devils. Moreover, the Prophet received knowledge directly from God through revelation, not through astrological methods. Therefore, these predictions are miraculous breaches of natural custom (kharq al-ada), like the softening of iron for David.

Key Terms
نبوة
غيب
معجزة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Prophet's knowledge of the unseen was occasional and not always accurate.
Correction: Al-Nasafi shows through multiple examples that his predictions always came true exactly as stated, with no errors.

Checkpoint
What was the reaction of al-Abbas when the Prophet revealed his hidden wealth?
A) He denied it and continued to reject Islam.
B) He was amazed and immediately accepted Islam.
C) He asked for proof and then accepted.
D) He remained silent.

Key Takeaway
The Prophet's accurate and repeated predictions of the unseen prove that his knowledge came from Allah, not from human means.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The story of al-Abbas shows that the Prophet knew his secret wealth. When you hide things from your family or community, do you truly believe that Allah will expose them just as He exposed al-Abbas? How should this change your attitude towards honesty?
?
The hypocrites feared that a surah would be revealed exposing what was in their hearts. Are there thoughts or intentions in your heart that you would be ashamed if Allah revealed? What are you doing to purify them?
?
When the Prophet did not know where his she-camel was, the hypocrites mocked him. Have you ever doubted the Prophet's knowledge when something didn't happen as you expected? How does this lesson affirm that his knowledge is from Allah alone?

How Prophetic Knowledge Differs from Soothsayers and Astrologers
Al-Nasafi contrasts the Prophet's revelations with soothsayers and astrologers.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Prophet's knowledge of the unseen differs fundamentally from that of soothsayers and astrologers, and why his predictions are considered miracles.

Core Idea
Prophetic knowledge is pure and perfect, unlike the mixed and impure reports of soothsayers.

After presenting examples of the Prophet's accurate predictions, al-Nasafi contrasts them with the predictions of soothsayers (kuhhan) and astrologers (munajjimun). He highlights the absolute reliability of the Prophet's reports compared to the mixed truth and falsehood of others, and the purity of his character versus their impurity. This distinction elevates the Prophet's predictions to the level of miracles.

Guided Path
1
Read the contrast passage
Read the portion starting from 'Then indeed all the reports...' and note the key points of contrast: truthfulness, purity, and method of knowledge.
2
Understand the difference in reliability
Al-Nasafi states that all of the Prophet's future reports came true without any falsehood, unlike soothsayers whose truth is mixed with falsehood.
3
Understand the difference in character and method
The Prophet was pure and engaged in worship, while soothsayers were impure and sought devils. The Prophet received knowledge directly from Allah, not through stars or divination.
4
Connect to the concept of miracle (kharq al-ada)
This is described as a breach of natural custom, similar to the softening of iron for Prophet David. The perfect knowledge of the unseen is a supernatural event.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Checkpoint
According to al-Nasafi, what is the source of the Prophet's knowledge of the unseen?
A) Observation of stars and planets.
B) Divine revelation from Allah.
C) Deduction from natural signs.

Key Takeaway
The Prophet's predictions are a miracle because they are perfectly true, come from divine revelation, and are accompanied by a pure character, unlike the flawed reports of soothsayers and astrologers.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever sought knowledge of the future from a horoscope, fortune-teller, or 'lucky charm'? What does this lesson reveal about the source and reliability of such knowledge, and how will you respond next time you are tempted?
?
The Prophet's purity and devotion were essential to his prophethood. Examine your own daily habits: are they drawing you closer to Allah and purity, or are you casually engaging in practices (even small ones) that resemble the soothsayers' reliance on created things? What specific change will you make today?
?
You have just learned that true knowledge of the unseen comes only from Allah, and that the Prophet's predictions were perfect miracles. Does your heart truly trust in Allah's decree and the Prophet's message, or do you still secretly rely on other sources for reassurance? What is one step you can take to strengthen your reliance on Allah alone?
